-chapter 329-

Outside the window, warm sunlight poured in, an unusual sight for winter.  

Yet, the face of the beauty gazing out from within the palace was as cold as the weather was warm.  

– Thanks to the Second Prince’s blunder, we have a good opportunity.  

– The Makryn confusion operation will be put on hold.  

– Before returning, implant more people in the Makryn royal palace.  

– If war breaks out between the Empire and Makryn, it will only cause further chaos. And…  

– I will accelerate the post-deity era.  

“My life being targeted is just a blunder…?”  

Luisa’s expression hardened again as she recalled her communication with her mentor.  

She knew the tower’s purpose and resonated fully with it.  

But how could she accept the idea that it would be her own sacrifice to achieve that purpose?  

Even so, she had no choice but to endure it for now.  

What could she possibly say in a situation where her partial mission failure had turned into nothing?  

“Baros. One day, I will make you pay.”  

She could only grit her teeth and make that vow.  

Moreover, the orders that accompanied those words were equally absurd.  

The instruction to plant people from the Kassel Magic Tower meant creating brainwashed individuals.  

‘Someone whose mind can deteriorate suddenly without attracting attention, yet occupies an important position.’  

“Is there even such a person?”  

The conditions seemed so unreasonable that a self-derisive comment escaped her lips. After all, wasn’t there a king in a country capable of breaking the tower’s magic just by coming near?  

“It would be easier to seduce a genuine prince.”  

Thinking of the rumors circulating in society, she let out a small laugh.  

The tales about Count Ronian and herself had become intertwined, adorned with all sorts of embarrassing stories.  

Though she had never seriously considered marriage, as a woman, it was hard not to be somewhat concerned.  

Furthermore, when she pondered on these daunting orders, it naturally led her to daydreams of escape, allowing those awkward stories to resurface more frequently.  

“…Should I actually try seducing him?”  

She would persuade the prince to betray the king.  

Wasn’t that a usual plot in the novels circulating in the markets?  

Just as Luisa was lost in pleasant yet futile fantasies, a voice she didn’t wish to hear came from outside the door.  

– Count Ronian has come to visit.  

“Ugh, the timing really…”  

It was a theatrical performance meant to cover up the imperial interference in the ambush incident and portray a friendly relationship.  

She found this stage bothersome, yet the other lead was particularly reluctant.  

Creak.  

“Are you free?”  

As soon as the attendant served tea and stepped out, Luisa shot a cold remark with an expressionless face.  

There was no longer any need for pretenses between them.  

However, the large young man with red hair and red eyes simply smiled and responded.  

“Well, this is my work right now.”  

“You surely don’t seem to enjoy it.”  

“Well, at least it’s nice to have an attractive company.”  

At around twenty years of age, he was full of youthful vigor.  

Surprisingly, even with a planned beauty practically undressing before him, the young man’s eyes held no glimmer of lust.  

‘Such restraint with his powers at that age; he must have considerable self-control.’  

That thought only made Luisa recall her own past that was shrouded in secrecy, causing a wry smile to escape her lips.  

Well, ultimately, since that was exposed, Baron Ronian’s disinterest might seem more pronounced.  

“How brazen. It seems you brothers are quite similar.”  

“Haha, that’s a first for me to hear. You think I resemble my elder brother?”  

Indeed, while the intense features of red-haired Ronian were prominent, the shapes of their faces were entirely different.  

Logan, who took after their mother, had gentle features, while Ronian sharply resembled their father, often leading those around them to expect discord between the brothers.  

Except for the fact that he once enjoyed hearing that he looked like his brother.  

Ronian, smiling naturally, put down his teacup and said cheekily.  

“Well, who’s more brazen? The princess or the terrorist who claims to be a victim? What could be more brazen than that?”  

“Victim? Who ever was truly victimized? It seems I solely spat blood.”  

“Our knight suffered serious injuries too. Or do normal knights no longer count as humans to you?”  

“As long as he’s alive, that’s all that matters.”  

The laughter exchanged bore thorns hidden within their smiles.  

Since that incident, her conversations had continued to be tiresome, yet the attendants outside would assume that everything was congenial.  

“I heard that you received gifts from the Dong-wang palace. At this rate, we really might set a wedding date soon.”  

“Don’t worry; that won’t happen.”  

“If you continue to stay here, it might become a reality you should fear.”  

“I’ll be leaving soon anyway. So just forget about it.”  

Sipping cautiously, as her nerves heightened, she couldn’t even taste the tea that flowed down her throat.  

After about an hour, she would have to endure more tiresome resistance, but there was no way around it.  

As Luisa gathered her thoughts, a rather enticing piece of information slipped out from Ronian unexpectedly.  

“Oh, it seems my brother is planning something big again recently.”  

“Something big? Hm.”  

Feigning indifference, her attention was entirely now singularly focused on him.  

Whether he knew how intrigued she became, Ronian wore a slightly amused smile, gazing steadily at her.  

“However, there was a message that the Empire may be interested, so I hope it’s solved amicably with the Dong-wang palace.”  

“Uh? Why are you telling me this?”  

“We’re not on bad terms, are we? Outwardly, at least.”  

“That’s merely surface-level.”  

“It’s for the purpose of combating the Empire. I think ‘they’ might like it.”  

Oddly emphasized words irked her ears, but curiosity quickly overtook them.  

“Go on. What is it about?”  

“There are plans to build fortresses at several key locations along the border.”  

“Pfft.”  

Her tea spluttered out, as her jaw almost dropped from surprise.  

She blamed Ronian’s evasive smile for suddenly dodging it.  

“What did you just say?”  

“Considering your response, it seems your ears are functioning well.”  

“Are you seriously going to build fortresses on the border? Are you blatantly declaring war against the Empire? And then asking us to soothe things over?”  

“Officially, we won’t announce it as just the ‘West’ but rather the entire frontier. Of course, we plan on constructing it solely in the West.”  

“Do you think the Empire is blind!?”  

“What do you want? They won’t interfere with internal affairs anyway. They might issue a warning, at worst. Or they might even march in sooner.”  

– The mere act of the Empire preparing for war will send ripples through the world. With decades spent in peace policies, they won’t be able to hide changes forever.  

– If the war is inevitable, why not choose the timing ourselves?  

Recalling her brother’s words, Ronian was smiling, “Heh… In the end, you’re all doomed.”  

Luisa sighed, neither knowing if it was a laugh or a scoff.  

Soon after, their gazes remained sharp, a fierce determination sparkling.  

‘Makryn knows of war against the Empire as an established fact.’  

‘They do not deny it. They are aware of the Empire’s preparations for war.’  

Just with one query, both sides found confirmation; one side understood the kingdom’s situation, while the other confirmed their guess was true.  

After a moment of silence, Luisa broke the ice first.  

“Officially, we won’t announce it, but a subtle pressure will emerge. What are the consequences?”  

“Perhaps the princess’s safe return?”  

“Hmph. Even if you threaten me with my life, you won’t sway my decisions.”  

“It’s not a threat; it’s merely a suggestion. ‘They’ will likely want it.”  

Upon Luisa’s brief silence, Ronian reclined against the couch, eyeing her carefully.  

But despite the carefree disposition of his posture, there was a noticeable tension.  

“Then my father may respond without making any official proclamations, but subtle pressures are inevitable.”  

The very thought brought further unease to her mind.  

“You may find yourself faced with some unusual requests.”  

“Seems plausible. But we might just take proper preventive measures.”  

“Yes, we understand. As long as information is reported, from now on, any small changes should be conveyed without delay.”  

“Yes, understood.”  

Staring deeply into Luisa’s sapphire eyes, Ronian suddenly leaned forward.  

“Actually, I’ve no intention of entirely cutting ties. Additional contacts can indeed be established.”  

With that said, Luisa couldn’t help but express her surprise.  

“But if you say there’s value in maintaining contact, I’d rather report to the Empire than to my brother.”  

“What will you do?”  

Biting her lip slightly, the depth of Ronian’s indigo gaze seemed to require careful consideration.  

“How can I approach giving up my connections with intention?”  

With sudden strength, Luisa declared, refusing to feel subject to sudden commercial laws.  

Forcing a smile to Ronian’s unfurling laughter, she managed to regain her composure.  

“Hmph. What’s worse than being tied down?”  

“Good luck with that. I’ll convey your words along with our own requests, regardless of anything.”  

“Alright. It’s not as if I can change matters overnight, but no need to panic just yet.”  

“Let’s get things settled straightforwardly.”  

When they finally stood up and embraced, she left the space with her own determined stance.  

Staring after her retreating figure, Ronian chuckled.  

Once the door swung shut behind her, he sighed deeply.  

“Haah… The princess is indifferent.”  

Staring blankly out the window, Ronian pondered aloud, though no one offered a reply.  

With that, the chapter closed, leaving unanswered questions lingering like shadows from the past.



-chapter 332-

I express my regret regarding the recent policies implemented in the McLain Kingdom.  

I am concerned that this may adversely affect the friendly relations between our two nations…  

The underlying meaning of the long message sent by the imperial royal family was straightforward.  

– Are you challenging us? Do you really want war? If not, stop your fortification efforts immediately.  

The McLain royal family swiftly responded.  

– No, that’s not the case. We’re just maintaining internal order. This will actually help your side. So, mind your own business.  

With both sides tentatively aware of the ongoing hostility, it felt like a game of blind man’s bluff.  

Naturally, the Empire sent an even stronger declaration.  

The intent was glaringly obvious.  

Moreover, the notice from the Empire was not only delivered to the McLain royal family but was also proclaimed in the eastern part of the Empire.  

The Empire was openly showing its teeth.  

In response, petitions from the nobles flooded the McLain royal castle.  

– Please cease the fortification work. To avoid conflict with the Empire…  

– The current Empire is at its peak…  

– A small nation must heed the wishes of a great power…  

“Small nation? Great power? Who wrote this? Are you out of your mind? Is this from the Empire?”  

Logan chuckled wryly while holding one of the petitions, but the expressions of those before him were tense and serious.  

Among them were Damian, the head of information; Dwain, the finance minister; and Count Roberts, the chancellor.  

Also present were the sword master who had rushed over upon hearing the news and Luther and Commander Wicken, who had been training with him.  

And now, Victor and Burdel, who had started to stick close to Logan like personal bodyguards and secret weapons, were also present.  

It was a gathering of the kingdom’s influential figures, excluding the cavalry leaders stationed in the McLain territory and the fortification efforts.  

The sword master spoke on behalf of the group.  

“The 3rd and 4th Legions of the Empire are scheduled to conduct training soon at the northern border. If things escalate, it could very well lead to war.”  

However, despite his worrying words, Logan’s demeanor remained resolute.  

“Our 2nd Legion will conduct training in the north as well. It could be quite entertaining to train facing the Empire’s forces.”  

“Your Majesty!”  

“Ah, I was just joking. Just a joke.”  

“Is this really a subject for jokes right now!?”  

The sword master raised his voice, which was a rare occurrence.  

“Yes, it’s still okay. Right, Damian?”  

Logan maintained a smile, casually shifting his gaze.  

“Yes, Your Majesty. According to what Senior Philip mentioned, there hasn’t been any significant fluctuation in the flow of war materials such as food, weapons, or iron ore.”  

“What do you mean by that…?”  

“Unlike the notice, it suggests that the Empire has no immediate plans to go to war.”  

“Hah… Can we judge simply based on that?”  

“It is indeed sufficient grounds. For a nation as large as the Empire, our Kingdom is not at a level that can be easily quelled by just one or two of their legions.”  

As Logan supported Damian’s statement, Damian flashed a grin at the sword master.  

“Philip said it like this: Words and letters can sometimes lie, but the flow of money never deceives.”  

*Clears throat.*  

Despite often hearing that it was blocked up, the sword master’s recognition was not merely for show; he acknowledged the validity of Damian’s words.  

However, recognizing this raised another question.  

“Your Majesty, you have claimed that the Empire will invade McLain sooner or later. Wasn’t the fortification one of the preparations for that?”  

“That’s correct.”  

“Then, it seems strange that the Empire would react so minimally while knowing that. Could it be that the Empire is not considering war…?”  

At those words, both Damian and Dwain’s gazes shifted towards the sword master.  

Logan’s assertion regarding the Empire’s invasion had become an accepted fact among the current McLain leadership, and all policies were being tailored accordingly.  

Even if there were those who had doubts about that judgment, who would dare to defy Logan’s orders?  

The only person who could question that premise was the sword master himself, so the curious gazes of the officials moved back to Logan.  

“Isn’t there no reason for the Empire to react more aggressively? We are not preparing to invade the Empire ourselves.”  

“Excuse me?”  

“The fortification blocking the gorge is fundamentally a defensive measure. If we were to attack, it would simply serve as a nuisance.”  

“That’s true, but…”  

While somewhat agreeing, the sword master still tilted his head.  

In response, Logan continued with a wry smile.  

“It seems they are still not fully ready internally. It could be about the crown prince’s investiture and such…”  

“But Your Majesty, the current response is…”  

“Above all, the Emperor likely does not consider our kingdom to be a significant threat.”  

“Excuse me?”  

“Whether they construct fortifications or organize legions, they likely believe they can easily trample us at any moment. It’s more of a minor annoyance, perhaps.”  

Logan’s voice carried a hint of certainty as he recalled the behavior of the Empire he had witnessed in his past life, alongside the face of the current Emperor.  

‘Whatever preparations we make, they might just think of it as us being a bit more bothersome.’  

Indeed, considering the power differences as viewed from a third-party perspective, the Emperor could think that way.  

However, Logan believed the actual military strength of McLain to be quite different.  

It was probably due to the peculiarities of the current continent’s war history where the Empire had been ignoring the power of their vigilante group.  

They were trying their utmost to prevent rumors from spreading about various artifacts and the Liberatio.  

And there were also the absolutely confidential superhumans and the Grand Magic Circles.  

Moreover, with new fortifications being constructed, there was enough confidence to believe they could withstand the Empire.  

‘Of course, the Empire also keeps the strength of its Central Legions a secret, so that’s the same for them.’  

Thinking that way, he felt a never-ending cycle of thoughts.  

Undervaluing the enemy could be fatal, but overestimating them could lead to great mistakes as well.  

Thus,  

“We must continue our preparations. If it turns out there’s no war after all, then… Well, that wouldn’t be a bad outcome.”  

“…That’s true. I’m convinced. Right, don’t you agree?”  

As the sword master responded in that way and turned his head to look, the silent giant standing by couldn’t help but release a smile as he spoke in a thunderous voice.  

“I have never doubted Your Majesty’s words.”  

“I feel the same way. You needn’t worry.”  

Seeing Luther Kyle and Wicken Kalia nodding with smiles, Logan realized the intentions of his teacher.  

In a time of rising tensions, it was a question meant to erase any small doubts that might have crept between them.  

Logan appreciated his teacher’s consideration and responded with a smile.  

“Of course. Even if war does not break out immediately, there will certainly be some countermeasures in place. Companies and trade-related entities operating within the Empire will likely face significant setbacks.”  

“…That’s a problem in its own right.”  

The sword master’s expression grew grave once more.  

“However, I have already devised a solution.”  

“Already?”  

“I received unexpected assistance.”  

At that, everyone’s gaze shifted to where Logan was looking.  

“Damian, how is the preparation?”  

In response, Dwain, with a scruffy beard, smiled and continued.  

“The support from the Eastern Department has been quite proactive. It seems there may indeed be some internal strife brewing within the Empire.”  

At that, the eyes of the sword masters, completely unaware of the inside story, widened in surprise.



-chapter 342-

How can one not be furious?  

Yet, his anger could not burst forth.  

Even after mastering divine power, the path to ascension remained obscured. Furthermore, the thirst for mana that he felt after reaching the realm of a divine being through magic grew ever more intense. If he attempted to root out those spreading rude rumors, his time left on the continent would dwindle away exponentially.  

Thus, I eventually had to make a choice.  

To abandon humanity and forge a path to ascension beyond the magic realm.  

Or remain in this world, embracing the fall from grace and reaccepting the limits of my lifespan.  

He rejected both options. Either one felt like fleeing from the ‘betrayers.’  

If there is no road to take, then one must simply forge their own.  

From that moment, he instead encouraged the faith in the nine gods among humanity.  

The basis for his change in attitude lay in the essence of divine power.  

Divine power is the seed of the nine gods, sown throughout the world. The flower that blooms, nourished by human potential, eventually returns to the divine as a much greater harvest.  

He intended to become the representative of faith himself and swallow the ‘fruits’ destined to return to the gods.  

If it was impossible with just his own abilities, he would seize the power of the betrayers and ascend.  

With that plan, he created the sect of the nine gods.  

Over the course of a hundred years, his plan seemed to be thriving. Sitting in the position of the ‘Unified Pope,’ he had become the ruler of humanity, known as both the zenith of faith in the nine gods and another god as well.  

He believed that the rewards and dividends he rightfully deserved were finally in his hands. Yet, intoxicated by the sweetness of power tasted too late, he realized far too late how foolishly he viewed the betrayers and the gods.  

By accepting divine power, he extended his lifespan, but in doing so, he drifted farther from mana. Instead, he manipulated the ‘spirit’ of humanity to collect divine power and became more entangled in surpassing the limits of ‘dimensions.’  

While striving for his ascension, he was unaware that the ground beneath his feet was flipping over.  

It was a critical mistake.  

As he was gathering the offerings required for the ascension ceremony, the nine high priests assisting with the ceremony betrayed him all at once. They had been his loyal subordinates in ordinary times, so he could not fathom that they would betray him so suddenly.  

But the moment he saw the faces of those betraying subordinates, he understood the reason for his error.  

They were no longer his subordinates. They had taken possession of the bodies of his ‘apostles.’ Those monsters, revoltingly, contained parts of the personas of the betrayers. They had stabbed him in the back.  

Of course, even if he had clung solely to ascension, he was a supreme being. Any fragments of the gods, who had originally sent down only a portion of their power and personas from another dimension, should not have been his equals.  

However, it was different during that time, leading up to ascension when 90% of his power was bound to the ceremony. Despite that, he was still able to deal with all those ‘apostles.’  

The cost, however, was excessively high.  

The fragments of divine power he had worked hard to gather scattered away. Most of the power that should have been his vanished into thin air. Such an irretrievable opportunity was squandered so meaninglessly.  

The gods who had forcibly created the ‘apostles’ must have also suffered considerable backlash. That alone was my small consolation.  

Thus, his desire intensified even further.  

There were hints in the words of the apostles, who spat out nonsense, calling it divine blasphemy. My methods were not wrong. If they had not interfered, I could have become a ‘much stronger’ god than those betrayers who had ascended before me.  

However, during the process of dealing with the apostles, he had overextended himself, and the ceremony had become distorted. A complex set of reasons inflicted an irreparable wound upon him.  

And there was a greater problem.  

With the entire leadership of the sect dead, the sect he had painstakingly built would scatter, but they would reunite at some point in the future. Moreover, the gods would thoroughly erase all traces of my existence.  

Furthermore, my name would be erased from the history of humanity itself, in accordance with their will.  

That signified the death of the soul.  

It was true character assassination, denying all the accomplishments achieved by the mage-saint, Zibrik Cassel.  

In fact, there was no record of Zibrik Cassel, the first demigod among humans, in any documents today.  

It was strange, even if he was a demigod from a millennium earlier than the Great Emigration event. No, it was certainly abnormal that the one who would later lead diverse races toward the Great Emigration, effectively rewriting human history, disappeared from the chronicles altogether.  

I did not want to vanish like that. I wished to leave a possibility behind. Even if not me, I wanted another to become the pinnacle of humanity, the god of humanity, aspiring to crush those betrayers.  

So I gathered the remaining divine power and my last bit of strength to leave behind a legacy, for those with suitable qualifications. Hear my voice, for you shall seize the latent power hidden within my legacy.  

In a flash.  

Once again, a dazzling white light spread forth.  

Yet Logan, only after a while, realized he was standing alone in that white space. The staggering information acquired from rapidly experiencing the life of a supreme being swirled within his mind, leaving him unable to regain his composure.  

‘This is absurd…’  

Only after sorting the chaotic thoughts in his head did Logan come to understand that he belonged to an incomprehensible space and that someone existed before him.  

– Are you coming to your senses?  

A man with red hair and red eyes.  

An unusual appearance seen only by direct descendants of the MacLein line.  

A middle-aged man, who seemed somewhat similar to Logan in a few decades. He addressed Logan.  

And now, Logan could clearly identify who that man was.  

“…Zibrik Cassel?”  

– Yes, my descendant.  

“…Descendant?”  

– Do you not recognize me, even seeing my form? You would know if you glimpsed my thoughts. I assure you I’m not speaking falsehoods.  

“…It does seem like it.”  

The visage he had seen in the memories was indeed similar.  

Amid the flood of monumental events, he had glossed over the appearances of the parties involved.  

– The red eyes and red hair, such peculiarities I ensured were directly inherited. That appearance, between fathers and sons, will remain eternal, will it not?  

Logan could not help but stiffen at those words.  

This clear physical trait inherited without exception among the direct male descendants of MacLein was indeed uncanny. The family’s members often joked that it might be a remnant of ancient magic.  

Of course, that lineage did not boast any particular abilities associated with such legendary bloodlines.  

“…I am MacLein.”  

– The surname holds no importance. This magic arises from my firstborn son. However, if that is not the case, it shall pass to the closest blood relative. That very appearance stands as proof of your worthiness to inherit my legacy.  

“Just blood?”  

– Both bloodline and ability must be fulfilled. In your previous life, your abilities were inadequate thus I could not pass my voice to you.  

“!?”  

That was something Logan could not help but react to.  

But then.  

– Why the surprise? I, or rather, a remnant of my half-soul residing in this legacy, had accompanied you throughout your past life. Your presence in this place results from the means I devised to prevent what I’ve painstakingly prepared from falling into the wrong hands.  

“Ah…!”  

A gasp escaped involuntarily.  

As he observed Zibrik Cassel, the soul of his ancestor, smiled.  

– Is that not enough to earn your trust?  

“Excuse me?”  

– Through the use of divine manipulation, I have brought you to this moment by expending some of the divinity I possess hidden within this legacy. Had my wishes been fulfilled, you would have undoubtedly become a divine being surpassing those betrayers.  

With difficulty, Logan nodded to the voice that contained especially intense fury.  

Yet.  

– In my previous life, the pitiful one, you are to reclaim my legacy anew. Glorious, indeed. While you may change everything possible, I expected your brother to come to me.  

The following words caused his expression to harden unconsciously.  

He had often lamented that if the divine sword had gone to Roniant instead of himself while fleeing during his previous life, the fate of the country and the family might have changed. If the words spoken by the soul before him are indeed true, knowing such facts was unquestionable.  

However, amid their conversation, one of the most significant questions remained unaddressed.  

‘Doesn’t he realize that my talent itself changed after returning? What about the divine sword vision? What is going on?’  

As Logan was about to pose the question, Zibrik’s remarks came out without giving him the chance.  

– Does it matter? All is well. Although the remaining divinity is now merely a portion, by obtaining this, you shall seek the supreme bracelet and gain the possibility to ascend to divinity while inheriting my strength.  

The supreme bracelet.  

He had a good guess regarding what it might pertain to, so that statement barely occupied his focus. However, the following words surprised him significantly.  

“You mean… divinity?”  

– Correct, the potential to become a superior god, surpassing even the false gods.  

As Zibrik Cassel’s spirit finished speaking, his form faded, and in his hand appeared a small luminous orb that shimmered with light.  

– Were it not for the strength used in your regression, this alone could have bestowed upon you the strength of a demigod. Regrettably, it cannot be helped. Even so, this is sufficient for you to attain power equivalent to that of a great archmage. Accept it.  

Those words were an irresistible temptation.  

It was difficult not to believe him, especially since he carried the burden that the archmage standards had likely shifted considerably during this era.  

Nevertheless, Logan did not brush aside the vague unease that persisted in the back of his mind.  

“Isn’t it all thanks to you, ancestor? It became possible because my innate talent changed after my regression. I wish to express my gratitude. Moreover, the swordsmanship passed down in my family was exceptional too.”  

– …That was simply what I ought to do as an ancestor. Do not mind it.  

Seemingly unaware of the divine sword vision, he spoke very little.  

‘Why do you seem ignorant? I memorized it countless times even immediately after obtaining the sword.’  

It was strange. The expression on Zibrik’s vague countenance, while not clearly visible, seemed laced with a touch of embarrassment.  

Unintentionally, a sense of vigilance arose in Logan’s heart.  

“Do I have some task ahead of me to earn this inheritance?”  

– There is none in this realm. Merely ascend as a god, crush the betrayers, and prove my greatness, Zibrik Cassel. That is sufficient.  

The unmistakable fury in that voice seemed genuine.  

Yet, filled with doubt, Logan did not easily fall for the temptation.  

“What about the diminished divinity due to my regression? How can it be restored?”  

In turn, he attempted to redirect the conversation, but the ancestor’s spirit offered no further details.  

– You will come to understand upon seizing this. My legacy possesses that much power.  

Despite the haze, he caught a glimpse of an unmistakable smile.  

The traces of a great hero persisting throughout his life remained vivid.  

And for that very reason, it was even more absurd.  

Unintentionally, Zibrik Cassel had revealed too much to Logan. Though not observing the entirety of his life, the major currents of Zibrik’s existence lingered as vividly as if he had watched it from nearby.  

In that memory, he was not the person Logan envisioned.  

“To bestow everything just because I am a descendant? That’s not the kind of person you were, was it?”  

Zibrik had grown up believing himself to be the best from a young age. The ambition to surpass limits stemmed from the pride in being the best, and it was for that singular purpose that he abandoned his clan with family ties.  

Moreover, his later benevolence toward humanity derived from the notion that humanity was his ‘possession.’ He simply could not relinquish ownership of his belongings.  

Additionally, he had borne witness to the by-products gathered through the nine gods from the war with the dragons, yet it was well understood that simply having reached demigod status, he lacked the depth of understanding when it came to the realms of power compared to long-standing supreme beings. Therefore, he gained nothing.  

Yet, he called them betrayers without imparting that understanding to me?  

– …You could say that the pain runs deep regarding those betrayers.  

Above all, he was one who would do anything for a purpose.  

He had effectively crafted the continent to be as hostile as possible for other races to thrive, wishing to become a god, even if it meant spreading false faith.  

A greedy man.  

He was unyielding when it came to giving, with no absolute purpose behind such acts.  

Furthermore.  

‘The only son seen amid the memories displayed a pitiful figure, the eldest son, barely visible.’  

When most people periodized their greatest joys in life, they would mention the birth of children. Yet, throughout Zibrik Cassel’s entire life, that bloodline had barely shown up in the grand record.  

Would someone like that truly offer everything to their bloodline alongside sacrificial intentions?  

Something felt peculiar about the aura accumulating in the palm of that fading spirit.  

Determining whether it was divine or something else remains difficult. However, Logan believed he could confidently ascertain what part of it comprised.  

“If I judge correctly, ancestor, it doesn’t feel like you’ll be leaving vengeance to just anyone. Could it be the divinity you’re handing over is your very soul?”  

It was as if a sharp dagger had pierced through the haze of the fading spirit.  

In a distinct upheaval, the spirit trembled faintly, growing even more translucent in Logan’s gaze.  

– …Do you think merely receiving that power will be achievable by absorbing energy?  

“You mean I must bear your soul?”  

– It is a togetherness. In the end, the vessel of flesh will be yours.  

“The soul will belong to you.”  

Having achieved some unfathomable accomplishment in the current world, still far less than the realm of a demigod, yet it was undeniably minute compared to the power wielded by Zibrik Cassel.  

Would he manage to even endure an instance of the soul thriving with a portion of the divinity?  

‘That can’t be right.’  

The moment Logan’s expression froze, a sense of urgency erupted from the spirit’s voice.  

– Do not waste this unparalleled opportunity in hollow doubt, descendant!  

Logan couldn’t deny it.  

However, that fatal realization did not make for a smooth transition.  

Why not allow his competitor to take possession of the sacrifice instead?  

He needed to ensure the final confrontation to reclaim his soul.

Even if he passed over the most critical memory haphazardly, it intertwined with the horrifying aftermath created by Balros at the last moment of his past life—  

“Was the offering you utilized to ascend to divinity a human?”

-chapter 341-

The overwhelming presence emitted by the holy sword made subsequent actions cautious.  

Suppressing the impulse to draw the sword and uncover the secret immediately, Logan instead chose to focus on recovering his energy.  

He took a handful of rations he’d stowed away from the enemy’s supplies and began to meditate quietly to restore his force.

After some time had passed, Logan confirmed that more than half of his energy had been restored.

Flash!

I have waited long for this moment.  

As the voice rang out, memories not his own flickered through Logan’s mind, intensely vivid, as if lived first-hand.  

A prodigious infant who recognized things clearly from birth and fluently spoke the common tongue before reaching one hundred days.  

Had it been peaceful times, that child would have grown to be an exceptional scholar or sorcerer, but instead, he was born into an era beset by monstrous chaos, living a life of constant flight from danger.  

During an age where monsters attacked, other races asserted dominance, and humanity was often forced to become nomadic.  

In a fortuitous twist, the child was born into a large tribe with over a thousand members, yet that tribe too was destined to a life of constant wandering.  

Despite the continuous shifting of residences every six months during these perilous times, the child’s brilliance shone through unimpeded.  

When pursued by orcs and lizardmen, the child learned from their combat techniques, and when passing through the elven woods, absorbed their archery and elemental magic of wind and water. Brief transactions in the dwarven city led him to learn their crafting skills and study fire and earth elemental sorcery.  

– This child is the future of our tribe.  

When the whole tribe acknowledged the child thus—  

A voice from the heavens dispelled such fancies.  

– No, this child will become the future of humanity.  

A revered sage from the elusive Okan race had descended into the village where the tribe resided.  

The reasons unknown, but from that time forth, the sage began to teach the child about “magic.”  

That marked the turning point in his life.  

The child absorbed the sage’s teachings as if born for magic, ultimately becoming a superhuman capable of casting 7th circle spells at the age of just twenty. Not merely human circle magic, but the notoriously complex class magic of the Okan.  

‘7th circle for a superhuman? Wait, class magic is from the Okan?’  

This reality contradicted Logan’s known common sense, adding knowledge to what had previously been unknown.  

In a moment of confusion, he snapped out of the immersion in memories of the “child,” but the grand narrative continued unfolding, pulling Logan back into the scenes replaying vividly before his eyes.  

The child naturally became the chief of the tribe, and within less than a decade became the representative for all humanity across the eastern continent.  

At that time, he had achieved the 8th circle and was heralded as the Grand Magus.  

At just over thirty years old, he was the youngest in history to reach that status, not just among humans but across all races.  

Thus, he became known as the transcendent being, earning the world’s reverence.  

‘8th circle as Grand Magus? What are the standards here?’  

Amidst further astonishment, Logan sought to regain his focus when, echoing in response, he heard the voice once more.  

After reaching the pinnacle of magic, I believed myself to be the greatest being in the world. That was close to the truth, but it could never be a reality.  

Ten more years passed, and he was declared the strongest Grand Magus among humanity.  

Indeed, the strongest ‘human.’  

He could never be the world’s greatest; for there were others who had also achieved the 9th circle.  

Half-gods, those long-lived beings who stood above mere mortals, and the great scholars from the Okan lineage, as well as leaders from other races.  

Alas, his magical prowess could not touch the realm of those half-gods.  

– How tragic it is. Had you not been human, perhaps you could have reached the 9th circle, the stage of divinity.  

It was the limitation of his race.  

The sage from the Okan who taught him magic spoke those words with genuine sorrow.  

The apprentice who had caught up to his master within an impossibly short time, yet the sage deemed it impossible for him to surpass the limits of his race.  

Once a child, now a middle-aged Grand Magus—he fiercely opposed.  

He would prove he could do it.  

He could transcend any limits.  

For the first time, a prodigy lashed out in anger at his teacher’s doubts.  

If the path his master laid out was untraversable, then he would seek another path.  

With obstinacy, the prodigy secluded himself, shunning all glory.  

Decades later, a calamity, unparalleled in history, erupted upon the world.  

The Ancient Dragon, existing since time immemorial, lost its sanity during its challenge to ascend to godhood, entering a frenzied state without explanation.  

Fueled by insanity, the dragon brought devastation upon the world.  

The world’s supreme beings convened to discuss the obliteration of the dragon, but by then, a third of the continent had already been reduced to ashes.  

Without a supreme being to lead them, humanity could not participate in that council. Instead, they were selected as mere sacrificial offerings, intended to drain the dragon’s strength.  

That incident—specifically, the cries for help from descendants who had fallen victim to the dragon’s flames—summoned the hermit prodigy back into the world.  

Regrettably, the prodigy’s achievements had come to a standstill at the 8th circle. Humanity’s hopes, unable to challenge the demi-gods, could not sway the half-gods’ decisions.  

The prodigy’s return was akin to pouring a bucket of water onto a fire of kindling. Although humanity’s destruction was already decided, the ancient genius did not yield to despair.  

Through decades of seclusion and research, a wall that had never been breached was shattered in the battle against the dragon.  

The prodigy emerged from the fight with newfound understanding, surpassing his limits, ultimately entering the council of the supreme beings as the first demi-god of humanity, the Shin-in.  

Although all human Grand Magi had perished in the battle, and nine-tenths of the warriors from his race were wiped out, there was still a glimmer of hope.  

Standing for humanity’s rights and survival, he appealed, gaining the acceptance of the demi-gods of other races.  

At that moment, true global unity came into its own.  

Of course, it took a long time to defeat the dragon after the alliance formed.  

The mad dragon indiscriminately summoned entities from other dimensions with the powers of a fledgling god. By the time the alliance finally dispelled the dragon, the world had fundamentally changed.  

The greatest shift occurred when the southern sea was swallowed, replaced by an endless mountain range.  

Not merely a mountain range—it was a dimensional barrier connecting entirely to realms beyond. Neither I, nor even the demi-gods could erase this distortion entirely. Alone, I was powerless against it.  

Changes occurred to the ten demi-gods who led the dragon’s eradication. The battle against the dragon brought forth not just an opportunity for the prodigy.  

The remaining three ancient dragons and two great sages of the Okan had cultivated their powers over the long war against the dragon, discovering ways to surpass their own limits.  

And they had not shared this wisdom with me, a heavy anger began to seep into the voice.  

The remaining dragon kin, the last three ancient dragons, along with two great sages of the Okan, beings who had ruled over other races throughout the ages…  

It was precisely the day after the war ended that ‘nine’ gods came into being.  

‘What!?’  

Logan’s mind jolted awake, breaking free from the immersion in the life of the demi-god.  

‘So, the nine gods are…?’  

In response to that question, the demi-god lamented.  

They were truly irresponsible beings. They claimed divinity for themselves while forsaking the world to satisfy their own ambitions. Alone, I had no choice but to fortify myself.  

As the sole remaining demi-god, that prodigy could never confront the dimensional rift alone. Thus, he reinforced the barrier within the continent, pressing back the mana to erect an unseen wall in the south.  

As time passed, races accustomed to mana would find life difficult on the continent, yet for now, preventing erosion took precedence.   

Yet, this unavoidable decision brought forth immense unforeseen circumstances.  

The first consequence was the decline of other races.  

The dragon kin began to depart one by one toward the deeper chasms where mana was still abundant.  

They were beings born of mana, thus could not endure the diminishing concentration falling around them.  

Moreover, with all those who had reached demi-god status, save for the three ancient dragons who had ascended, the demi-gods from the dragon races had been completely annihilated, leaving the remaining remaining to oppose the progenitor of humanity.  

In a time when dragons were reduced to mere legends, the second consequence surfaced.  

In this declining era, astonishingly, a select few humans began to awaken and harness the power of life energy, a substitute for mana. It was weak compared to mana, but I hoped this ‘force’ would sustain the human race.  

“Force?”  

In shock, Logan involuntarily blurted out the words, but no answer came in reply.  

This was a positive variable amidst the context where a demi-god still existed while humanity, the weakest race on the continent, appeared to gain an advantage.  

Lastly, the third variable fell upon the demi-god himself.  

The reason for the dragons’ departure intertwined with Logan, too. Having divorced himself from human biology and existing solely on mana, his life in the continent grew increasingly tenuous as well.  

However, it would be absurd to nullify a spell already established in the process of survival.  

He could not forsake the humanity that had only just begun to stand on its own, neither could he retreat from the vastness of the rift.  

Amidst such despair, the prodigy encountered another dilemma—  

The faith of the nine gods! When had they reached out to humanity? It was inconceivable.  

A faith had emerged among humans worshipping the demi-gods who had ascended after the war against the dragon.  

In reality, the nine gods had begun to bestow strength upon those who believed in them—helping normal humans who could neither use mana nor force to find grace.  

The enraged prodigy initially sought to eliminate the priests. But slowly, he began to sense another possibility emanating from them.  

Divine power, that force was peculiar. It bore a resemblance to mana but felt even more refined. And the true essence of why beings who became gods could influence the world reverberated in him. This revelation ignited a spark in his imagination.  

Back then, he had fought against entities who had become gods, and instinctively he found ways to make that energy his own.  

Perhaps one day he too could become a god.  

Without transcending dimensions, he could remain as a currently active demi-god.  

Rekindled in forgotten desire, the genius delved deeply into divine powers.  

Soon, he wielded powers far mightier than those called priests.  

From that point forward, his title transformed.  

From a savior of humanity to the Magus Son.  

Even at that level, he thought nothing of it…  

– The Magus Son is the envoy of the nine gods.  

– Following the wishes of that transcendent being, we must believe in the nine gods.  

– He is the first servant…  

Absurd proclamations began to spread across the world, turning a legitimate demi-god into a mere servant of the very gods he sought to transcend.  

Could he not feel anger at being deemed a servant by those who had betrayed him and fled?

Even with her appreciative offer, Logan shook his head.  

“No. It’s something I must do alone.”  

Gripping his wife’s warm hands wrapped around his chest, Logan reassured himself once more.  

“Why not? Wouldn’t I be of help?”  

“That would be the case, but it’s also dangerous.”  

At those words, Aileen’s grip tightened.  

The idea that a superhuman aura user could face danger was alarming.  

“Then I must go even more so.”  

While her determined grip expressed her will, Logan shook his head once again.  

“…It’s not that it’s physically dangerous.”  

“Huh?”  

“I told you, the Cassel Mage Tower. It’s similar to that. Here, the issue lies.”  

Logan tapped his head lightly, revealing part of his worry.  

The doubts that emerged with the liberation of memories showed no signs of dissipating.  

“Is this related to the sorcerers of the Snake? To them as well?”  

“It’s similar. So don’t worry. My relationship with that subject is like oil and water.”  

This last sentence was merely a bluff. He couldn’t guarantee anything about the matters concerning the Holy Sword.  

‘That sword, who knows what havoc it could wreak, I can’t take anyone else with me.’  

Before his memory fully returned, the sword had simply been what he wanted to reclaim.  

But now it had become oddly concerning.  

If the name “Holy Sword” didn’t correspond to a powerful sacred energy, it should instead be called a cursed blade.  

A sword that interferes with one’s mind could only belong in legends of cursed blades.  

‘…No.’  

As those thoughts raced, a sudden idea crossed his mind.  

‘Wait, is that divine power genuine? Just recently, the incident with the previous Pope…’  

A late realization struck him like a bolt.  

Not to mention Vanitas, the meaning enclosed within that name…  

“Could it really be a cursed sword…”  

“Pardon?”  

“No, never mind. Anyway, can you understand?”  

Feeling the nod behind him, Logan let out a sigh of relief.  

‘Going alone is indeed the right move.’  

Given his current skills, he could likely navigate any worst-case scenario and escape just fine.  

Assuming he treated the Holy Sword like a cursed blade, he believed he could avoid such dire circumstances entirely.  

If things turned ugly, he could discard the sword on the spot.  

In his previous life, there was no way that sword had returned; however, the sword piercing through space, Sky Piercing Slash, was not limited to merely breaking through the dungeon’s barriers.  

Logan’s crimson eyes glinted coldly.  

* * *  

“Again?!”  

“Yeah. I’ll be back within a month, or rather, a few weeks. I appreciate your support once more.”  

“Excuse me? Am I your servant or something? Why must I keep pretending to be His Majesty!? This could backfire!”  

Rick’s rebellion held valid points.  

Initially, it had been somewhat entertaining, and the second time allowed him to relish an unanticipated honeymoon with his wife, Layla.  

Yet even that has its limits; no matter how the King begged, it wouldn’t bode well if he were actually discovered assuming the role of the monarch.  

At least, what bugged him the most was the various things he’d charmed from the King’s father, and he had no doubt that Lord Dwayne would chuckle upon finding out.  

Neither did it seem plausible that this apathetic master would generously compensate him, so Rick had to find a way out for himself.  

“If this goes on, I’ll get used to it! Why is a country’s king frequently disappearing?!”  

“Don’t worry. You’re doing splendidly.”  

“I’m saying it’s not okay!”  

“Feeling rebellious, are we?”  

“Shit…”  

Logan chuckled lightly as he patted the sulking Rick on the shoulder.  

“I’ll give you a nice gift when I return. Just hold out a little longer.”  

“For that?!”  

“Artifact.”  

“Assurance! Leave it to me!”  

“Alright. Make sure to take care of yourself as well.”  

Logan turned away after saying so.  

There was no need to reconvene further at the site of the dungeon.  

‘The Crown Mountains of the Empire are very well-known.’  

Moreover, during the duration away, he had already informed his wife of potential variables to manage.  

If anything else were to happen, she would surely handle it well.  

Still, more than that, he needed to hurry back.  

The war with the Empire lay loads closer now.  

‘This could be my last journey abroad.’  

Logan pondered as he stealthily slipped out of the castle under the cover of the dark night.



-chapter 343-

The history of present humanity is riddled with gaps, even regarding events that occurred a thousand years ago during the Great Emigration. 

Let alone the history of a thousand years prior, which is virtually unknown. 

However, there were stories passed down through the ages, much like folktales, since ancient times. 

– Disobedient children will be taken away by the demon with red eyes. 

This phrase, intended by parents to frighten disobedient children, echoed across the eastern and western ends of the continent, appearing similar regardless of location. 

While most historians claimed it explained the widespread threats from monsters existing in the world, a few historians held a different viewpoint. 

– In ancient times, there were monsters, no, rulers who abducted children throughout the entire continent. A ruler with red eyes. 

This was a story not told within the Mackleian family, where red eyes were inherited, and thus the shock was profound upon first hearing it. 

Why did that story resurface now? 

“Was the sacrifice to ascend to divinity human? Children, at that?” 

The question slipped out unintentionally, and the ancestor couldn’t respond. 

Yet, that silence spoke volumes. 

“Ha….” 

– For a human to ascend as a substitute means the advancement of all humanity. It was a sacrifice for the greater good. 

“Surely, it would have been the devil instead of a god.” 

– …No matter how distant a descendant they are, I cannot accept such an insult. 

“Considering you take that as an insult, I see there’s no further discussion.” 

The great hero, once a protector of humanity, was now absent. 

What remained was merely an embodiment of selfishness, indifferent to the lives of the innocent for their own desires. 

There was no desire to become a devil who might sacrifice them all for the sake of saving their family and country. 

‘Not as someone else, but as myself.’ 

Logan tried to turn away. 

But then— 

“Ugh!?” 

His body wouldn’t move. 

– I have waited nearly 2,000 years. Do you think I would abandon this ‘flesh’ I have finally obtained? 

The once-clear spirit of Zibrik Cassel abruptly roared in a twisted expression. 

There was no sweetness in its enticement anymore. 

Creak. 

Summoning all his strength, Logan barely turned his head to glare at the spirit of his ancestor. 

“The hero who saved humanity has become excessively corrupted. Aren’t you ashamed!?” 

– In this age where mana is disappearing, what do you think the probability is that a descendant has ascended to the level of a grand mage or possesses a comparable body? And what’s the chance that descendant will seize my legacy?! Do you have any idea!? I cannot give up! I will never give up! 

His response to the question of shame was simply inappropriate. 

– I will endure the loss of divinity. If you disagree, I have no choice but to forcibly take it! 

With that shout, the spirit morphed into a blinding white light, and the space where Logan stood began to collapse around him. 

– Hand it over! My flesh! 

In the fully white vision, the only discernible shape was that of a piercing red eye. 

It no longer resembled anything human. 

Creeeak. 

“Not a chance…!!” 

Woooom. 

Amid the gargantuan pressure squeezing him, Logan resisted against the immense force amplified by his heart. 

However, even with all his effort, the weight pressing down on him felt insurmountable. 

While he struggled with all his might, the fading white shards of space began to seep slowly into his body. 

There was no need to guess what it might be. 

‘Ah, no!’ 

In that moment, an unexpected event transpired. 

– What, what is this!? 

For some reason, the white energy invading his body made the ancestor’s spirit shriek in horror. 

As he concentrated his mind, he envisioned the golden aura clashing against the white energy enveloping him within, seemingly deriving the opposing response that had appeared among the followers of the Cassel Mage Tower. 

Fortunately, it seemed to have reacted to its origin. 

And that surprising turn of events seemed unforeseen even to the grand ancient hero. 

– Wh-what’s happening!? 

The expression of clear turmoil was evident. 

Don’t you see? 

Indeed, the divine sword vision had nothing to do with this ancestor… 

– How can you harness the power of origin? 

What did it mean? 

– Do you think I would give up because of that!? 

Along with the ancestor’s incomprehensible words, an increasing amount of white energy rushed toward his aura, pushing it down again. 

It meant overpowering the force through sheer numbers. 

Regrettably for Logan, it proved effective. After consuming half his strength in the ruins, he felt a pang of regret. 

‘If that’s the case,’ 

Crack. 

At that moment of resolution, the characteristic ‘Up’ activated, and Logan’s aura magnified exponentially in an instant, countering the encroaching white energy. 

Yet, it was still insufficient. 

– Not a chance! 

With a voice laced with rage echoing in his mind, enormous energy poured out, pressing down on Logan’s aura little by little. 

Despite activating his abilities, he felt steadily overwhelmed. 

‘Damn…’ 

In a moment of desperation, Logan inadvertently bit down on his teeth. 

Suddenly, an unexpected memory flashed before him. 

– I will certainly achieve this. Just watch! I will make you who despised me stand beneath my feet! 

The image of a man shouting while looking up at the sky appeared. 

That was undeniably a scene not drawn from Logan’s memory. 

Nonetheless, he could feel his anger, self-loathing, and indignation clearly emanating from the man. 

Thus, Logan grew enraged. 

‘That’s not mine!’ 

Completely different from the feeling he had when observing Zibrik Cassel’s life from beside him, this time it felt as if he was being immersed. 

Yet despite that looming peril, the assimilation process remained active. 

– I approach the greatest among the heavens. 

The mere term ‘heavens’ stirred discontent. 

– I greet the sole God of the Holy Empire, the agent of the Nine Gods. 

An agent. 

That was not who I was. 

Anger began to consume Logan’s soul, extending its pressure. 

– Agh! 

– Please, save me. Ughhh! 

– Mommmm! 

The voices of dying children atop the enormous magic circle echoed like screams. 

And then, he caught sight of that dignified ‘self’ overseeing the gruesome spectacle on the altar. 

In that instant, Logan suddenly snapped back to reality. 

Crack. 

‘That’s not me!!’ 

In the fleeting moment of self-awareness, Logan uncovered a fragment of possibility buried within Zibrik Cassel’s memories. 

A superior being who had reached the pinnacle through alternative means of magic. 

– The power of young lives holds potential… 

A minuscule fragment of knowledge Zibrik had prepared for his ascension stood as a stepping stone for Logan. 

It would be sufficient to leap over the low walls that remained. 

Woooom. 

Under the flash of inspiration, the core of his heart expelled another core. At the same time, the previously insufficient power erupted like an explosion. 

As the overwhelming uncontrolled white energy flooded toward him, Logan discerned an opportunity. 

‘Too late.’ 

With a jolt, he released his amplified power, forcefully expelling Zibrik Cassel’s energy entirely. 

– No—! 

“Yes!” 

His voice was unconsciously carried forth. 

And in that moment, Logan realized he had reclaimed full control over his body. 

Woooom. 

Furthermore, he could distinctly feel the vibrations resonating from seven cores amplifying within his heart, yet he could not afford to relish the exaltation of existence in this moment. 

Before him, Zibrik Cassel’s spirit began to reappear once again, blurring into form within the crumbling white space. 

– I-I cannot… How can this be…? 

That look of despair struck Logan as utterly disgusting. 

“You’ve become far too pitiful, ancestor. It’s time for you to depart, following the natural order.” 

There was no doubt that he was a hero who had saved the nearly doomed human race. 

Logan sought to maintain his decorum until the very end. 

Whether or not it triggered the ancestor’s spirit, Zibrik Cassel’s expression, one filled with vacancy, regained a glimmer of awareness upon meeting Logan’s gaze. 

He abruptly asked, 

– Let me ask you one last question. 

“What is it?” 

– How could the aura change? 

“Perhaps there are visions you wouldn’t understand. Within the power of the aura you disdained lies infinite potential.” 

Despite knowing about the divine sword vision, Zibrik didn’t seem to recognize it. 

The ancestor’s spirit appeared to be grasping at a deeper level. 

Zibrik’s words flowed haphazardly  – anything that disruptive completely denied the essence of the issue! 

– Vision? Ha! Such trifling techniques of mere aura hold no weight! This is about substance! How could a normal aura resist the divine…? Huh!? You really don’t know anything! 

The look of disbelief washed over Zibrik’s face. 

He could not agree with the dismissive tone regarding the divine sword vision, yet the spirit’s expressions of sincerity had undoubtedly increased. 

That feeling nurtured fundamental doubts in Logan’s heart. 

However— 

– Who are these entities that dare to meddle with my creation…? 

The time had come to handle this matter first. 

As Logan observed the spirit’s wrathful and distorted expression regarding his works, he felt a chill settle within his chest. 

Woooom. 

“On your way, this descendant shall escort you.” 

With his level finally raised, the side effects of utilizing his traits had lessened. 

According to Logan’s will, the golden aura accelerated the collapse of the white space. 

As the superior aura user had achieved the ultimate understanding against space, the Cassel ancestor’s spirit began to fade at an alarming rate. 

– I will never give in…! 

“It’s time to leave, ancestor.” 

With Logan’s words, the surroundings shattered, and the white space vanished. 

In its place, the gray plaza re-emerged before Logan’s eyes. 

And in that instant— 

Crackle! 

The sword, which had been inverted on the altar, began to quiver. 

The holy sword, Vanitas, had released a small sound from the pommel that had begun to sparkle with vigor. 

Simultaneously, the divine energy emitting from the holy sword vanished before Logan’s eyes. 

“Vanitas… What was the meaning behind that?” 

The ancient dialect for falsehood or vanity solidified its strange nuances. 

It seemed Logan finally understood the sword’s perplexing title. 

“And now…” 

Questions still lingered. 

Doubts regarding the divine sword vision and what Zibrik Cassel stated about the substance changing. 

Nonetheless, both issues felt trivial compared to the heavy realities ahead. 

Resolving those queries wouldn’t guarantee victory in the war against the empire. 

‘Perhaps those from the Cassel Mage Tower might hold the answers.’ 

Yet it wasn’t possible to set those worries aside entirely. 

For now— 

“I need to focus on reality.” 

Fortunately, he had genuinely stepped into the supreme level much more smoothly than anticipated. Besides his mentor, he finally felt confident against the sword spirit, Tris Hornsby. 

Regardless of the proud evolution, the feeling that his strength was building incrementally to halt the empire gave him confidence. 

But the immediate concern remained— 

“What should I do with that sword?” 

Before him lay the sanctified sword, its divine powers now absent. 

Logan’s gaze settled upon it, once again calm as the reality before him settled.



-chapter 330-

To find a safe route that a sizable merchant guild could utilize, the number of potential paths was reduced to a mere few dozen.  

However, when it came to routes that could accommodate thousands, or even tens of thousands of troops without incident, the choices dwindled to just a handful.  

In reality, there were exactly three routes identified.  

The “Merchant’s Road” connecting the trade hubs of Kyle and Luspelheim,  

the “Hunter’s Way” winding south around the northern demonic forest to link the northern hunting towns, and  

the “Adventurer’s Path” bypassing the northern mountains to connect the southern cities.

“If we are to speak precisely, all routes can be considered merchant paths since they are essentially roads made for profit,” Logan pointed out.  

At his words, Damian tilted his head in confusion.  

“Are you suggesting that all three routes will serve as invasion paths?”  

“Of course.”  

“…Even the Central Avenue can handle an army of 100,000 troops all at once. Now you’re saying the same for the north-south trade routes…?”  

“The Imperial army far exceeds those numbers.”

In reality, when the Empire first launched its invasion in his past life, the concluding efforts of the Sword Saint and the Esperanza territory troops managed to hold up an Imperial army that numbered well over 100,000 for more than a week at the border.  

Thanks to the time bought by the Kingdom’s most formidable aura user and the strongest knight order, the Grandia Royal Family quickly mobilized their forces.

However, the circumstances were different now.

“It is possible.”  

“…How can you be so certain?”  

“Well that is”  

In his past life, you said those words.

“I’ve heard about it.”  

“Pardon?”  

From you.

Damian, unable to hide his incredulity at such an assertive statement, could only flash a perplexed expression, prompting Logan to smile reassuringly.  

“Of course, we’ll be setting up the Grand Magic Circles too.”  

Logan had proclaimed this with utmost confidence, yet Damian remained bewildered. This gave the impression that decisions regarding policies that might cost an exorbitant sum were being made based on merely random hearsay.  

Nevertheless, with the King’s serious demeanor, Damian felt a rising sense of suffocation.  

“Well, considering the consistent achievements he had made, I can’t say it’s entirely impossible.”  

Heaving a sigh, Damian decided against further arguments.

“Pardon?”  

“We have the best professionals in the world.”  

“Ah…”  

With a wry smile at Logan’s confident expression, Damian sent a silent prayer for the wellness of his compatriots, who were bound to have arduous times ahead.

“It feels strange…”  

As he rolled about the bed, Hamal stumbled to his feet, stretching his short arms and yawning explosively.  

Rubbing his seemingly protruding belly, he blinked to find freshly baked bread and warm tea set neatly on the table nearby. A basin filled with washwater was placed just outside the door.  

“There’s surely nothing wrong, but…”  

Is there really nothing wrong? A decade ago, he had never imagined living such luxury, reduced to the status of a discarded dwarf slave due to the incompetence of that dwarf master.  

Now, the owner of the Taren Magic Workshop, a significant figure responsible for national affairs and a close aide to the king, he had grown accustomed to having guards at his side for security.  

However, something felt off.  

“Why am I so bored?”  

Could it be because the workshop was running too smoothly?  

‘I can’t purposely break something either.’  

Lost in thought while munching on the bread, Hamal suddenly froze.  

“Now that I think about it, I feel like creating something… Wait!”  

Startled, he covered his mouth and looked around, as if he had heard someone’s voice speaking faintly.  

—Isn’t your race naturally gifted in crafting?  

The whisper of a long-absent demon came to mind, prompting Hamal to shake his head vigorously.  

“Ugh, no, no. I’m just overthinking this. Come on! Not creating anything and just playing around is so much better!”  

Shaking a fist in a self-reassuring manner, he tried to convince himself, yet an undeniable itch to create overwhelmed him after not crafting anything for nearly half a year.  

“What if I just do a little sculpting?”  

Thinking of his first love, he recalled the dwarves who had retreated deep into the mountains to escape humans. There had been a damsel among them who had gifted him true happiness with her unparalleled gaze.  

“…Nuar.”  

As memories flooded back, including mishaps of trying to recreate those mesmerizing eyes only to be caught in trouble, nostalgia washed over him.  

“Ah, every time I think about that…”  

It seemed as though he had subconsciously forgotten her over the past few periods.  

“I have failed to honor your memory, Nuar. I’m sorry.”  

In that instant, a desire to seize his hammer and chisel ignited within him again. Although he’d never acknowledge it, it was indeed a joy rooted within his dwarven lineage, despite the ridiculous fantasy surrounding the notion of crafting as an adventure.  

“Alright. Sculpting is just a hobby.”  

As he rationalized, pulling himself off to leave his room, he suddenly paused when…  

“Hamar!?”  

BANG!  

“Oof!”  

As if struck by a sudden collision to the nose, Hamal couldn’t avoid tumbling backward.  

“Uh? Haha… Why were you there?”  

Walking boldly through the door was a one-armed dwarf named Tamer, sporting an awkward smile.  

“Ugh… What? Why were you there, you damn punk? Is it a crime to be in my own room?”  

With blood trickling from his nose, Hamal approached menacingly, only to cause Tamer to stumble back in fright.  

“Wh-wh-why are you acting like this?!”  

“Because I was planning on taking a day to set a date soon!”  

“N-no! Not at all! It’s not the time!”  

“But here’s what’s happening actual now!”  

“There are orders from the King!”  

At Tamer’s desperate declaration, Hamal halted in shock.  

“What?”  

His expression stiffened; trepidation settled in deep.  

“They… ordered for two fortifications to be constructed within three months!”  

“And you’re saying what now?! Two fortifications? In three months?”  

“Yes.”  

“What kind of madness is this? I’m pretty sure they were talking about castles!”  

“I think it is indeed castles!”  

“Are they out of their minds? That castle was not small!”  

“But they say you can recall what was created back when we built the Aegis Fortress!”  

“That was that fortress! And I was deep in a trench! Can’t they just not tell me to do it again?”  

In utter disbelief, Hamal opened his mouth once again, yet Tamer’s unchanging tone indicated the dreadful news would not let up.  

“They said it must be built with stone and… two!”  

With that revelation, unexpectedly, Hamal realized he was indeed at the mercy of fate.  

THUNK.  

“Ugh… Damn it… Why did I even say I was bored?”  

Among his futile attempts to scream in frustration, tears of realization streamed down Hamal’s cheeks.

-chapter 340-

**”He has indeed dug deep in just three months.”**

Sufficiently wide to allow ten people to walk side by side, the corridor was adorned with dynamic murals.  

‘Dragons, humans, lizardmen… Are they all ancient races?’  

No matter the pigment used, not a single image had faded despite eons passing by.  

Among them, what caught his eye first was a massive dragon breathing flames, scorching an enormous mountain range, surrounded by warriors of various races standing before it.  

Traditional enemies, displayed shoulder to shoulder, opposed the dragon. The murals continued on either side, chronicling the story before and after the conflict began.

Historians claimed that ancient transcendent beings or grand sorcerers had deliberately placed traps to obstruct those who dared to trespass without permission.

The vast majority of unearthed remains indeed possessed such treasures.  

Historians surmised that these mighty ancients held extraordinary power akin to deities, hoarding riches within their domains.

Golden coins fabricated from eras beyond memory formed hills, while every kind of jewel turned into decorations and artifacts radiated splendid light.

What he glimpsed in fleeting memories from the past now felt more tangible than anticipated.  

Before his eyes lay an unreal spectacle.  

It seemed this hoard could easily exceed the kingdom’s yearly national budget.

Buzz.

‘Nothing else matters. Only the books. The kind of literature.’  

As a highly advanced aura user, possessing abnormally keen senses, he was capable of such a feat.

Having now structured the power into finer strands, the web-like force moved far more slowly but more delicately through the treasures.  

Nevertheless,  

No matter how many times he repeated this process, nothing fitting his vision came forth.
