From afar, multiple distant voices reached his ears as bushes began to stir.  

The hidden workers were all fleeing in unison.  

It wouldn’t take long for word to spread that a silver aura user had slaughtered the imperial knights.  

‘So, I need to pick apart the ruins as quickly as possible.’  

Logan’s gaze turned toward the tunnel, where he could feel a divine force calling out to him.



-chapter 334-

Without even moving, Viktor was nearly invisible to ordinary eyes thanks to his artifact equipment and enhanced physical abilities from becoming a superhuman. These attributes allowed him to maximize the effectiveness of the Sword Saint’s movement technique, Phantom Shadow, by several times.

The central temple, known for having tighter security than most royal palaces, had not a single guard who noticed Viktor as he moved from shadow to shadow, even evading the keen senses of the Holy Knights.

However, just as he reached his target building, Viktor had to stop.

Among the temple buildings, all filled with an air of antiquity, one white building stood out, not because of its size but because of its heavy security. Despite being smaller than even a common chapel in the MacLaine Diocese, the security surrounding this building was extraordinarily tight.

This was Viktor’s original destination. The sight of its airtight defenses, suggesting that the Saintess was inside, had initially been a relief.

But soon, something unexpected disturbed Viktor’s senses.

“…Magic?”

Although he wasn’t as keen as his lord and master, Viktor’s senses were unnaturally developed compared to other knights of his rank. His heightened awareness detected an unusual flow of energy coursing through the target building.

“Magic in a temple?”

The temple acknowledged other supernatural powers like force and mana, but it denigrated them as lesser powers compared to divine power.

So, to find a security system based on magic within the temple was indeed astonishing. Yet, Viktor quickly realized that it might make sense.

“If the person confined there has reached the pinnacle of holy law, then a divine barrier would be meaningless.”

This only increased the likelihood that Saintess Illia was inside.

Though it felt a bit wasteful to have prepared a method to bypass a divine barrier, this situation would actually make things easier for him.

Everything seemed to be going smoothly, but suddenly, Viktor felt a presence that poured cold water over his confidence.

“Wow, I’ve heard the temple knights are rigid, but I didn’t think it would be to this extent. The discipline here must be incredibly strict.”

A middle-aged man with a grinning face slipped through the ranks of the temple knights standing guard.

Unlike the Holy Knights, who wore armor adorned with overlapping concentric circles in nine different colors or a single color, this middle-aged man wore armor engraved with an extremely ornate golden dragon design, and he openly played around in front of the temple knights.

“Hey, hey!”

He tapped their shoulders and waved his hand in front of their eyes, but the Holy Knights remained unresponsive. Losing interest, the middle-aged man plopped down and hung his head.

“The higher the rank of a Holy Knight, the less emotion they show? The more elite, the more they turn to stone? How boring.”

It looked as if he was deliberately provoking the Holy Knights in the middle of the central temple. A common person would have been severely punished for such behavior, but the Holy Knights purposely averted their gaze, as if the man didn’t even exist.

“Hey, don’t be like that. I don’t want to be here either. This is such a pointless task. Why would a general of the Empire—…ugh, if it weren’t for the prince, no, if it weren’t for the crown prince, I would’ve just…”

The man threw punches at the air, looking truly pitiful. His tone was light, and his demeanor even lighter, but what came out of his mouth could not be dismissed.

Not just a knight, but a general. In the Empire, the title “general” was used only for the commanders of the Eastern 8th Legion or the Western 7th Legion.

In other words, this seemingly carefree man was none other than—

“An Aura User.”

The man, with his blonde hair and pale skin, might have passed for a reasonably handsome middle-aged man if not for the long scar running across his right cheek and his clouded left eye, which looked nearly useless.

“…Who was he again?”

Thanks to his master and lord’s insistence, Viktor had memorized the characteristics of all the Empire’s legion commanders. He quickly found the answer to his question.

“Western 7th Legion Commander. Crazy Sword, Max Illeia.”

“The Empire’s western forces likely won’t invade our side. If the Empire starts a war, they’ll have to strengthen their defenses on the western front as well.”

“Though if things become critical, they might even deploy superhuman legion commanders.”

That’s what his master had said, pointing out a few individuals to watch out for, and Max Illeia was among the most dangerous.

“He’s known to be a mid-level Aura User. However, in battle, they say he’s far more powerful than that.”

“Interestingly, he’s a self-made man who rose from a mercenary to become a noble of the Empire, and is notorious for his rough personality. In other words, he’s a battle maniac.”

“It’s rumored that the Emperor kept him close during his youth, fascinated by his talent, but later sent him to command the western legions because he grew tired of his personality.”

In other words, this man was indeed the Empire’s legion commander.

“Why is a superhuman from the Empire here?”

It was bewildering, but there was no time to unravel that mystery now. Viktor suddenly felt grateful for his unnaturally sharp senses. Max Illeia’s ability, especially in this situation, was a major obstacle.

As Viktor carefully moved away, wary of entering Max’s sensory range—

“Damn it! This is so boring! Who’s coming here? At least bring your commander out! Let me have a sword fight with him!”

Max suddenly shouted, jumping to his feet.

“The Divine Sword? Let’s see if he’s worthy of that grand title. As a general of the Empire, I’ll personally verify it! Even my old man’s nickname is Sword Soul, but Divine Sword? Come on.”

Watching him cause a scene, Viktor couldn’t help but think that even the Emperor would get tired of this man.

“Is he out on a mission? Then call him back! Why don’t you? Are you scared of me?”

It was clear why the Holy Knights remained unresponsive. They must have been strictly ordered not to engage with him to avoid provoking him.

Finally, when the Holy Knights still didn’t respond, Max sat down again, exhausted from his own outburst.

“Ah, what a bunch of boring guys. I’m bored to death.”

Yaaaawn.

As he let out a long yawn, his face suddenly changed, as if he had noticed something.

“Huh?”

He smirked.

“…Somewhere nearby, interesting.”

Laughing to himself, Max muttered something and then suddenly stood up again.

“I’ll be back in a bit. Don’t snitch to the Crown Prince about me disappearing, okay?”

With that, he vanished, leaving behind a completely pointless warning.

“Thank goodness.”

Viktor let out a sigh of relief, feeling the cold sweat that had been running down his back.

While he was confident that his artifact and the Phantom Shadow technique would allow him to infiltrate without being detected by a stronger opponent, rescuing and escorting the Saintess out was an entirely different matter.

And now, whatever the reason, the greatest obstacle had just disappeared, making this the perfect opportunity.

“His known abilities place him one level above me.”

There was no time to analyze the situation. Viktor’s body, like a phantom, slipped into the building, avoiding the flow of mana.

The interior of the building was smaller than he had expected.

It seemed like a unique prayer room, with three floors and only one room on the top floor.

And inside that room was the Saintess.

Even the worn and baggy robes she wore couldn’t hide her radiance. However, her complexion was somewhat pale as she prayed with her eyes tightly closed, looking utterly holy.

It wasn’t just a metaphor. There was an actual cloud-like aura of divine power, invisible to the common eye, overflowing around her.

The two Holy Knights assigned to watch over her were so overwhelmed by reverence that they stared at her blankly.

Thanks to this—

Thud. Thud.

It was even easier to subdue them.

“It’s been a while, Saintess.”

The moment Viktor’s voice reached her ears, Illia turned to look at him.

Her eyes, widening with surprise, were filled with joy, a rare sight even in such a dire situation.

“Sir Viktor?”

“Yes, it’s me. I’m here to escort you out. We must hurry.”

“How…how did you get here?”

“It’s a long story. We need to move first.”

Perhaps it was because she felt somewhat relieved.

As Viktor smiled softly at the Saintess, he heard an unpleasant, no, an impossible voice.

“So, this was the place. I thought it was outside earlier.”

When Viktor turned his head, he saw the scarred face.

“You’ve got some peculiar skills.”

Max Illeia grinned as if he found it amusing.

It seemed that the temple’s security measures, which were meant to block out external noise, had dulled his senses.

“Damn it.”

The problem wasn’t just that Viktor had allowed the man to approach unnoticed.

In his relief, Viktor had removed his mask, which meant the man had seen his face.

“There’s no escaping now.”

Even though Viktor wasn’t famous yet, the Empire’s intelligence network would soon be able to track him down.

So there was only one option left.

Screeech.

“Let’s hope your sword skills are as impressive as your tricks. Try not to scream too much. Let’s just keep this between us, shall we?”

Max Illeia, clearly thrilled, lowered his voice and grinned from ear to ear.

The only option was to kill this lunatic right here, right now.

And do it swiftly.

“Saintess, please stay back.”

“…Yes.”

“Good choice. I wouldn’t want the Saintess to get hurt. In exchange, I’ll make sure your death is quick.”

He sneered.

Defeating an opponent who was clearly stronger in a single strike?

It would be impossible with any ordinary method.

Viktor quickly racked his brain.

“Max Illeia. His ability is known as ‘intuition.’ You could call him a lesser version of Jerome Decaid. But in battle, especially against multiple opponents, his ability gives him an advantage.”

Intuition—a vague and ambiguous ability. But they weren’t on a battlefield, and Max was more eager for a one-on-one fight.

Just as Viktor had gauged his opponent’s level, Max had also assessed Viktor’s strength.

Complacency.

Furthermore, Max’s earlier remark suggested another possibility.

“Thought it was outside, but it was here. His ability clearly has its limits.”

“The manifestation of an ability is a reflection of one’s desires. Naturally, some abilities seem useless or strange.”

“Hawk-like vision that can see people beyond the horizon or hearing that can pick up sounds kilometers away—these are still somewhat useful.”

“But the more ambiguous the ability, the less efficient and useful it is. For example, something like the ability of ‘peace’…”

Shaking his head, Viktor dismissed the irrelevant thoughts.

Max’s intuition didn’t reveal everything.

If so, there was a chance.

“Put everything into one strike.”

Viktor concentrated the force from his heart’s Force Core.

His sword began to emit a peculiar grayish light, swelling with power.

But Max remained unfazed.

“Oh? That’s quite impressive.”

Of course.

Channeling Aura into the blade before even making a move wasn’t for slaughtering weaklings. It was merely a waste of energy.

This only fueled Max’s arrogance.

“A gray Aura? How unusual.”

Pat.

With a light step that barely seemed like an effort, Viktor shortened the distance between them.

At the same time, Max swung his sword.

The red Aura condensed at the tip of his blade before suddenly stretching out, aiming for Viktor’s heart.

It all happened in an instant, but any Aura User could react in time.

In that moment, Max’s one remaining eye flickered with doubt.

‘He’s not trying to dodge?’

His ability, “intuition,” had clued him in on Viktor’s intentions, which seemed absurd.

‘Is he trying to die together? But…’

Realizing this, Max’s red Aura shot forward even faster.

‘The only one dying is you.’

Max was only disappointed that his anticipated amusement would end too quickly.

However—

Puuuck.

Woooong.

As Max’s heart was pierced, Viktor’s gray Aura blade expanded several times over, instantly piercing through his opponent’s heart.

Puuuck.

“Guh, guh!”

“Urgh!”

It all happened in the blink of an eye.

‘Did I… succeed?’

Seeing the shock in his enemy’s eyes, Viktor forced himself to endure the excruciating pain.

“You, you crazy bastard…”

Max’s remaining eye widened, and he cursed.

A moment later, a sharp scream echoed from behind Viktor.

“Kyaaah! Sir Viktor!”

“I’m… fine…”

Confirming that the light in his enemy’s eyes had faded, Viktor swiftly pulled out the sword embedded in his heart. As blood spurted out like a fountain, he felt an inexplicable weakness in his limbs.

‘This… this can’t be happening.’

Heal.

You can do it!

Viktor clenched his teeth and ordered his body to respond.

The five Force Cores within his heart spun continuously around the central core, emitting Force.

And the “endless vitality” of his ability wasn’t just about mobilizing more Force than his level.

This ability’s most unique feature was its regenerative capability, healing any wound.

It was this that Viktor had gambled on, yet his heart refused to obey.

And Viktor quickly realized why.

‘O-Oh, Aura. Damn it, how foolish.’

His expectations were only half met.

While the five Force Cores managed to prevent his heart from being completely destroyed through a momentary Aura conversion, the lingering Aura from his opponent was hindering his regeneration.

Aura, a force that destroys everything.

It was preventing his recovery, and his ability wasn’t mature enough to overcome it.

In his haste, Viktor had underestimated the situation.

But—

‘I… I can’t die like this.’

Viktor gritted his teeth, clinging to the last spark of life.

And then—

“Blood… blood! No!”

Illia, who had cried out in desperation, pressed down on Viktor’s chest, where the blood was gushing out.

“Please…”

Divine power radiated from her hand, shining with a bright white light.

The holy energy quickly spread throughout his body, revitalizing his dying flesh and restoring clarity to his fading mind.

As his brain regained its function, the conditions for survival became clear in Viktor’s mind.

‘A power that destroys Aura.’

Fortunately, Viktor knew one technique that could accomplish this.

The 5th Form of the Divine Sword Art: Life Severing Slash (生靈斬, Saengryeongcham).

Until now, he had only been able to execute it with great effort during training. But if he could fully master and apply it, it might be possible.

His life, hanging by a thread, triggered an intense concentration, and the divine power stabilizing him provided the foundation for that focus.

Before long, every aspect of Life Severing Slash became clear in Viktor’s mind. Soon, the enemy’s lingering Aura in his heart was obliterated.

At that moment, Viktor realized that he had just broken through another wall, ascending to a higher level.

Woooong.

His Force Core birthed a sixth nucleus, and the surge in power doubled his Force and enhanced his ability, quickly healing his heart’s wound.

Moments later, Viktor gasped for breath as if he had barely escaped drowning.

“Guh, guh!”

“Huh? What? This…”

Tears streaming down her face, Illia looked astonished.

Seeing the tears in her eyes, Viktor involuntarily coughed up blood.

Cough.

‘That was really insane. I was lucky.’

Relief washed over him, along with a surge of confidence. He had gained so much from this insane gamble.

Not only had his level increased, but he had also killed a superhuman from the Empire in a single strike, and without causing a commotion.

The fact that two superhumans had clashed, yet the soundproofing magic hadn’t even been disrupted.

So Viktor smiled.

“It’s okay now. Let’s go, Saintess.”

To reassure her.

“Kyaaah!”

“…?”

“Oh, no. I’m sorry. Let’s go quickly.”

He hadn’t considered how a blood-soaked smile might look to someone else, but fortunately, the Holy Knights outside remained quiet.

Viktor carried the Saintess out of the building without incident.

And the next morning—

“A fake Saintess, Illia Gabon, has been excommunicated.”

A piece of news that would shake the world, starting from the Holy Kingdom, began to spread.

Adam groaned involuntarily under the weight of the load on his back.

the Teresa Gorge, known as a crossroads leading to the Esperanza Duke Territory in the north and the northeastern part of the Empire, along with the eastern end of the Hunter’s Way.

“Hey, Squad 13! Pick up the pace a bit!”

At just fifty years of age, Clayton, who had achieved the level of an archmage and belonged to the younger generation among the superhumans, was openly praising his young disciple.  

And for Clayton, it was entirely warranted.  

His young apprentice possessed talents that went beyond merely achieving the status of an archmage before turning twenty.  

The seemingly simple scene was not a straightforward product of chance.  

To make golems move like real people was a task that required tremendous skill—exceeding even the bounds of magical power. For an experienced mage like him, controlling more than one or two golems was an arduous challenge.  

When he handled a large number of golems, he would set their behaviors based on magical principles in advance, simply adding magic power afterward.  

When commanding dozens of them, he had only managed to have them follow basic commands, thus he’d always thought that was the limit the situation could allow.  

But this young disciple was managing a full twenty golems as if they were people.  

Despite having awakened a higher form of elemental affinity with Earth and feeling everything perfectly attuned to the land around, it still seemed unbelievable.

It was a concentration and control ability that could not help but impress him.

It truly was astounding.

‘Those looks… Is it possible they possess the bloodline of legendary dragons? Hehehe.’  

Such a silly thought involuntarily crossed his mind.

– Empty the ground thoroughly and refill. The more limits are encountered, the faster growth occurs; research lies beyond limits.  

All this stemmed from the teachings he had spread throughout the Mages’ Guild.  

In truth, the students of the Golem School had shown considerable growth in comparison to their peers from the other four mage towers.  

Because since the days of the McLain territory, they had endured burdensome working schedules imposed by Logan and their master.

As a result, mages from the royal mage battalion, which belonged to the royal family, had begun to flock to construction sites.

“Uwaah!”

Even when terrified knights desperately swung their swords, hoping to strike the reaper,  

Thud.  

The leather armor wrapped in silver aura easily deflected the attacks without sustaining a scratch.  

“An aura barrier…”  

A technique possible only for those at the intermediate level or higher in Aura usage.  

The knights, knowing precisely what that meant, dropped their swords with vacant expressions.  

“That aside, it’s only for a moment!”  

“If we press him hard enough, we’ll win!”  

Despite their fading hopes, the knights who continued to flame their fighting spirit were ultimately met with despair, falling without resistance under the continued assault.  

In mere moments, close to fifty knights had crumbled.  

And only then did elite knights begin to burst forth from the tunnel.  

“Who are you?!”  

They shouted, and Yaksel Frigment’s axe unleashed a crimson Force Blade.  

It was not merely an elongated blade but rather one that took the form of the axe itself, its head suddenly enlarging to the size of a great sword.  

The crimson Force Axe flickered with an unusually bright red hue.  

‘Oho. Is it a transformation of Force, along with compression?’  

That form could only be displayed by an elite knight at the pinnacle of skill, clearly showcasing how he maintained his position as the supreme commander of the Eastern 1st Legion.  

Yet, Logan’s gaze drifted not toward the shouting Yaksel but rather to the sorcerer standing behind him and the knights.  

‘Huh?’  

A softly flowing gray mana.  

While Logan couldn’t ascertain it from far away last night, this fellow was indeed a mage – from the Cassel Magic Tower, no less.  

‘The heir to the mage lineage, Zibrik Cassel.’  

Now, he could clearly speculate about their origins.  

In hindsight, it seemed strange they knew of this location.  

Yet there was one question that arose.  

The reason he hadn’t noticed its identity from afar wasn’t because the sorcerer was concealing something.  

It was simply because…  

‘Weak. He hasn’t properly refined his mana. At most, he’s a beginner of the 6th circle, barely at the level of a superhuman.’  

It was puzzling how he could attempt to dissolve the barrier with that level, but Logan couldn’t afford to ask about it now. He simply kept a stiff expression on Yaksel.  

“Is there no value in even exchanging a few words?”  

Just as Yaksel took a cautious step forward with a hard expression, the knights behind him moved in unison, quickly rearranging their formation.  

Knights bearing shields or heavy weapons formed the front lines, while swords and spear-wielding knights positioned themselves behind, preparing to lash out at a moment’s notice.  

They intended to fill the flanks and rear as Logan sliced through the leading knights.  

Then, just in front of them, Yaksel, brandishing the gleaming Force Axe, spoke again.  

“How dare a superhuman involve himself in the Empire’s affairs! You shall pay with your life for your sins.”  

His confident expression held no trace of fear.  

Indeed, after trading a few blows, his surrounding knights would likely enclose Logan.  

Knights of the Empire, especially the elite of the Legion, were known to fear nothing in the face of death, so even if many were sacrificed, they would not retreat.  

Thus, it was not incorrect for them to believe they could slay a superhuman with merely their numbers.  

‘If they were ordinary Aura users or a low-tier superhuman, perhaps.’  

No, perhaps even at the intermediate level, if they were willing to absorb a majority of casualties, it could be achievable.  

Yet for these knights now grappling with Logan, it was but a futile story.  

Even if he forcibly reduced his level to facilitate the conversion of his aura, he wasn’t someone who could easily be handled by their numbers.  

So, what truly lingered in his mind were the sorcerer standing behind them.  

Of course, it wasn’t solely Logan who was apprehensive.  

“The mage!”  

“Don’t worry yourself, Knight.”  

The moment Yaksel’s shout erupted, Logan vanished from his position, moving in a ghost-like manner toward the sorcerer.  

“Ugh!”  

Then, on the heels of Yaksel’s startled voice, he appeared right in front of the sorcerer.  

Bang.  

The silver blade of aura sliced through at such a terrifying speed that even Yaksel couldn’t follow its movement.  

However,  

Thud.  

The blade met a transparent barrier surrounding the sorcerer.  

“Huh?”  

Clang!  

A sharp sound echoed as something shattered within the sorcerer’s grasp, and soon the transparent barrier began to gradually dissipate.  

“Tsk.”  

Boom!  

At the same moment, the silver blade struck the vanishing barrier, cleaving through its remains, but its rate of extinction only quickened; the barrier did not crumble easily.  

Taking advantage of that gap,  

“Get lost!”  

The sorcerer’s magic erupted right before Logan’s nose, astonishingly wide-eyed.  

Boom!  

An explosive shockwave erupted.  

Thanks to that shockwave, the remnants of the barrier completely vanished, but Logan was pushed back several dozen meters in the process.  

‘Damn it.’  

He felt regret.  

Had he displayed his true strength, whatever artifact the sorcerer possessed would have been cut through, and he would have decimated the sorcerer in one sweep.  

But still, he couldn’t afford to dwell on regret. Before he could regain his stance, a deadly aura surged from behind him.  

“Die!”  

A massive red axe that seemed to engulf Logan’s entire body loomed.  

Amidst that overwhelming pressure, a faint silver flickered briefly.  

Boom!  

And the outcome stood in stark contrast to the apparent ferocity.  

“Ugh!”  

Yaksel, staggering back, began to vomit blood as he staggered backward.  

While Logan merely took a few steps back to regain his composure, his demeanor remained unfazed.  

The disparity between Aura users and Force users was that stark.  

But still, there was something new in Logan’s eyes.  

‘Not bad.’  

He was about to shatter the axe in one fell swoop and behead him,  

But Logan sensed a flow of opposing aura attempting to contend with the destructive force underlying the opponent’s strikes.  

If the current level of control over his aura was merely raw awakening, then from the firm pressure he felt, 

he could probably endure at least ten exchanges without yielding.  

The implication was concerning.  

‘If he bears an innate skill among the Empire’s higher-tier power, I might have to take that into account.’  

That lesson was a valuable insight Logan took into consideration and made a mental note to investigate thoroughly upon his return.  

Yet even amidst such easy thinking, his body had already inched closer to Yaksel.  

Again, the sparkling silver flickered.  

It was to be a lethal strike aimed at solidifying the downfall of the injured opponent, but once again he was interrupted.  

“Captain!”  

“It can’t be like this!”  

Knights surged left and right like moths drawn to a flame.  

Their bodies and swords absorbed Logan’s strike intended for Yaksel.  

Splatter.  

Amidst the cascading corpses of the knights, Yaksel’s face was painted with fear, eyes widened beyond recognition.  

“No!”  

With a scream-like cry that tore from his throat, Yaksel’s eyes blazed red.  

“Kill him!”  

Acclaimed as untouched, Yaksel charged forth without hindrance alongside the knights who were previously surrounding Logan.  

“Die!”  

The lightning-fast strike came down harder than before, even stronger than the earlier exchange.  

His lower body was unyielding despite the heavy wounds, and the anger on his face didn’t falter.  

Both elements represented a testament to the training he must have undergone.  

However, the gap in levels was undeniably real.  

‘So many flaws.’  

Even with the number of gaps visible to Logan, he found it difficult to target them.  

The direct offensive was less than optimal. Throwing darts at the flank or attacking diagonally was not the issue.  

Neither could he disregard the spear aimed behind him nor the swords thrusting beneath his armpits.  

Regardless, he had to clear out the surrounding knights right then and there. Waste energy on an aura barrier in this skin-deep battle would be pointless.  

Regret arose anew.  

‘If only I could use Whip Blade.’  

But there was no other choice in that scenario.  

As Logan didn’t intend to go about slaying the witnesses, he had minimized his identity exposure as much as possible.  

Clang!  

He struck at the side of the axe, redirecting its course and spinning away. His agile movements left a silvery trail anew.  

Crack—!  

“Cough!”  

With a painful cry, the knights fell apart around him.  

A knight barely managing to retain a single arm fell wearily backward while Logan remained standing.  

But before he could savor the moment, yet again, he was faced with the vicious flash of an axe aiming for his side.  

In that very moment.  

“Take this!”  

A sharp scream echoed from afar, drawing a gray mist closing in around Logan’s head.  

‘This one could surely kill any superhuman!’  

Unless it was Logan himself.  

With a chilling smile, just as silver flickered once more,  

Slash.  

“Argh!”  

A significant wound appeared on Yaksel’s body, and the knights charging forward lost their lives in vain.

“This is the information that Philip of the merchant guild sent over. It seems Bishop Illya did not just enter into training without any reason.”

“The Pope’s words, not to mention Prince Barros’s visit to the Holy Nation… and the disappearance of the Saintess?”

At Damian’s words, Logan let out a low growl. He had been considering a similar line of thought.

The Sanctuary had traditionally kept a distance from worldly powers and maintained a politically neutral stance.

The ghosts’ artifacts lose their effectiveness over time without a master. That mechanism had not even been analyzed by Clayten yet.

In that regard, the ghosts that attacked Luis had ended up being helpful.

Flop.

Pause.

If Victor had exhibited a reaction on hearing this, Philip would just exclude him from the mission right then and there.

Click.

A grand, antiquated castle adorned with elaborate decorations.

As the group crossed the moat, knights and soldiers stationed at various points offered disciplined greetings.

After several inspections that followed, the party reached the innermost parts of the inner castle.

In front of a massive stone door, the guiding knight halted his steps.

“That is where Duke Gile is currently engaged in solitary training,” he remarked.

A chuckle escaped from among those following him at his words.

Everyone present was aware that the ruler of this kingdom had decided to forsake Duke Gile, yet the knight still displayed an air of respect towards the abandoned figure, which struck them as amusing.

“Was Duke Gile’s position so significant in Liberty?”

The one accompanying as Greet’s aide, Janzen, inquired, causing the knight from Liberty to flush red.

“…Please be cautious with your words. Duke Gile is a hero for the nation. He is one whom anyone in this country ought to respect.”

The knight’s discomfort was evident on his face.

Meat shields.

Swish!

Gag.

They turned the noble warriors into beasts.

Suddenly!

However, this wasn’t enough to satisfy him.

Gile retaliated, and within that instant, their destinies entwined.

In the tense clash of wills, an explosive shockwave marked the start of a chaotic duel, one Greet had never anticipated, ushering in what appeared to be a dark omen for both factions.

“Mission to subdue the monsters has been completed, Commander.”

“…It wasn’t necessary for you to come here in person, Commander. The situation in the Gaia Kingdom could have been resolved internally without your presence.”  

The adjutant’s statement was not incorrect. The southern region beyond the empire’s borders had a monster presence, particularly a rare high-grade monster, the Chimera, located in the southernmost part of the Gaia Kingdom, adjacent to the Southern Mountains.  

It was undoubtedly a threatening monster; however, it could have been dealt with by sending just one superhuman from the kingdom or four to five top knights. It was not a serious enough problem to warrant the dispatch of the Divine Crusaders’ commander.

“There are rumors that His Holiness is wary of your presence, Commander…”  

“Enough. It would be disrespectful to His Holiness.”  

“…Yes.”  

Although he forced an answer, the adjutant, Ryan Harper, was filled with dissatisfaction. It was understandable, given that the elite members of the Divine Crusaders, who prided themselves on being the world’s strongest knight order and the ultimate military force representing the will of the gods, were being used on such a distant frontier.  

However, Harmon’s thoughts differed slightly.  

“It is stranger that we, who are tasked with dealing with the enemies of the divine, have solely focused on the defenses of Noviens. Confronting monsters—monsters—is our original purpose. I believe this aligns with what His Holiness desires as well.”  

“Commander…”  

Seeing the pitiful expression on Ryan’s face made Harmon chuckle. He, too, was not a fool.  

He understood perfectly well the purpose of the new Pope wanting to keep a check on him. However, it was still within a range he could sufficiently comprehend.  

“The Order needs a new symbol. If my temporary absence from the center allows His Holiness to shine, then it is quite bearable.”  

For the message of the Nine Gods, who coordinated everything in the world, to be fully conveyed, a unified structure of the Order was necessary. Unlike the previous Pope, who cared only for his own wealth and power, there was sufficient faith in Pope Austin, who was sincere about delivering the will of the divine.  

That was Harmon’s conclusion.  

Of course, there were concerns lingering in his mind.  

“What news of the Saint?”  

“Pardon? I mentioned it to you not long ago…”  

“Nothing has changed?”  

“Yes, that is correct. But why do you care so much?”  

“Hmm? Is it strange?”  

“No, not at all. I just felt you’re overly concerned with the Saint. You generally didn’t have an interest in the Order’s politics before.”  

“Politics… Is that merely your opinion?”  

Seeing Harmon’s brows narrow, Ryan realized his mistake in wording.  

To address something publicly declared by the Order as mere politics was inappropriate.  

Pale-faced, he waved his hands in haste.  

“Ah, no, it’s not that I don’t trust the Order. I just don’t understand the situation…”  

“However, I absolutely do not suspect the Order!”  

Harmon couldn’t help but realize how others perceived him at that moment, watching Ryan deny it repeatedly.  

“It’s fine.”  

“Pardon?”  

“What’s wrong with expressing your own thoughts? So long as you don’t misinterpret and spread the will of the divine, it matters not, whether it is the Order or an individual.”  

Hearing that, Ryan briefly wore a flustered expression before hesitating to speak again.  

“…Are you saying my opinions go against the will of the Order?”  

“Yes.”  

Ryan’s expression turned blank at those words. The awkwardness of the moment was compelling.  

“Weren’t you supposed to be somewhat strict in such matters?”  

At that, Harmon chuckled lightly.  

The previous Pope had also been rather wary of him. Thus, it was customary for adjutants within the Divine Crusaders to be frequently replaced, perhaps due to his inflexible and fastidious character.  

Ryan had only been his adjutant for around eight months.  

Given the many events that transpired during that time, it would be hard for anyone to discern his character fully.  

‘I had no intentions of breaking any laws of the Order.’  

Thinking about the previous Pope and that swindler’s timidity made him chuckle again.  

Eventually, that swindler received his due punishment. Perhaps that too was guided by the will of the Nine Gods.  

“Strictness is only necessary when adhering to doctrines. The Order exists to spread and exemplify doctrines, not to distort them. If it is not mindless blasphemy, valid criticism must be accepted, be it from the Order or an individual.”  

Harmon laid his fist against the nine concentric circles engraved on his armor, swearing like a vow.  

He understood that the long-accumulated image could not be erased with one statement, thus declaring it through his faith in the divine.  

Fortunately, Ryan’s complexion brightened immediately upon hearing that.  

“Then, you won’t behead me or cut off my limbs…?”  

This made Harmon nearly stumble.  

It seemed that the rumors must have spread more wildly than imagined.  

“…Were there such rumors?”  

“W-well, h-haha. I truly thought it was just baseless gossip. Really!”  

Harmon couldn’t help but chuckle at that unnatural reaction.  

‘I’ll have to change this gradually.’  

However, at the moment, his curiosity was piqued more by what Ryan had just said.  

“That said, do you really perceive the declaration of the saint’s legitimacy as politics?”  

When one’s image hardens from solely focusing on training and cultivation, communication with others suffers.  

Harmon affirmed to himself that he needed to be more open. He awaited Ryan’s response.  

“…Yes. It was an utterly out-of-the-blue and strange event. After all, the Saint had assisted the current Pope Austin in unveiling the true nature of the fake Pope. But now, to claim that such a person had been fake, it’s only natural to feel perplexed.”  

“So you believe His Holiness was performing a political act by dismissing the Saint?”  

Ryan’s expression grew tense again. It appeared he was contemplating whether or not to respond truthfully.  

Nevertheless, possessing newfound courage, he nodded.  

“Yes. Honestly, thinking that way is much simpler.”  

“Is that the predominant opinion?”  

“Yes, it is.”  

“…I understand. Just as I thought.”  

Harmon sighed deeply.  

He had known the true Pope Austin would never do such a thing.  

“This new Pope is not that kind of person.”  

Thus, the sinking feeling caused by Ryan’s response could not be shaken off.  

He had known that Pope Austin, in reality, was not that person.  

After all, he believed the power of the gods could change even the hearts of the demi-gods over time.  

Yet now, it felt far too painful to accept.  

“Nevertheless, it looks like tonight will likewise be spent in prayer and training.”  

* * *  

“…To the Nine Gods who control the world.”  

On a brightly moonlit night.  

Kneeling on bare earth without an altar or idol, Harmon felt the divine power surging within him and sensed that the gods had responded to his prayers.  

It felt as if his heart had been cleansed, like being washed by crystal-clear water.  

And now, it was time to cleanse the body.  

Swish.  

Clang.  

With a soft flick, Harmon effortlessly drew the treatise sword, Purgatio, its clear sound revealing the pristine white blade.  

Although it could not be compared to the sacred sword Poena, which was strictly preserved in the Order’s underground, this sword was also a relic blessed by one hundred high priests. As the sword radiated with divine energy, it felt as though peace swept over his heart.  

Tap.  

He stepped lightly.  

With each step he took, the sword gracefully swirled.  

Receiving the moonlight, Purgatio reflected that light, revealing the divine power embedded in it, and the dance, which began as a prayer during the event honoring the Nine Gods, flourished into a beautiful light display against the darkened fields.  

With exceptionally lucid focus.  

The untamed path of the sword moved effortlessly with his will, and the light exuded by it granted him refreshing liberation.  

“Freedom in following the natural order.”  

A dance celebrating the divine will while rejoicing in the happiness derived within it.  

As the intensity of the dance reached its peak, the chaotic turmoil in his heart began to settle.  

As always, training following prayer did not betray his expectations.  

But.  

“The Saint…”  

As he recalled Ryan’s words, a behavior from the Order that he could not fathom once again twisted his heart.  

After decades of corruption, the Order had found the right path again.  

In the end, he believed it was a reward for faith in the divine’s will that guided everything.  

With a priest known for his integrity and the real saint, that combination should have been more than adequate.  

Yet here it was again, such behavior.  

“Pope Austin, has your once-earnest faith been consumed so swiftly by desire?”  

If that were truly the case, what was he supposed to do?  

– The Divine Crusaders cannot intervene in the Order’s political affairs.

The laws of the Order that he had engraved upon his heart weighed heavily upon him.  

Should he remain silent, just as when the prior Pope and his faction had disrupted the Order?  

During the impeachment crisis, the voice full of sincerity that pleaded with him resurfaced.  

– Commander! I have a request for you under the authority of a cardinal!  

– Commander, I hope…  

The Saint at that time undoubtedly held sincere feelings toward the divine.  

The long time spent seeing Pope Austin and the Saint clash clouded Harmon’s heart.  

Suddenly, the beautiful dance blended with harsh, discordant sounds. The fierce energy emanated from where the sword touched.  

While moments earlier, the dance had symbolized peace, this time it expressed anger.  

The wrath of punishment to descend upon those who defied the divine will manifested itself like sword blows onto the darkened fields.  

Swoosh!  

As the tip of the sword cleaved through the space, everything aligned in that direction was torn into halves.  

Even over one-hundred meters away, the trees in the forest, untouched by Harmon’s blade, struggled to maintain their form.  

The technique reflected his will to pass judgment upon everything that contradicted the divine will.  

And that technique was supported by the divine power that the gods had granted him. Forcing divine energy to intertwine with the power within him, that chain reaction continuously moved his sword.  

At that moment.  

Crackling!  

Boom!  

Everything his sword aimed for began to lose its shape and shatter.  

This devastation, resulting from a single sword, seemed unbelievable.  

However, it appeared that the wielder of that catastrophic might had no intention of stopping. Even as everything around twisted and lost its form, the one causing this havoc was determined to meticulously unpack every ounce of anger and conflict lingering in him through his dance.  

Unless someone intervened.  

“Harmon! Stop this immediately!”  

A voice echoed from afar.  

A high and clear voice he felt he had heard before quelled the burning fury in him.  

In that instant, Harmon recalled the owner of that voice.  

“Saint?”  

His sword came to an abrupt halt.  

From a distance, a figure adorned in black suddenly emerged.  

“How… are you able to be at such a distance… and what incomprehensible strength…”  

A figure bearing a shattered sword trickled blood from the corner of his mouth, appearing as if injured from the effects of Harmon’s strike.  

As Harmon beheld him, he noticed that this masked figure possessed extraordinary skills, having pierced through the distance, an impressive feat.  

The unusual ability to recover from injuries at a remarkable speed caught his eye.  

Yet…  

“Impressive, given your age…”  

However, he quickly decided that the wielder of that high voice could not have been so simplistic.  

“You weren’t the one who gauged my strength in hiding, were you?”  

Was it merely a figment of his imagination? As Harmon glared at the masked figure with subtle hostility, the figure responded.  

“Please, just wait a moment!”  

Simultaneously, the space behind the masked figure warped, and the aura of holiness began to radiate from within.  

This was a unique feeling of divine arts—sacred arts.  

It seemed that this masked individual had been injured while protecting his barrier from Harmon’s strike.  

In that moment, this intuition proved correct as a woman walked out from the holy barrier.  

“It is a pleasure to finally meet you, Commander Harmon.”  

The Saint.  

At her unexpected appearance, Harmon’s eyes widened in surprise.



-chapter 350-

Kwak kwak kwak kwak.

Head, heart, groin, and limbs.

An attack that seemed to target seven areas of the body simultaneously, Vortex.

It was the name given to Greet Ainshein, the knight of slaughter, and the name of his signature skill, often referred to as the “Demon’s Spear.” Its notorious reputation was such that if even a single strike was not blocked, one would die, or at the very least, the subsequent attacks would leave not even a corpse behind.

However, the number of blocks Logan needed to perform was quite simple.

Rumbling.

From the holy sword he swung, an enormous sword emerged like a pillar, exhibiting the might of a giant.

The brilliant shining silver pillar bore hints of ‘yellow light,’ but the only aura user capable of recognizing it was focused solely on blocking the attack.

Kawaaaaaang!

The clash of the giant’s sword and the seven Aura spheres produced an explosive sound that shook the stone chamber.

“Cough!”

“Ugh!”

Both parties were sent reeling backward, and the knights of the First Legion, who had charged at Logan just moments before, lost their balance and tumbled from the shockwave.

It was then that the mad expressions on the faces of the fallen knights began to fade.

“What!? Why?”

The bewildered knights turned their attention to a single direction.

It was to the mages they had considered allies.

Yet, they were huddled together in one place, having stopped casting spells altogether.

In the instant the knights’ faces went blank with confusion, a chilling gray magic energy soared from where they had gathered.

That sight sent shivers down the spines of the knights, who had already been toyed with once before. But the main participants of the earlier clash had no time to concern themselves with the mages.

Once again, it was Greet who regained his composure first.

“Not bad!”

An expression of surprise appeared on Greet’s face, which had been twisted in fury. He wasted no time and charged forward once more.

Conversely, Gile and Logan had to pause to seal away the power they had just released.

‘Tsk.’

Although he wanted to avoid risking exposure, Greet Ainshein was no opponent to face in his diminished state.

A strongman who looked beyond the upper ranks. He needed to match his assaults adequately.

‘Getting a huge catch like this poses a problem.’

As Logan frowned and prepared to wield his sword again.

“Power Word! Obey!”

From behind the slightly retreating mages, a bizarre shout that echoed in every direction rang out.

Turning his gaze slightly, he noticed a gray five-pointed star drawn beneath the feet of the lined-up mages. And astonishingly, there was a truly immense amount of magic energy surging forth from that spot.

Before Logan could understand and respond, the rising magic formed into a massive gray lightning bolt that shot toward him.

Flash.

The magic was so overwhelming that even Greet, who had been charging, tensed and assumed a defensive position.

As the power rushed toward Logan, a thunderous voice reverberated in his mind.

– Obey!!

Zziiing.

An enormous noise that distorted his sense of hearing and made him lose balance rang out, akin to being attacked by a powerful sonic wave.

But in that very moment.

“Stop, Count Greet! He’s been subdued by us!”

Greet, who was about to take a combat stance again, heard the confident voices from the mages.

‘Hm?’

Greet’s body halted once more, but Logan did not move, fully taking in the fleeting opportunity.

‘Could it be…’

The massive gray magic energy swirling within him tried to penetrate his mind but was frustratingly countered by the Force.

Even though he still did not understand what the origin power referred to by Zibrick Castle meant, witnessing that lower energy crushing his magic effortlessly made him realize that his strength stood in direct opposition to theirs.

However, Logan did not fully crush that magic and opted to observe instead.

“What do you mean, Gareth?” Greet questioned, while keeping a wary eye on Gile. Noting that he wasn’t moving at all, he shot a fiery glare at the mages.

There were not two but five mages present.

Which meant that at least three of them had powers capable of deceiving even his senses; opposing them now would yield nothing but losses.

Regardless, Greet could not lower his head before them completely, stung as he was by humiliation from his subordinates’ folly and his own pride.

But Gareth seemed unconcerned with those feelings, responding with a smile.

“This means that the author currently cannot resist our words.”

“What nonsensical talk is this?”

To Greet’s standards, that was utter nonsense.

The surviving knights of his legion wore equal expressions of confusion.

“I will show you proof.”

With a confident smile, Gareth turned his head to the back, at which an old mage nodded with a chilling laugh.

Then the bone-chilling voice resonated.

– Cut off your left arm.

Immediately, Gile raised his sword.

Swaaaak!

“What!?”

Without hesitation, Gile swung his sword, causing clear red blood to squirt from his left arm.

However, it did not sever completely as per the mage’s command. Blood dripped from the cut surface left behind by the slash.

“…Gah.”

Gile, his eyes reddened with rage, gripped his right hand tightly with his left.

Amidst the bizarre sight, the knights, including Greet, cringed, yet the mages were astonished, perhaps a bit impressed.

The burning silver aura emanating from the sword felt different to them.

– Enough. Await further orders!

A voice with an eerie resonance followed, causing Gile, who was groaning in pain, to straighten up and thrust his sword into the ground.

Thud.

Kneeling on one knee with his sword plunged into the stone floor, it was apparent to anyone that his face, flushed with blood and veins bulging, was not an indication of his will.

Yet his body no longer moved.

“The resistance of the holy sword is impressive…”

“Quite remarkable. To withstand such a powerful spell while consuming five Blood Crystals…”

“Indeed… it was a wise decision to come here.”

The mages whispered amongst themselves.

Most of their words were unintelligible, yet one thing was undeniable: this strange group had completely subjugated their objective.

But Greet felt a lingering unease over this ridiculous conclusion.

A knight who used to contend with him had been turned into a mere puppet in an instant.

Feeling a strong unpleasantness beyond mere resentment toward the enemy, he could hardly tolerate such magic.

And to suppress that discomfort, Greet’s foot instinctively moved towards Gile.

“Then let me take care of the ending.”

However, an unexpected obstruction occurred.

“Please wait, Count. It’s better to use a subdued enemy as a tool, don’t you think?”

Greet’s eyes narrowed at the voice blocking his path.

“Is it meaningful to leave that author alive?”

“To seek the treasures of the ruins. You wouldn’t assume that sword is everything, would you?”

At those words, Greet’s expression hardened.

“Moreover, the power of a superhuman is precious for the Empire, is it not?”

“What does bringing Liberty’s superhuman to the Empire even mean?”

Gareth smiled sardonic.

“Of course, we have our methods. And to be quite frank, given the resources we’ve invested thus far, we must take him alive at minimum to count it as a return on investment.”

Return on investment?

‘A superhuman knight being equivalent to some unknown resource?’

Greet’s face grew even more rigid.

Yet Gareth continued, seemingly unperturbed by Greet’s discomfort.

“You must understand. His existence has already been acknowledged by the Emperor.”

“How dare you speak so arrogantly!” 

Killing intent inherently surfaced in Greet’s voice.

With reference to his liege and the world’s ruler simply called ‘the Emperor’?

Instinctively, Greet’s body reacted as he brandished his spear toward Gareth’s throat.

“Ah, my apologies. I meant to say, with the Emperor’s permission.”

Cluck cluck.

Gareth’s expression, as he clicked his tongue while looking at Greet, bore no hints of regret.

However, Greet opted to step back.

“Watch your words, mage.”

His uneasiness surged at not even wanting to refer to Gareth by name.

“Haha. Naturally.”

Gareth merely smiled, as though he understood Greet’s resentment.

That loathsome expression prompted Greet to turn away.

‘For now, our objective is accomplished.’

The foe who had disrespected the Emperor had been thoroughly subdued.

Although these knights were now puppets, and the strange mages applied sorcery, they were undeniably allies for now, so there was no need to engage with them immediately.

‘It is not a retreat born of lacking strength.’

Greet reassured himself, grimacing in a plot of annoyance aimed at his own self.

Then he strode forward to approach the kneeling enemy.

“In any case, this sword possesses the treasures of the ruins, correct?”

“Indeed. He probably could’ve fought evenly against our forces thanks to that treasure.”

At Gareth’s words, Greet cocked his head in confusion.

From their exchanges, it felt as though Gile’s power was no measure of mere reliance on artifacts. The force he demonstrated would surpass that which could be replicated even with a class-six artifact of ancient origin.

Yet if that were indeed true.

‘It would be a treasure fit for offering to the Emperor.’

That thought momentarily placated his troubled mind.

However, the moment he stood before the kneeling enemy.

“Invisible Hold.”

“Terror Blind.”

“Mind Breaker.”

– Kyaaaah!

Accompanied by the morbid chorus of incantations, his body froze, and his vision turned dark, revealing all kinds of specters rushing towards him in a fantasy.

‘What!’

A sudden upheaval.

But Logan’s strong will and Force instinctively severed the magic that tried to probe his mind.

He was relieved to have been on guard and had raised the force, anticipating an unexpected movement from the subdued enemy.

However, just a few seconds of hesitation turned into calamity for him.

Fwoook.

“Kugh, ugh!”

The greatsword held in the kneeling enemy pierced through his chest.

“Commander!”

“Sir!”

– Stop that motion!

As the underlings screamed and surged forward, the old mage’s voice made them all freeze like puppets.

“You simply need to scrub away the memory.”

“A mere knight…”

“Without alerting the Emperor…”

“Of course…”

The eerie whispers of the mages reached Greet’s fading consciousness, and through his blurry vision, he saw the vacant-eyed figures of his subordinates staring at him.

‘Ah, no.’

An unbearable sight.

Taking in the dire reality, Greet’s eyes widened furiously.

He longed to leap up and strike the mages obscuring his path, but his critically wounded body refused to comply.

“Ugh… ugh…”

Lingering remorse, bitter regrets, all boiled within him but only emerged as incomprehensible groans, as a soft voice reached his ears.

“Farewell.”

The last flicker of consciousness as he locked eyes with the gaze.

Strangely sharp brown eyes appeared—too vivid for the gaze of someone deemed an enemy.

Greet couldn’t help but to chuckle grimly, envisioning the demise of those who had amassed this fate upon him.

‘…Bastards.’

Thud.

The spear of Greet Ainshein fell coldly onto the stone floor, but no mages mourned him.

– Come here.

“You’ve done well. Gile… was it?”

“What need is there for a name in the making of combat puppets?”

“Even so, it’s still appropriate to have some identifier.”

“But we have diligently retrieved the relic of the founding.”

“A marker is still needed for combat puppets.”

Only those who reveled in the successful return of matters floated through.

Yet, perhaps due to not yet being fully subdued, some of the knights stripped of their awareness stood, faces flushed like logs.

“This is the holy sword…”

“But why does it seem so less responsive?”

“It’s probably an illusion.”

– Hand over the holy sword.

As the heavy voice resonated, Gile stepped forward, targeting the mages.

But even at that moment, the mages merely looked at him with smiles plastered on their faces.

“Oh dear, did I pour in too much magic?”

“Indeed, one could argue that his intelligence is lacking.”

“Perhaps instruct him to offer the handle again?”

“Wait a second. Just a bit…”

Flash.

Swaaaak!

The moment Gareth felt something strange, the beam of light erupting from the greatsword drew a massive arc in the air.

Crimson rings cleanly severed the necks and upper bodies of the mages.

“Guh, kuh!”

“Gah, grk!”

“How…!”

As the fallen mages looked at Gile with disbelief, there was a slight smirk from Gile’s lips.

“It’s past time to stop pretending.”

With the mages departing into unconsciousness, Gile, feeling the surge of power, let out a ferocious howl.

“Ahhhh!”

Then he unleashed a torrent of silver-streaked storms from the greatsword.

Kwak kwak kwak kwak.

As the maelstrom of insecure power bearing life gripped the bodies of the mages crushed to pieces, he soon began to roar as though beset with madness.

“Uooooooh!”

Like a beast, he bolted forth beyond the stone chamber, wildly raging outside the castle.

They could hardly imagine experiencing a chain of such surreal upheavals in the practice grounds of the palace.

“What in the world…!”

“Commander!!”

“Damn it!”

“The mages are making mischief!”

Only a handful of knights from the First Legion remained at the site, feeling as though they had just broken free from the mages’ spell.



-chapter 348-

“Welcome. His Majesty, Kran III of the homeland, is waiting for you.”

Jordan Malins, the Marquess and Prime Minister of the Liberty Kingdom, bowed courteously. However, the man with a cold demeanor merely nodded in response.

Despite this rude attitude, there was no sign of displeasure on Jordan’s face. On the contrary, he glanced nervously at the group with beads of sweat pouring down his bald head.

‘No matter what, for the Empire’s superhuman to come in person, what in the world has that man done?’

Jordan’s gaze lingered on the face of the man standing at the forefront of the Empire’s secret envoy. 

With his snow-white skin and expressionless face, his neatly combed back white hair conveyed an even colder impression. The sharpness of his eyes further emphasized his icy demeanor, and locking eyes with him sent a shiver down one’s spine.

Sixty-three years old. Commander of the Eastern First Legion of the Empire, Grit Ainshein.

One of the Empire’s superhumans had come to Liberty, not officially, but as an unofficial envoy.

Jordan wiped away the cold sweat that was trickling down his forehead and opened his mouth again.

“Haha. I have heard of the infamous Devil Spear. It is an honor to meet you.”

“Guide.”

However, the only response was a cold single word.

Jordan hastily bowed his head to conceal his stiffening expression.

“…Yes. Of course, I will guide you. Please follow me.”

Even though he was a superhuman of the Empire, seeing him show no respect to a noble of a foreign country filled Jordan with resentment.

‘What an arrogant person. Surely, he wouldn’t be this disrespectful to His Majesty, right?’

It was fortunate that this visit was unofficial. There likely wouldn’t be many witnesses to this disgraceful spectacle.

‘Damn it. What exactly has Gile done…’

Unable to voice his complaints to the envoy, his unpleasant feelings merely translated into bitterness against Gile Slayer.

And that displeasure intensified further with Grit’s unchanging demeanor as they arrived in front of the king’s office.

As a secret envoy, he couldn’t meet the king while surrounded by ministers in the grand hall. However, to maintain the king’s dignity, he arranged for knights to be posted outside the office where they would face each other.

But the moment one of the knights shouted, “A precious guest has arrived!”

Bam!

The red aura extended from Grit’s casual hand gesture, violently flinging open the doors of the grand hall.

The expressions of all the Liberty officials who witnessed it froze, while Kran III’s brows furrowed as he glared at him from behind the opened doors.

But Grit maintained his impassive expression, turning his attention to the five people who followed him.

“You shall wait outside.”

“…Understood, Your Excellency.”

Jordan found Grit’s gaze towards his entourage strange.

Despite being in the royal palace of Liberty, the palace officials showed no concern with him. Instead, they seemed to be on guard against the others, those cloaked individuals who came with Grit.

‘It must be a misunderstanding.’

He must have tried to think of something else to endure the menacing atmosphere.

Jordan blamed himself for his own discomfort, quickly catching up with Grit as he stepped into the office.

“Count Grit Ainshein of the Empire wishes to meet the lord of Liberty.”

Grit’s bow was excessively brief, only slightly lowering his head while placing a fist on his chest.

The expressions of Gunter Liberty and the escort knights standing behind the king became noticeably rigid, but Kran III nodded with a neutral expression.

“…You have traveled a long way, Count. It would have been better if we met on good terms, but I understand that you have prepared an excess of personnel, given the circumstances.”

Though he spoke of shortcomings, his tone maintained proper etiquette. Kran III’s words could not be faulted, except for the fact that he had brought an abundance of elite knights, including Gunter Liberty, into the office for what was supposed to be a secret meeting.

A faint smile flickered on Grit’s previously impassive face.

“That is of no concern.”

He briefly raised one corner of his lips before returning to his blank expression.

At this, Kran III and the faces of those from Liberty grew hard.

The name of the Eastern First Legion Commander was unmistakably well-known even in the Empire.

However, under the guise of an envoy, the weapon known as the Devil Spear that he had brought along had already been left outside the palace. No matter how skilled Gunter Liberty and his twenty elite knights were, it would be impossible to handle Grit barehanded, no matter how much they tried.

As these thoughts crossed Kran III’s mind, he bit down on his lip.

‘He must realize it too.’

In truth, it was the current disparity between Liberty and the Empire that compelled him to tolerate much of the rudeness and oppression.

He pushed aside his discomfort with a brief cough to maintain a composed demeanor.

“Hmm… In that case, very well. I do know of the contents that have been relayed, but I would prefer to hear the matter formally through the envoy.”

“It concerns a man by the name of Gile Slayer and the treasure he took from the Empire’s territories…”

The essence of his words was exactly as expected.

However, the frigid tone in which Grit replied suggested that the honorifics added a slight pause that made it difficult to discern whether it was a mistake or intentional.

Kran III’s face hardened even further.

“…Gile Slayer is a war hero of ours, and within our kingdom, he is granted boundless freedom in his conduct. Therefore, all I can do is provide an avenue for him to resolve this.”

Grit’s expression shifted slightly upon hearing Kran III’s response.

“…Are you saying that it would not matter what conclusion arises from this matter?”

“Responsibility accompanies authority, so I believe Duke Gile will handle this appropriately.”

As Grit listened to Kran III’s response, his brows narrowed in confusion. It was a statement he could hardly make sense of.

“Your Majesty, do you truly comprehend what I am asserting?”

“…I have not said otherwise.”

Despite Grit’s rude rebuttal, Kran III simply nodded solemnly.

This left Grit momentarily speechless.

Wasn’t this equivalent to expressing the intent to cast aside the life of one of the Empire’s superhumans?

This was a move he had never anticipated.

– Retrieving the treasure yet emphasizing the submission of Liberty is of paramount importance.

The Emperor’s voice echoed in his mind repeatedly.

The original plan had been disturbingly straightforward.

After robust negotiations while maintaining a strong stance, they would offer Gile’s life in exchange for liberty’s surrender, backed by the treasures from the ruins and one or two national treasures of Liberty. 

This aim had seemed so certain until now, yet the path ahead suddenly felt obstructed from the outset.

‘Perhaps I have pressed too hard.’

That thought crept in briefly, but Grit quickly steeled himself.

‘No, it doesn’t matter even slightly. Showing the Empire’s might is far more crucial.’

Although he had received the Crown Prince’s request, he had not been entirely excited about it.

Claiming the lives of a hundred or so of his loyal subordinates, including Yassel and the elite knights, seemed excessive for merely the subjugation of a small nation.

Thus.

“The punishment regarding him lies in my hands. I shall now convey the demands that our Empire wishes to outline upon your return.”

If he were to respond unexpectedly, it would necessitate adding unforeseen demands.

Grit’s words made Kran III’s expression stiffen.

“What does that mean?”

“Should he bear the responsibility for his actions, it is only right that the Duke’s rudeness against the Empire be compensated by the royal family of Liberty.”

The arrogance displayed was one far too presumptuous.

The response came from behind the king, erupting with an explosive bang.

“Isn’t this excessive, Count Grit!”

The very marble beneath their feet cracked, accompanied by the formidable pressure that surged through Grit’s entire body.

However, the pressure meant to intimidate failed to make a proper approach and merely whisked past Grit like a spring breeze.

A hint of a mocking smile graced Grit’s lips, while Gunter Liberty’s face grew even more rigid.

“…What more do you desire?”

The king raised his hand, halting his younger brother’s outburst.

“In exchange for vowing that the kingdom of Liberty shall serve the Empire as its suzerain, I would also like to require a hostage or proof to substantiate it, Your Majesty.”

Excessive. 

Far too excessive.

This sounded like the intention to consume an entire nation now that a reason had fallen into their hands.

Naturally, Kran III’s displeasure leaked out through his voice.

“What if I cannot agree?”

“You would then have to bear the Emperor’s wrath.”

A look of disdain veiled Kran III’s expression, hinting at the thought that Grit had dared utter threats.

Yet, such words left those present dumbfounded.

For the Kingdom of Liberty, which shared no borders with the Empire, the Emperor’s might felt as distant as the winds of another land.

This left Grit’s earlier demand echoing as mere nonsense to some of the escort knights.

Yet, Kran III, who understood the Empire’s might better than all of them, could not let it pass lightly.

However, at that moment.

– The Empire is poised to utilize this incident to fully subjugate the Liberty Kingdom. Correct? Ah, while I do apologize for Gile’s actions, one must understand that…

– …These kinds of opportunities could always be seized by the Empire, regardless of the present situation. Evidence? You shall find it if you experience it yourself.

Hearing the words from McLain, who could be blamed for all this, even as they rang through his mind, Grit’s expression suddenly became visible again.

Entrusting the disposition of Duke Gile entirely to him indicated an act of total submission toward the Empire.

‘Yet it seems he will proceed this boldly?’

Now he realized McLain’s words weren’t false.

‘However…’

In the end, this moment formed a diverging path.

The Empire of McLain.

Given their domestic powers, they ought to back the Empire, yet the distant threat posed by the Dragon might render them unable to withstand a domestic situation.

Liberty, meanwhile, lacked the strength to withstand even the claws of a dragon, with the hostages already in Grang.

‘It’s entirely our kingdom’s lack of strength that has brought this upon us…’

Beneath the desk, Viktor’s fists clenched tightly, unintentionally.

Truly lamentable.

However, despite his deep convictions, he found that he was confronted with no choices.

Unlike the Empire, which still viewed Gile as a Liberty man, McLain had anticipated the Empire’s response and provided countermeasures. 

“…All matters can wait until after we deal with Duke Gile Slayer.”

Those words seemed unforeseen.

“…You mean the war hero? It seems that he holds greater influence than you.”

Grit spoke with a calm tone. Such a statement could be interpreted as ridiculing the king’s authority. 

The response that followed shocked everyone.

“Indeed, that is accurate.”

Not Gile, but rather, it was McLain who now handled Kran III’s unspoken intentions underneath the facade of a king.

The genuine feeling untouched by others shocked both Grit and the deputies.

“Your Majesty!?”

“What does this mean…?” 

Witnessing the shock of those around him, Grit’s expression finally cracked.

“No king has ever confessed such things; however, upon witnessing their incompetence in posterity, I dare to presume you now realize such matters.”

‘Nothing could be more ridiculous.’

Witnessing the embarrassing nature of such a proclamation sent chilling waves throughout the crowd. 

However, an unexpected declaration echoed soon after.

“Thus, should our interactions with Duke Gile proceed according to your plans, I shall comply with the Empire’s demands. Yet, if you fail to subdue Duke Gile, I would like to request you leave immediately without fulfilling any requirements.”

Unable to accept the unexpected turn of events, Grit’s face turned grim, leaving his mouth agape.

‘Does he intend to sacrifice the life of one of our superhumans?’

This was a move he had never expected.

‘Moreover, should we report it in such a manner?!’

There was a flaw in Kran III’s sudden actions.

He could never disregard the life of one of the superhumans who belonged to his side.

However, if they reported it to the top, there would have to be consequences.

“What can we truly expect from this entire situation?” With this sudden declaration, the atmosphere in the room tightened drastically.

A clarion call sounded for chaos to be unleashed within the current state of affairs.

“Failure?”  

The cold anger expressed in the calm voice penetrated the air.

“There was an obstruction. A superhuman using silver aura appeared and massacred the commander of the Eastern 1st Legion, Yassel Friedman, along with a hundred knights, and killed the mage sent by the Dongwangbu.”  

At those words, Clid forcibly suppressed the boiling anger within and considered the worst possibilities.  

“…Is there a chance this is a scheme of the Dongwangbu?”

There were officially 32 superhumans in the empire, but with one recently deceased, that number was now 31.

In regional warfare, they served as tactical weapons that could change the tide, and in national wars, they could strike at the enemy’s core in a single blow. Their value was immeasurable, to the point that among the small nations on the continent, there were many that had no superhumans at all.

It wouldn’t be surprising for the Emperor to take an interest.

With that alone, Clid’s fury subsided as if it were a lie.

That alone made no sense.  

*In the worst-case scenario, it means Father fell for their tricks.*  

That couldn’t be possible.

That certainly did not bode well for him, for even if everything balanced out now, it meant his rival had gained an incredible trump card that he did not possess.  

*It’s quite likely that the Emperor has restricted movements to verify whether they truly surrendered.*  

Clid’s theory drew nearer to the truth. And that thought instilled a sense of impatience within him.  

His rival had unexpectedly gained a powerful force.  

A force that had once cornered the imperial throne itself.  

Moreover, he was now unaware of significant tasks assigned to him.  

*I can’t relax just because I’m slightly ahead right now. No, the current situation itself is perilous.*

*There must be information that shouldn’t be known to me.*

-chapter 360-

Luisa still remembered that day.  

No, she couldn’t forget it.  

Twenty-four years ago, the saddest day of her life.  

“Luisa, don’t forget your mother.”  

A wistful face with tears streaming down, looking at her with a haggard expression.  

Mom.  

The queen was being dragged away by those who didn’t even know who her wife was,  

but her father, in his facade of a good king, could not stop them.  

“You must forget, Luisa.”  

He merely embraced her while saying different words from her mother.  

The young Luisa had no idea what was happening.  

She simply cried and threw a tantrum at the thought of never being able to see her mother again.  

Her father, having gone to the palace, returned much later.  

And that night, as she searched for her mother, he held Luisa tightly, sobbing the whole night.  

“I’m sorry, Luisa. I’m so sorry… Father truly is sorry…”  

After that day, the Eastern Wheel King of the Empire neglected state affairs and drowned himself in alcohol.  

It was a reality that was hard for the young Luisa to bear.  

Her warm mother had disappeared, and her once-affectionate father no longer regarded her.  

From then on, Luisa became a troublemaker wandering the palace, while her once-perfect family fell apart.  

Then one day, amidst the days that felt fragile like thin ice, change occurred.  

“How much you must be suffering.”  

An elderly man with a warm presence—a jester called to amuse the sorrowful king by an overly loyal minister.  

However, the old jester showed them a miracle.  

“A chance will come to straighten everything that has been twisted.”  

He extended his hand toward them, the great magician thought to be nonexistent in this era.  

“The time of prophecy will come soon. When our wishes are fulfilled, the imperial family and the emperor will pay the price.”  

“And on the day He descends…”  

At that time, Luisa had no idea what his words meant, but she clearly remembered how her father wore a look of ecstasy for the first time in ages.  

From that moment on, her father stopped drinking and began to smile actively while engaging in external activities,  

and the mischievous young princess began to receive training from that magician, supposedly due to her talent in magic.  

Time passed, and when Luisa finally grew curious about the past,  

her master revealed the truth of that day.  

“The queen… your mother.”  

She was accused of crimes she never committed on the orders of the current emperor, who sought to secure the crown prince’s position, and was taken away to the gallows at dawn.  

But the only “crime” of her mother was being born from the same womb as another prince who was a rival to the emperor.  

That single factor altered the fate of the father and daughter.  

Additionally, her master shared a shocking revelation that Luisa could never have imagined.  

“Your father, the Eastern Wheel King, executed his own wife.”  

For the sake of proving loyalty to the crown prince, or so it was said.
