But she soon recalled her father’s figure welcoming the imperial messenger on the fateful day.  

“How could he hesitate for an act to slay a traitor?”  

At the time, she didn’t understand, but the memories of that day were still vivid.  

And now she understood the meaning behind those words.  

The tenuous father-daughter relationship finally shattered that day.  

“Why! Why did you do it? Why!”  

Her outcry, filled with madness, met her father’s unyielding gaze, which held no smile at that moment.  

After a considerable passage of time, her father’s heavy voice finally broke the silence.  

“It was… your mother’s wish. For you and our family…”  

“Don’t be ridiculous!”  

That claim could not persuade Luisa.  

By then, she already knew.  

The couple loved each other dearly, and the fruits of that love—their daughter—were cherished deeply.  

Had her father not done that, the master of the Eastern Wheel would have changed immediately.  

But while she could understand this intellectually, her heart could not accept it.  

Ultimately, Luisa spat out words that drove a stake deep into everyone’s hearts.  

“You abandoned mother to save yourselves!”  

Since then, the father and daughter had not engaged in meaningful conversation, aside from matters of duty.  

So much time passed.  

The Eastern Wheel King became known as the ruthless husband and treacherous royal,  

and the princess, the unknown sorceress who mastered ancient magic,

only after a long while did the time of prophecy finally approach.  

Signs of the gods leaving this era appeared, and the power of those who would change their destiny was confirmed.  

However…  

“The royal family has drawn swords. All elders, prepare to retreat.”  

Were they telling her to hold her breath and wait for the occasion once more?  

‘No way!’  

The pent-up anger that had festered since that day was now being unleashed, refusing to step back from the stage of learning.  

So, Luisa smiled.  

Like her father, who now felt very distant.  

With an expression devoid of any feelings.  

“Haha. Count, I find it odd for you to be surprised. It seems you’ve forgotten why I came here.”  

“Ah, this is quite perplexing. It seems quite different from what you said recently.”  

Well, the situation did change.  

Even as she looked into his sharply transformed red eyes, Luisa smiled again.  

“Haven’t you heard the saying that a woman’s heart is as fickle as reeds? It seems I’ve taken quite a liking to you as we talked.”  

“Did our conversation possess any romantic elements? You make quite the frightening statement.”  

Despite Luisa’s enchanting smile, Ronian only displayed wariness.  

To Luisa, the sight of a young man showing such a reaction felt refreshingly new.  

“It is terrible to imagine hosting someone who committed an assault on the royal palace.”  

The role-play of lovers and the red-haired youth, who was essentially her guard, now bluntly expressed that thought.  

A chuckle escaped her lips.  

‘Well, that’s understandable from their perspective.’  

While their beginning had gone very wrong, in a marriage of their status, emotions hardly mattered.  

“Wouldn’t it be beneficial for the kingdom?”  

“Pardon?”  

Ronian asked back in disbelief, but Luisa continued in a calm voice.  

“You’re preparing for war against the empire. I believe we’ve gone to great lengths to calm the fortress.  

If our marriage is achieved, who knows? Perhaps within the empire, they may respond if war breaks out.”  

“Hahaha! What absurd claims…”  

Indeed. If they did not understand their situation, that would be a normal reaction.  

And in truth, it was an unrealistic exaggeration.  

‘If the forces of the Eastern Wheel were commanded to threaten the royal family, they would instead aim for my father.’  

That was merely a predetermined structured system, tied to the very foundation upon which the Eastern Wheel was established when alliances formed.  

One deeply guarded secret of the empire, impossible for outsiders to perceive.  

Especially in wartime, disobeying orders would be utterly unthinkable.  

Thus, the father-daughter duo had turned their gaze away from the outside world.  

Yet Luisa was unwilling to retreat.  

‘This kingdom will withstand the empire’s offensive. Unlike what is publicly known.’  

She had keenly sensed that truth while residing in the royal palace.  

Simply observing the young count before her and his renowned friend, not to mention the servants rigorously trained within a week, had clarified everything.  

The power to change destiny… a King would not personally unravel the enslavement of mere servants. And if he did, he would have warned her beforehand.  

That implied  

‘He possesses magical powers beyond my comprehension.’  

Of course, she didn’t imagine this meant they could win against the empire.  

As a member of the Cassel Tower, she had learned about the empire’s hidden power through its infighting.  

It was considerably greater than she had surmised.  

But if the tower’s hopes were to be realized, it would serve best if the war escalated.  

Thus, the kingdom’s resistance was all the more welcomed.  

If the one who changes their destiny can be made to form alliances amidst despair, nothing could be better.  

‘After all, the king is unlikely to believe me, much less trust us.’  

That had become a fate the wizard could carry, someone who held power over the human soul but had already committed misdeeds.  

Thus gaining the trust of such individuals would be nigh impossible.  

Ultimately, Luisa must emphasize that she, the Eastern Wheel, could prove beneficial to the kingdom.  

“I understand your distrust. So, let’s make a deal.”  

“A deal?”  

With that ambiguous expression still on his face, Luisa reluctantly showed her hand first.  

“How about we share complete honesty regarding what we know? The kingdom stands against the empire, and the empire readies for war. This is a fact already known to the heads of both states.  

While the empire may disregard the kingdom, they will reconsider if I marry.”  

“Ha ha, it’s quite nonsensical to propose half-baked reasoning…”  

Certainly, lacking insight into their conditions made it a normal response.  

Yet her logic did hold merit.  

“Okay?”  

“I will let you grasp the intelligence of the empire’s military from the Eastern Wheel. In return, there’s nothing more that will suffice as a bridal gift?”  

Seeing the red-eyed youth’s excitement brighten at her statement, Luisa couldn’t help but smile.  

‘This kingdom aims to compel the empire, pouring its blood to the brink of flowing over and overwhelming it. Then that itself would become the sacrifice…’  

That picture of her great master, the tower’s leader, lingered faintly in her mind.  

“And if that’s the case, I shall try not to oppose. To prove everyone wrong.”  

“Really? Then I’m glad you understand, Count.”  

Luisa’s heart warmed, a sense of satisfaction washing over her. 

But if he truly understood the implications of her words, they would surely find their path blocked.  

“One thing to be warned of,” she smiled.  

The topics of discussion vanished mysteriously amongst her expressions.  

Pointing out those tattered remnants of the past, she beckoned Ronian, who reluctantly tilted his head with uncertainty.  

“I’d rather be married than give up a mediocre present.”  

“No, I’m certain you will soon want to restrain me.”  

Luisa dismissed his gentle jest, and her features hardened significantly.  

When it came to shaming her agreement, Luisa had little patience for those who betrayed trust.  

“Who are you—”  

Luisa interrupted, biting off a bitter joke that she would soon regret, “Fine, my life is already at stake.”  

“That’s not easy.”  

Glancing at him with defiance, she resisted the impulse to reject him and quickly declared, “How rude!”  

“You should know.”  

At that, the playful tension gave way, and Ronian regarded her comfortably.  

So simple was the flicker of excitement, hidden beneath, and a color of hope glinted in the young Count’s eyes amidst his dark mane.  

Then, as if waking from the depths of a dream, peace filled the air.  

Yet simultaneously, either delving into expectations or reality would swiftly follow.  

“Listen closely; I’ll agree, but you need to heed my words as well.”  

Luisa’s tone thickened again, a resolve resting painfully across their desires.  

With the shadows flickering, everything hung by the weight of one truth lingering in the air—the very fabric of fate.  

In that moment, without so much as a hint of what lay to come, their futures merged and transformed, intertwining fates awaited unfolding plots.

Despite enduring the absurdity of experiences with the Divine Sword Harman Killer Blue, having just ultimately dashed towards the castle under extreme measures, he had finally breached the intermediate wall.  

Yet now, facing the clash of battling powers, the learning curve was tremendously steep.  

But Ronnian’s eyes narrowed in focus once more.  

“Dear brother! You must be cautious!”

Seven swords burst into existence from the orange aura bursting forth as seven dazzling lights shot forth like beams from each sword’s tip.

This ominous wavelength could splatter even the same aura to pieces.

Life Sword Vision 5th Level, Life Cleave (生靈斬). He could wield this technique, yet never had he thought of Ronnian utilizing it in this fashion.

Though easily stated, that accomplishment was far from simple.  

The sword techniques required concentrating one’s soul into each strike. Dividing it forcibly into seven would mean the power would dwindle, and becoming internal injuries was almost guaranteed.

Logan spoke nonchalantly, reproaching his younger brother with ease.

Ronnian’s trait of Seven Souls.

With Ronnian growing weaker, Viktor felt bolstered hearing those words filled with true belief.  

“You will find your place!”  

Thus, he steeled himself, anew, clenching a firm grip on his sword.  

He would not be dethroned this time.  

If there was an opportunity to shine, it lay in this bout of skills and his uninterrupted stamina; he had the advantage of possessing fortitude and endurance over a teammate to not give in.  

Never falling short!  

A surge of gray aura erupted, electrifying each fiber of his being.  

Thus, Viktor rampaged forth, charging straight at Logan, who stood before his teacher.  

What was just another day, now flickered as another battle began.

“Cough. Cough.”  

“Well fought!”

But with Viktor’s recuperative powers and fortitude, catching up should not take long.  

As for Ronnian—the one truly lagging behind, he would have weak hopes for a brotherly catch-up.  

With every rising star hopeful, seasons change with new beginnings; it had struck Logan that the countdown toward war had kicked off.  

“In war, preparation is key.”  

So, he focused on his own record, steadying his powers and honing the skills of those still able to grow without restriction.  

The likes of his teachers, Luther, and Wicken, already seemed at their limits.  

Everything rested solely with these two.  

At present, this was an amiable choice indeed.

Working towards attaining the highest realm of aura users, he envisioned the pinnacle—charting out his next course of action.  

Though the ultimate barrier still lay daunting before him.

**’Monster…’**

Viktor gripped his trembling hands and glared at Harmon.  

The physical shock had already subsided, but the mental shock was something he couldn’t shake off immediately.  

The sight of him slashing away, uprooting everything within a hundred meters, was terrifying enough. He had stepped forward just to prevent the shockwave from disrupting the barrier. In other words, he had only blocked the incoming shockwaves, yet it felt as if the entire space had compressed and struck him back with tremendous force.  

‘Is this not a matter of me being unable to endure the aftermath instead of merely an attack?’  

How could a human exhibit such strength?  

He had never even imagined it.  

Thus, Viktor was certain.  

‘If that being wished to harm the Saint, I wouldn’t be able to stop it.’  

– If the Divine Sword seeks to capture the Saint, do not resist and let it pass.

He also understood the meaning behind his lord’s command.  

The Divine Sword. The name resonated with immense presence in his heart as if it had suddenly become new.  

Overwhelmed by that shock, Viktor could not prevent Ilia from approaching Harmon.  

“I, Ilia!”  

He recognized it late and shouted out.  

“It’s fine. Please step back.”  

The one he needed to protect was instead smiling gently at him, reassuring him.  

Feeling powerless in that moment, Viktor gritted his teeth and followed right behind her.  

“…Grand Commander of the Holy Knights, Harmon greets the Saint.”  

At least it was fortunate that the Divine Sword’s attitude toward her was respectful.  

Viktor had no choice but to look at the monster in human form with a complex expression.  

“I am aware that you have been formally announced as an enemy. Yet, why such excessive courtesy?”  

“If you have ever met the Saint, you would surmise that something must have gone wrong.”  

Ilia felt a sense of relief at Harmon’s words, which were famous for their strictness. The worst-case scenario she had dreaded did not seem to be occurring.  

“Then, did you come to see me?”  

“Yes.”  

“How could you be here…?”  

“I had people helping me.”  

Ilia turned to look behind her, but she couldn’t bring herself to trust Harmon, who was wearing a mask.  

“…You are quite skilled; and what place do you come from?”  

“I’m sorry, but I cannot reveal that yet.”  

At her refusal, Harmon’s eyebrows twitched slightly.  

“I apologize, but if this is merely about internal politics within the Holy Order and the Saint has brought foreign influence into it, then I must follow the Order’s orders.”  

He reached once more for the hilt of his sword.  

That single motion engulfed the surroundings in an oppressive atmosphere once more.  

It was not merely a feeling. In an instant, the dust within a ten-meter radius was violently pushed away, placing Viktor right in the center of his domain.  

Viktor wanted to leap forward, but a slender arm blocked his path.  

“Absolutely! You must not do that. I can swear on my life to God.”  

Harmon quietly regarded the Saint’s eyes.  

An endlessly righteous gaze, and a shine that only a clergy could see reflected in her eyes. The sacred light that had stripped the false glimmer away during the impeachment trial of the previous Pope flowed over her still in its entirety.  

That alone allowed Harmon to be convinced that the Holy Order’s declaration was false.  

“…I will trust you.”  

“Thank you.”  

At a word, Harmon relaxed his guard, and Ilia responded with a smile.  

Viktor could not catch up to the distance between them, feeling bewildered as they seamlessly continued their conversation.  

“What in the world happened?”  

“Though you may find it hard to believe…”  

Ilia launched into an explanation of everything she had experienced and gone through, presenting the unreasonable measures currently taken by the Order as evidence.  

By the time the lengthy tale and her impassioned plea concluded, the long night had passed, and dawn was breaking.  

“That’s… really hard to believe.”  

Could it be due to the overwhelming nature of her tale?  

Harmon’s expression hardened like stone as he spoke.  

“It is unfathomable that His Holiness, the Pope, the Sententia—the artifact of the Nine Gods—could not protect his own mind.”  

“…I would be in disbelief weren’t it not for witnessing it firsthand. But there is no doubt that Tracy possesses a method to manipulate the mind by bypassing divine power!”  

“Being able to manipulate the divine power… Do you understand that mere mention itself is a blasphemy?”  

Ilia’s face momentarily stiffened at Harmon’s cold voice.  

Harmon, gazing at her with a heavy expression, sighed before continuing.  

“If it wasn’t the Saint speaking those words, I would have executed punishment myself.”  

His tone contained sincere goodwill laced with resignation.  

However, that did not mean Harmon was fully convinced.  

“I will return to the Order and judge once I see things for myself. Please understand that I cannot respond right away.”  

“…That could be dangerous.”  

“It won’t be dangerous. If what the Saint said is true, then neither I nor the Saint would possess the ability to brainwash you.”  

“Even so, if you were to forcefully restrain whether due to our current scenario…”  

“Who is there to say that?”  

“No matter how you say it, there are limits to what the current Knights Commander can do…”  

“There’s plenty I can do. If I declare an emergency situation under my authority, the Holy Knights, the most powerful military faction, must follow my orders over those of the Pope himself. Even if not…”  

How dare anyone restrain me?  

The words left unsaid distinctly lingered in Viktor’s and Ilia’s minds.  

Regrettably, Harmon’s confidence began applying to the two of them as well.  

“Therefore, you must comply with me. My mind and heart implore me to trust the Saint, but my position and status do not allow for that. Please understand.”  

His outward appearance seemed ordinary, with merely common brown eyes, yet an overwhelming pressure bore down on them, grasping their bodies as if it sought to bind them.  

The implication was unmistakable.  

“Don’t make me laugh! How do you intend to execute this?”  

Viktor brandished his sword in front of the Saint and confronted Harmon.  

Daring to look upon the one who had instantly transformed into a rabid beast, Harmon’s gaze flickered momentarily.  

A brief moment of surprise crossed his face.  

Eventually, he looked up once more with heavy eyes, regarding Viktor and Ilia with the weight of his gaze.  

He took a single step back.  

But that one step was all that changed.  

“If you refuse, I will no longer be able to trust the Saint’s words. Please give me your faith.”  

“Saint! There must be another way. You do not need to follow!”  

Harmon’s words clashed with Viktor’s cries, creating chaos.  

“…If they claim they have taken me, then that would provide a valid reason for you, Commander, to return me to the Knights. That’s it.”  

“Saint!”  

Viktor was stunned into silence by Ilia’s unexpected words.  

However, she simply shook her head in response.  

“Do not resist. This is the best option.”  

Viktor bit his lip upon reading the message.  

And at that moment, Harmon ignited a flame in his chest.  

“Feel like you’re being dragged away against your will? You’re quite the young one; your pride is remarkable. Would you take a chance, or will you come at me like this?”  

“Don’t make me laugh. You are making one massive mistake…!”  

Harmon provoked him further, causing Viktor to raise his spirit. Yet a voice broke through him immediately from behind.  

“Calm down. Commander Harmon is simply trying to understand your identity.”  

“The journey back to the Holy Kingdom is long, Saint. You’ll find out regardless…”  

Harmon did not deny Ilia’s words.  

Viktor’s face twisted further at the sound of such descent, but she replied with a calm expression, “No. He will return where he belongs.”  

“…I cannot accept that.”  

“You shall accept. If not, you will witness the Saint committing suicide.”  

In a peaceful tone, she produced a tiny dagger and poised it at her throat.  

A stream of blood began to trickle down her soft skin from the gleaming blade.  

“Saint!”  

Horrified by Viktor’s shout, Harmon’s voice suddenly broke forth.  

“You’re serious. Why would you do such a thing?”  

“I cannot cause more trouble from the indebted position I have already been in.”  

“…They may attempt to exploit the Saint. I have never heard of any group that possesses a superhuman at such a young age…”  

“If that were truly the case, I would inform you personally of it in due time.”  

Ilia interrupted Harmon’s methodical voice with an earnest face.  

As Harmon continued to stare at her resolutely, something whispered to him in an unexpected place.  

“Saint! I have my own duties too! I can’t just leave you in danger…”  

“It was indeed my duty to ensure the Commander meets the Saint. So return to that ‘one’ now. That is my rightful duty.”  

“But…”  

“Regardless of the outcome, I pledge to not forget the favor you’ve done for me. Please do convey my gratitude to them too. …I will not forget.”  

Ilia nodded her head politely.  

That gesture resembled a farewell, as if she were leaving behind her last words before death. Viktor couldn’t just leave her like this.  

Crack!  

As he clenched his teeth and swung his sword, it cut through the air in silence.  

Boom!  

Suddenly, an explosive sound erupted between Viktor and Harmon.  

Although he could not follow the movements, he knew it was a matter that could never occur.  

In shock, he opened his eyes wide, and his mouth gaped in horror as a scream involuntarily escaped him.  

“No!”  

Yet fortunately, that collision ended there.  

Two swords crossed in a shape of the cross. The fierce gray and glimmering silver auras intertwined fiercely, and droplets of blood began to fall from beneath the pitch-black mask.  

Although it was just a single clash, it was clear where the upper hand lay.  

However, in that moment, Viktor’s momentum matched Harmon’s.  

Harmon gazed at Viktor with a hint of surprise within his brown eyes as they widened slightly.  

Amidst the astonishment, the question lingering in his mind revolved around how Viktor could accomplish such a thing.  

The ruby and sapphire odd eye that appeared through the cracks in the mask glared back fiercely into Harmon’s eyes.  

“Should the Saint fall into danger…”  

From the blood-covered mouth, those unacceptable words surged forth.  

“…I will kill you,” Viktor declared.  

Despite his tremendous potential, he was still far from being at that level. One could dismiss him casually, but Harmon nodded soberly.  

“…I shall remember that.”  

The peculiar color of the aura and its unique odd eye—along with the blue hair slightly revealed through the cracks—would easily expose his identity upon thorough investigation.  

However, he did not regard the young superhuman standing before him as trivial. Instead, the sincerity he sensed from that warrior’s spirit weighed upon his heart.  

‘If that blasphemous remark is indeed true…’  

It would lead to significant upheaval within the Order, rekindling immense chaos. Nevertheless, his urgent hope was fading at a rapid pace.  

It wasn’t about merely worrying for the Order anymore.  

‘Is it possible for magic to breach divine power? How is that even conceivable.”  

This was a matter shaking the very fundamentals of his beliefs.  

Harmon felt as if his journey back toward the Order would be long and detached from his expectations.



-chapter 355-

“Everything is for humanity!!”

The descendants of Zibrick Cassel repeatedly shouted this as they protected the city with their peculiar and grotesque magic.  

It was a sight that sent chills down the spine and felt utterly nauseating.  

It wasn’t merely the sins they committed in their past lives that revolted the onlookers.  

While tribes like orcs or lizardmen, which initially rejected humanity, might be understandable, even races like elves and dwarves, who were historically friendly to humans, had begun to turn hostile. This shift stemmed from the persecution of Zibrick Cassel, the archmage they revered.  

Persecution?  

At this point, Logan couldn’t help but smile wryly.  

“After all, it seems my ancestors didn’t show me any information that might be unfavorable to them.”  

The grudge Zibrick Cassel held against the various race leaders, the Nine Deities, seemed questionable in its justification, not to mention how poorly handled it was.  

By showing his journey to his descendants while omitting this fact, one could assume he was at least somewhat ashamed of it.  

…Not to mention the matter of sacrifices.  

“It’s hard to believe that the Nine Deities were once the leaders of other races…”  

If Zibrick Cassel’s true essence was as such, others may very well have kept the ascension path from him on purpose.  

As he sighed, Logan felt an old resentment toward his ancestor swell within him once more.  

Just then, something lightly nudged against his leg.  

“Mm?”  

A wolf, yawning with boredom next to the altar, pecked him with its forepaw, urging him to read quicker.  

Having experienced so many tales from myths back to back, the presence of that wolf seemed more relatable than strange.  

“I get it, I get it.”  

With a chuckle, Logan realized he had been standing reading the book the whole time and took a seat.  

Thinking back, without any personal effects, perhaps that protruding altar served merely as a desk.

Feeling settled, irrelevant thoughts began to flood his mind.  

But a moment later, as he shifted his gaze back to the book, they vanished without a trace.  

“Ah!”  

The next passage drew a gasp from Logan once more.  

He noticed the word “Magnus.” The term, meaning “large” in ancient language, was also the former name of the present capital city, Grang.  

It referred to the name before the founding king of Grandia and the great mages established the massive walls and magic circles.  

“The old name of Grang…”  

Logan felt an unexpected fondness for the author of the book.  

“It truly came to be like that.”  

It felt as if he were answering an unseen author as he recalled the founding myth of Grandia with a smile.  

Until a millennium ago during the great migration, there hadn’t been a proper human nation on the Central Continent.  

Thus, Grang—Grandia—was formed by the superhumans of humanity in the continent’s eastern part, becoming a beacon of hope for all humans.  

The public opinion of the citizens who had immediately been aided during the city’s defense had no choice but to turn favorably towards them.  

Eventually, even a young man holding memories of his past life couldn’t openly reveal his animosity toward them, as he was a helper in saving the city, not its leader.  

Ultimately, he masked his true feelings, maintaining a cordial attitude while secretly observing their movements.  

After much effort, the young man finally uncovered signs reminiscent of his previous life.  

Magnus continued to grow, just as in his past life.  

However, the successors of Zibrick Cassel, not the young man and the archmages, led this power.  

The troubling fact was that in the process, cases of missing individuals began to emerge.  

While the residents were busy welcoming the city’s endless growth, they paid little attention to the disappearances of a few outsiders.  

But the young man reacted sensitively to those disappearances.  

In the end, he succeeded in capturing those seeking to use humans as sacrifices to elevate their own status.  

However, the results were different than he had anticipated.  

“Tsk.”  

His heart throbbed with guilt, even though he had done nothing wrong.  

“Mm?”  

At this point, Logan’s eyes gleamed.  

Though he had established preventative measures against Cassel Tower’s magic due to improvements in the large magic circle, it wasn’t foolproof.  

These measures would only be effective within major metropolises like Grang that had additional forts installed.  

If he could directly identify those who fell victim to their mental magic, he could relieve himself of some worry regarding them.  

But as he read the next part, his expectations withered away.  

Good news. Bad news.  

While discovering that the brainwashing magic was indeed a good piece of information, the description of the timeframe for its effects was too ambiguous.  

How long was a long time?  

Months? Years?  

“…If it’s years, that would be problematic.”  

How should he apply it?  

A sigh escaped him, but at least it was better than having no clues.  

Thinking positively, Logan kept reading.  

‘This person, my fellow.’  

For some reason, the same sense of kinship arose, and Logan smiled brightly.  

He had also resolved to devise meticulous strategies based on the information he knew from the future.  

It seemed easy, yet once he attempted it, it became challenging.  

Watching how his own actions altered the present compared to his past life only led to growing worries about unintended changes.  

One might say he found himself feeling more impatient.  

“Of course, I guess my personality or intellect is part of the issue, but… Ah?”  

Wait, did this person also mention something about being slow-witted?  

“Tsk.”  

Upon grasping the reason for his sense of kinship, a peculiar bitterness washed over him.  

In the process, the young man’s strength and presence attracted considerable attention.  

The words spoken by the archmage before disappearing echoed.  

– While not as powerful as mana, it is something ordinary humans can train and cultivate. It’s called Force, spread it among the commoners, and encourage them.  

For a long time, that had been misinterpreted to belittle Force.  

The common perception equated it to a power used only by the defeated, those who couldn’t wield mana.   

Perhaps this mindset remained in the region, leading to Grandia becoming a kingdom of knights.  

As Logan nodded in thought, another surprising story followed.  

The young man and the descendants of Cassel continued to collide across the continent countless times.  

And in the majority of those fights, the young man emerged victorious—against them, as well as the other monsters and humans they manipulated.  

This booklet recorded all those innumerable battles.  

While the details of the process and outcome were only summarized, even that alone was an extensive length.  

However, the deeds of Cassel Tower’s schemes and the magic utilized at the time were remarkably detailed, conveying the author’s intent effectively.  

“…Incredible.”  

While the sheer volume could become overwhelming, it was worth reading for Logan.  

After a lengthy record concluded, a different story began to emerge.  

“The Sword God?”  

That term sounded familiar.  

Logan tilted his head, only to find troubling content following.  

Hadn’t he done enough?  

Though bewildered for a moment, he quickly grasped the reason.  

“Ha!?”  

That phrase was too familiar.  

And only then did Logan find assurance that the handwriting that felt familiar wasn’t a mere illusion.  

Despite only one additional character, it was enough to confirm.  

It was a bit precarious, but by participating in the city defense, I could withstand the onslaught of the orc shaman.  

For the second time across three lives, I protected my city, ‘Magnus.’  

Anyone aware of the backstory wouldn’t be able to favor the descendants of Zibrick Cassel.  

But within the sages gathered in Magnus, some defended them for their part in saving the human race in the war against the dragon several centuries ago.  

Capturing the culprit alone took a year of persistent efforts.  

While he maintained suspicion, he remained cautious of their movements.  

However, there were too many of them, and he was alone.  

Even the clues he grasped seemed accidental.  

Those ruffians dismissed the incident as an individual errant act, severing the entire narrative.  

But the individual I caught bore the typical characteristics of Zibrick Cassel—red hair and red eyes.  

During that time, I was unaware that my connection with the descendants of Zibrick Cassel—or rather the black serpents—began a tough and bitter fate.  

Despite numerous victories granting me illustrious honors, I could not root out the black serpents’ origins.  

The cornered agents simply vanished, fleeing from me.  

Those who manipulated human minds had chosen to hide, leaving even the Sword God unable to scour the continent alone unless he was a true god.  

The individual reading this may possess the power of desire or has gained that vision.  

After the archmage’s disappearance was confirmed, the continental central region faced the rise of various races.  

Consequently, rumors spread that the area was no longer habitable for humans.  

Even the kind-hearted elves and dwarves began attacking humans; shocking tales emerged where humans were enslaved and traded in some regions.  

The price paid for the archmage’s persecution of other races had returned to humans.  

As an aftermath, my city, Magnus, tilted towards the eastern continent, and its population continued to rise.  

Some began to proclaim that this place, my ancestral homeland, would not just be a city but humanity’s hope someday.  

The horrific rumors about the archmage hunting down children across the continent persisted among humans, suggesting that fear towards him was even more profound than among other races.  

Eventually, the events drew widespread sanctions.  

In that process, I discovered publicly that the majority of the city’s leadership had fallen under their mind control.  

The method was simple; those exposed to their mind-altering magic for prolonged periods became unable to perform even basic arithmetic.  

It was a fatal flaw if those chosen as representatives of tribes became reduced to being fools.  

Furthermore, that condition was certified as a magical consequence by other mages.  

The descendants of Cassel rebelled, their representatives claiming it was merely the envy of others.  

Since they had never revealed any aspect of mental magic, they outright denied knowing such tactics.  

Knowing the truth, I had no choice but to become enraged, acting impulsively. It was a mistake.  

However, that proved to expose their true nature.  

Once I attacked their representative, soldiers nearby rushed at me with their eyes crimson with madness.  

That sight was undoubtedly abnormal.  

The fact that they didn’t know me turned out to be fortunate.  

The figure known as the Tower Master had attempted to cast magic on me repeatedly, leading to the decisive moment when he vomited blood.  

Due to that, they were ultimately forced to leave the city in haste.  

In our Magnus, the symbol of their presence, the black serpent, was declared a primary enemy before other races.  

Although the mana gradually diminished, the number of those sensitive to it only dwindled as time progressed.  

Yet that perception persisted.  

But in Magnus, I managed to eradicate it completely.  

While my power of desire inadvertently caused the results of extreme ascension solely for the descendants of Cassel, I pretended not to know it.  

Considering the fading mana, humanity’s means to develop in the future would not be magic but Force.  

I believed that confidently.  

One day, rumors about me began to spread.  

That I could defeat weak monsters using mere techniques and Force, leading to miraculous outcomes.  

Now people revered me, transitioning from mere interest.  

They began likening me to the High Priests of the Nine Deities, who showcased incomprehensible powers.  

Thus, I was known as the one favored by the God of Weapons or the Sword God.  

Although I felt proud of my efforts to respond to the power of desire that reincarnated me, I could not be satisfied there.  

This was because my companion and close friend, the archmage Talon Ares, had uttered unsettling words.  

As long as I failed to eradicate them completely, they would someday resurrect Zibrick Cassel.  

Even if I overlooked his power of prophecy, it sounded reasonable to me, someone who had fought against them for decades.  

Yet realistically, there was no way to annihilate them.  

I pondered and puzzled over the issue.  

Then suddenly, an idea burst forth.  

If I couldn’t root out those who would reappear, perhaps I could dash their hopes.  

The easiest method, disseminating the power of desire, proved impossible.  

Thus, I toiled to further develop the techniques I had created during those years of fighting them.  

With only the power of one life in Force, I aimed to bring down a divine being, perhaps become a god.  

Of course, that wasn’t easy.  

But the power of desire within me stood firm, supported by my friend Talon.  

And the black serpents—who had fought with me throughout my life—spurred that inspiration.  

Thus, I could achieve the vision of cutting down Zibrick Cassel, the god they were attempting to bring back.  

Comprising three techniques that sever existing matter, three that erased all extraordinary abilities, and extending to three more that would cut through the roots, space, and souls—right up until I almost achieved the final technique.  

All in all, ten slaying techniques.  

Along with that, I infused my wishes into it, naming it ‘The Vision of the Sword that Slays Gods’ (殺神劍?傳) to be passed down to posterity.

The fact that the imperial envoy had come to Liberty was a secret from the outset.  

However, it was impossible to completely hide the news of the accident that had occurred at the Duke Gile Slayer’s castle, not too far from the capital.  

The loud explosions and screams, along with the master of the castle who had disappeared beyond the northern hillside with a shriek, were witnessed by many.  

Moreover, since the commotion unfolded in the residence of a war hero who had long been in seclusion, the citizens of Liberty could not help but be intrigued.

– The disappearance of Duke Gile Slayer.  

– Terror incidents carried out by remnants from Tria, Romaine, and Tahiti.  

– The royal family would devote all efforts to find the missing Duke and would thoroughly cleanse the remnants of the fallen nation.

[Yes, that is correct.]  

The face of King Kran III was hard and rigid. He could not present himself with aplomb while relaying the news that the main military strength of a nation, borrowed from hidden superhumans, had gone missing.

Rick thought that no matter how ignorant one might be, he could be certain of this much.  

Both Dwayne and Damian seemed to share the same sentiment as they were smiling broadly.  

With great effort, Rick managed to suppress an urge to smile back and read the writing on the paper lifted by Damian in a casual tone.  

“Hmm, no. One cannot obsess over what has already transpired; how can one be a ruler of a nation? We have no choice but to take solace in having discovered the Empire’s true intentions through this incident.”  

[…While that is indeed the case, are you certain you are all right?]  

“Yes? What do you mean…?”  

[The last sight of Duke Gile was reportedly one of madness, and there were even witness accounts claiming he jumped into the den of northern magical beasts.]  

“Ah….”  

Even for a superhuman, diving into one of the two major magical realms on the continent while insane would almost mean certain death.  

However, as the information in hand differed, the impressions of those hearing the news could not help but vary considerably.  

‘Wow, how far that man has gone…’  

But unable to reveal his true feelings, Rick merely averted his gaze and let out a deep sigh.  

“Duke Gile was a martyr who spent his life concealing his identity for the nation. How could his sacrifice be for nothing? But!”  

Rick paused mid-sentence, burying his emotions, as if to calm himself.  

With a subtle pressure, he pressed his eyelids before quickly reopening them and glaring as he spoke sharply.  

“He has stabilized the chaos of his allies and illuminated the Empire’s schemes. And in the process, he slaughtered what will undoubtedly become powerful foes for the Empire. He has fulfilled his duty. The spirits of our forefathers residing in heaven will surely commend him.”  

As though genuinely mourning for Gile, Rick trembled and strained his eyes to bring forth tears. Moments later, a single tear dropped from his eye amid the residual swelling.  

Feeling the need to hide that tear, he clenched his eyelids shut and turned his head with a solemn voice as he added his final words.  

“Now, what remains is our responsibility to those left behind. So please, remember together with me, Gile Slayer and his great sacrifice.”  

[…Of course. And once again, I offer my apologies.]  

When Rick slightly opened his narrow eyes to gaze discreetly at the communication device, Kran III’s already heavy expression grew even weightier as he delivered one last sincere apology.  

Behind him, Dwayne and Damian were nodding their heads with astonished expressions as they raised their thumbs repeatedly.  

‘Maybe I could really be an actor?’  

The protagonist who pulled off a perfect performance felt high levels of satisfaction with his own acting abilities.  

[If the Empire provokes again, we will not sit idly by in Liberty either. We will join forces with McLain and stand against it! Thank you once again for your kindness, Your Majesty!]  

What could only be described as incompatible with the context of king to king, the term “Your Majesty” employed by Rick affirmed the perfection of his acting.  

“Then I will proceed to discuss strategies among my retainers to deal with the Empire’s schemes.”  

[Liberty will also be with McLain. Just give us a prompt when needed.]  

“Of course.”  

With an enthusiastic line as the final remark, Rick concluded the communication and confidently inquired,  

“What do you think!?”  

However, the response to his self-assured voice came back with a reluctant expression.  

“Everything was good, but the final part was a bit…”  

Rick mumbled an expression of confusion as he repeated Damian’s words.  

“Huh?”  

“It sounds like you’re asking for assistance if the Empire provokes Liberty again. You said you understood.”  

“Does that mean… that?”  

“Yes. On the surface, it appears to be a conflict between Liberty and the Empire, but you insisted McLain would help.”  

“Ah….”  

It wasn’t until after hearing those words that Rick finally understood his mistake.  

“Ugh… How naive of me.”  

As Rick lamented while holding his head, Damian chuckled and patted his shoulder.  

“Kran III is just a sly fox. He just got their support with a bow from you. Well, when the war breaks out, it will ultimately fall upon us to grapple with the Empire first, so there won’t be any harm.”  

“Yeah, you did well.”  

Once Dwayne joined in with the encouragement, Rick’s expression brightened again.  

“But where is His Majesty right now?”  

“Who knows? He mentioned needing to go through the Forest of Magical Beasts after potentially disappearing.”  

“He’s probably returning about now?”  

“If he entered from the northern part of Liberty, then he’ll emerge at the eastern edge of the Forest of Magical Beasts. If he turns back from there… maybe in just a few weeks.”  

“That seems likely.”  

While the three laughed and rid themselves of their worries, the true protagonist of the story was desperately running through an unseeable, pitch-black darkness.  

* * *  

In a forest where massive trees with a circumference of at least twenty meters stood tall, enormous leaves veiled the sky, causing the forest’s interior to remain exceptionally dark.  

Of course, embarking on such a journey in complete darkness had become no challenge for Logan at this point.  

However, he was continuously sighing.  

“Everything was going so well for me…”   

After driving out the spirit of Zibrick Cassel and awakening the core of the Holy Sword, Logan found himself pondering what he could do with the remaining husk of the Sacred Sword.  

Before arriving at the ruins, he had aimed to provoke a conflict between Cassel Tower and the Empire using the Holy Sword as bait.  

Currently, he was allied with the Empire, but in a precariously ambiguous position.  

Yet, recently he had suspected that even the Pope of the Sacred Kingdom had been brainwashed and was now likely working under the influence of this formidable enemy.   

First, he thought about shattering the alliance between Cassel Tower and the Empire. This thought emerged as he believed it was almost confirmed that the Prince Baros was behind Cassel Tower in his past life. Thus, they would surely desire to grasp the legacy of Zibrick Cassel at any cost.  

To divert the Empire’s attention toward Liberty, he intentionally exposed his identity as Gile Slayer and then attempted to lure Cassel Tower into movement through Louisa with the Holy Sword to serve as bait.  

If he, who had an opposite affinity to the magical powers of Cassel Tower, borrowed the strength of the Holy Sword, he could be certain that he wouldn’t fall to them unless a legendary Archmagician or Aura Master showed up.  

Even if things reached a worst-case scenario, he believed he wouldn’t mind offering one sword to Cassel Tower. Regardless of the past life of Baros, it seemed the current Emperor did not fully embrace Cassel Tower. Therefore, he thought the disasters of his previous life would not repeat themselves.  

However, an unexpected appearance of an ancestor’s spirit had resulted in the core of the Holy Sword being shattered in the process.  

Moreover, with Cassel Tower not being able to recognize the powers of the Holy Sword, his original plan was now out the window.  

Nevertheless, to just think, “Well, I’ve practically eliminated the Magic Sword, so it’s fine,” would be squandering a good opportunity.  

Therefore, he decided to push himself slightly further.  

– If I can’t use the complete Holy Sword as bait, then let’s use what’s left of it instead.  

A reckless plan stemming from the sheer will to somehow incite a confrontation between Cassel Tower and the Empire began to take shape in his mind.  

The memories of an ancestor fortified his courage to enact this reckless endeavor.  

If Zibrick Cassel’s delusions had reached Cassel Tower to any extent, they would undoubtedly never give up the Holy Sword, at whatever cost.  

However, carrying out such a plot necessitated his own intervention.  

Fortunately, the silvery aura he used during his disguise as Gile might appear similar to the sacred power of the Holy Sword at a glance, and inducing a misconception by causing alterations in its properties would not be too difficult to execute.  

The issue, however, was that this would only be possible if it were in his possession.  

Thus, Logan resolve to continue the role-play of Gile Slayer, knowing that the Cassel Tower and Empire would temporarily move together to handle the occurrences from the ruins, enabling him to disrupt their alliance.  

If the Holy Sword were present, mages from Cassel Tower would certainly arrive, and his goal was to slay the Empire’s envoy that would arrive with them, pinning the blame on Cassel Tower.  

Of course, this won’t be an easy task. But when push comes to shove, he felt that it wouldn’t be altogether impossible—unless some gargantuan like Trist Honsby was sent from within the Empire, he could easily toy around with the foot-soldiers due to their lower skill levels.  

Furthermore, he did not worry about the mages from Cassel Tower using magic that he couldn’t resist.  

‘Rather, the real concern isn’t that.’   

The most worrying scenario was if the Empire attempted to retrieve the artifact through negotiation.  

If that happened, things could get complicated, but fortunately, the arrogant Empire was moving just as he predicted.  

No, they exceeded expectations indeed.  

‘I thought they would merely send envoys.’  

The Magic Spear, Greet Ainshein.  

Logan still did not know why the esteemed commander of the Eastern First Legion personally intervened, but his presence equated to a tremendous catch.  

It was also unexpected that the mages of Cassel Tower would openly attempt to slay the commander of the Empire.  

There must have been some underlying conflict that Logan was unaware of.  

‘Well, that has made the act much easier.’   

The greatest risk had emerged when he initially heard them order him to sever his arm.  

After all, that would have been the most perilous phase he ever faced.  

He had lightly self-inflicted his skin before becoming anxious, fearing that the act wouldn’t go well.  

Fortunately, aided by the unforeseen internal conflict, everything managed to proceed successfully beyond what he had imagined. The masterpiece he directed and acted in came to a perfect conclusion.  

As they imagined, chaotic scenes must now be unfurling within Cassel Tower and the imperial family.  

The mere thought exhilarated him, filling him with exhilaration.  

Everything was indeed going swimmingly.  

Yes.  

Until that moment.  

– Kyaaaa!  

“What the hell is this…?!”  

Swish!  

Suddenly, Logan confronted a lethal intent that erupted from the very edge of his contemplations.  

As he instinctively swung his sword, the large maw leaping out from the darkness was split apart by the golden aura that met it head-on.  

He had no time to wipe away the vile shower of blood that violently splattered around him.  

The brilliance of gold flickered in the shadow. Perhaps that was a factor as well.  

– Kyaaoo!  

– Uuuuu!  

– Kyaarrr!  

From all directions, ghastly howls erupted.  

Logan couldn’t contain his pent-up annoyance any longer.  

“Dammit! I was doing so well avoiding things!”  

With an outburst of frustration, he unleashed a battle cry that echoed despairingly.  

In response, the eerie roars from every quarter crescendoed exponentially.  

– Kyaaaak!  

– Grawawa!  

– Greuaaa!  

The aura surrounding Logan intensified further.  

“Aah, damn it! This is a hell of a situation.”  

Logan’s gut churned—he instinctively gauged the threat level, mentally preparing for what seemed to be a worst-case scenario.

“I’m merely stating the basic principles outright.”

Whirr.

As the monumental tension escalated, small items around them started to shift precariously in place.

“Back off! Widen the distance!”

“Everyone, disperse now!”

The Holy Knights and knights from the Empire, who had escorted Tris, were all alarmed and instinctively distanced themselves, unable to withstand the pressure emanating from two of the strongest beings.

Yet, such circumstances led their expressions to harden like stone. The standoff showcased the psychological conflicts amongst the two apex beings, deeply unsettling those present.

– Both of them are genuinely serious.

The feeling came over them, while similar thoughts followed closely.

– Why this insistence?

They, the towering exemplars representing both nations, were well aware that a minor misstep from either side could provoke irreversible damage to their countries.

If the Divine Sword made an error, all justifications claimed by the Empire would evaporate, and if the Sword Soul falters, the Empire would find a solid justification for annihilating the Holy Kingdom.

Even if both remained unharmed, merely maintaining this confrontation could severely escalate tensions between their nations. It was a silly game, played with the gravity of an actual war looming over their heads.

While neither of the two apex beings lacked common sense, their perspectives naturally narrowed once confrontation ensued.

HUUUM.

Crackle.

As the red and white energies clashed savagely, the gazes of the two super beings flickered with a change.

They had belatedly realized their miscalculations.

HUUUM.

‘This…!’

‘Hah, it’s…!’

They had come to a point where the stakes would spiral out of control the moment one were to yield.

In a brief moment, pride incited spontaneous actions.

Both combatants, undefeated for more than a decade against their respective challengers, would capitulate only if they held complete certainty that their rival lacked as much strength.

However, in circumstances where neither had clear supremacy, considering yielding would become unthinkable.

‘The Emperor’s will is unwavering. Regardless of circumstances, war will unfold, and if I can break the Holy Kingdom’s blade before then, it will serve my interests.’

Those around would be shaken by such insane thoughts, yet the two, consumed by their own passions, quickly justified themselves.

* * *

That very debate had been a timeless one.

– Who’s the strongest among humans?

Knights or mages. Force users or mana users.

In an age where super beings surpassing human limits persisted.

That particular debate often arose at noble gatherings in the Kingdom.

And over the past ten years, two figures had remained inseparable from the conversation.

– The greatest swordsman of the continent, Sword Soul Tris Honsby.

– The greatest swordsman of the Holy Kingdom, Divine Sword Harmon Killerblue.

Upon the current Emperor’s ascension, the Sword Soul had cut down a hundred elite knights during the rebellion mounted by another prince, who refused to acquiesce.

The Divine Sword was said to have single-handedly thwarted monster waves that besieged the villages on the southern foothills of the Magic Mountains, enduring a fierce battle for three straight days.

Even snippets of their legendary tales often seemed like fabrications. Most gossipers speculated they were grossly exaggerated.

Yet, within those critical moments, the two figures proved that their feats were far from fanciful as they stood at the very center of Nobiense.

In an instant.

Only red and white light populated the space, as everything bathed within the radiance fell apart into pieces in that moment.

Swish.

As the flash of energy shot outward, it cleaved through the building’s protective arch, smashing apart the sacred structure unwaveringly fortified by various divine spells.

Beings of myth wielding a single sword.

With a single swing, beams of light would surge forward for dozens of meters. Whichever hue it was—snow white or fiery red—slashed down to leave everlasting marks on the earth. When swung horizontally, it turned into a harbinger of destruction, shattering every obstacle in its path.

At the moment they collided head-on….

BOOOOM!

An unimaginable, overwhelming sound erupted as the fury of a tempest surged across the battlefield.

Everyone present, shaken beyond belief, could hardly digest the macabre scene being unleashed.

“This… this is impossible.”

“How… can a human…?”

“Monsters….”

The aides who believed they knew them well stood frozen, watching the carnage unfurling. Among them was Jerome Decade, who shared the title “super being.”

“How… is this possible!?”

For Jerome, shock was an understatement.

He had attained the intermediate level of aura use, and although he had yet to witness the Divine Sword up close, he believed he had some inkling of his master’s prestige, which was touted among the highest ranks.

However, all sense of confidence fell away in that instant.

‘An aura user at such a caliber… rumors suggested space itself rends as a result. Yet even so…’

It acted like a force not entirely of this world.

The tales told in common parlance felt like mere whispers compared to the extraordinary things happening before his very eyes. Witnessing such powers, Jerome felt support for any conventional military units he could rely on had utterly faltered.

While he struggled to regain composure, the surrounding radiance slowly waned, as the gust settling from the clash revealed clouds of dust swirling around.

– A conclusion has arisen.

All eyes of Nobiense converged onto the ruins of the central shrine.

Clatter, clatter.

Barros’s bluntness struck hard, enough to warrant her tightening grip against the ire creeping in.

“……You recognize that our stands could differ frequently, your Highness. However, should we choose to tread over the cliff, I will stand firm.”

Barros, now moving closer, lowered his voice deliberately.

His words twisted upon her thoughts with an uncertain yield.

Barros turned away, his demeanor indicative of leaving the inquiry hanging in uncertainty.

“You do worry, don’t you, your Eminence? Scheduled for everything we have and even securing time seems straightforward compared to my side.”

“Is anything ever simple for anyone? Even if it sounds dull, it’s still filled with worry.”

“In this game, where one creates pyramids of chances while figuring out what I’ll have to do to survive, I hear many of us seek the Saint to bring them back from the grave.”

At that juncture, Cardinal Tracey’s expression lost its imposing nature, finally cracking a small smile.

“Would you dare to bring such remarks openly again, your Highness? What if the rumors become concrete and reach the right ears?”

Mere shields could do nothing against such confrontations, and Barros let out a soft chuckle before waving off her worries.

“Shall we agree to disagree? I would at least expect greater effort on your side as well.”

Barros moved away, clear in the absence of tension as he stepped away. 

After he exited, Cardinal Tracey felt the weight of the room distilling in fresh air but couldn’t dismiss the concerns that had settled deep down.

‘Truly, there’s a chance for disaster looming over…’

With a sigh resonating with realization, the thoughts drew no further consequence—it was still reverent to maintain the façade of indifference amidst the fracture of promises between sacred foes.

Yet one truth lingered— the necessity to discover resources before taking on the burdens, and Cardinal Tracey realized the need for vigilance that soon awaited the crossing.

“……I mustn’t let my guard down.”

Meanwhile, as control ebbed away from both sides, anxiety crept back into the undercurrents, mirroring the confusion of the situation ahead.
