“Failure, failure… I seem to be hearing that phrase quite often these days.”

At the quietly resonating voice, the bodies of those bowed down stiffened.

“Yes, sometimes you fail while working. However, repeated failures do not suit our empire. Surely, I’m not the only one who thinks this way?”

The heads of those who were bowed sank even lower.

“First Max and now Grit… Not to mention in Grit’s case, hmmm…”

A subtle rage was felt in the Emperor’s calm voice that followed.

The three individuals who were kneeling before the Emperor, a sight rarely seen, could scarcely move in front of the Emperor’s rage.

Tap. Tap.

In the vast chamber, only the sound of the Emperor’s fingers drumming against the armrest of his throne broke the silence.

After a while, the Emperor spoke again.

“…What do you think they are plotting?”

The anger just felt moments ago had vanished, replaced by a calm voice reverberating through the chamber. However, no one there could see that as another face of anger.

In the cautious atmosphere, the person in the center among the three bowed even lower in respect.

“I dare not presume, but I would like to offer a statement.”

The elderly man, whose gaunt face was etched with deep wrinkles, revealed his considerable age and firm demeanor.

“Speak.”

“I have heard that the black serpent faction conveyed their intentions of surrender through His Highness the Second Prince. However, soon after…”

“Shortly.”

“…I suspect that a certain Gael, having acquired something from the ruins, deemed it valuable enough to betray your Majesty’s trust.”

“To stake the organization’s fate, is that it, Prime Minister?”

“…If not, then I cannot explain their reckless behavior.”

“Indeed. That is true.”

The words of the current Empire’s Prime Minister, Roktus Guspelt, held merit.

But as if that was not enough, the Emperor’s gaze shifted to the left of the Prime Minister.

“You are the only one who has met their leader. Galen, what do you think?”

The white-haired sorcerer, with youth in his demeanor that belied his age, lifted his head. His expression was careful, unlike the arrogant and proud sorcerer that formerly traversed the Sorcerer’s Winds.

“An individual who conceals a serpentine nature beneath an ordinary facade. It felt as if the records of the royal sorcerer’s tower regarding the serpent that swallowed the truth were detailed without alteration. He does not appear to be one to act impulsively.”

“…Is that so.”

“If they were to take such reckless measures, they must have their reasons.”

Once he finished speaking, Galen Dikaid lowered his head again, but the Emperor did not show a satisfied countenance.

“Then what do you suppose those reasons could be? Aside from the usual assumptions.”

The disappointment and anger lingering in the Emperor’s voice were palpable.

The three individuals, bowed beneath the heavy aura enveloping the chamber, involuntarily shuddered. It had been over twenty years since the Emperor took the throne, yet it was rare to see him display such open emotions.

Yet even with their silence, the Emperor’s gaze, which slightly frowned, turned to the remaining individual.

“Tris.”

“…Yes, Your Majesty.”

The aged knight, still hailed as the strongest on the continent, quietly lifted his head.

“Do you know what angers me the most right now?”

“Please command me with anything. As Your Majesty’s sword, I shall cut down anything that obstructs you.”

The knight’s bold words seemed to please the furious Emperor somewhat.

The Emperor, with a bitter smile, continued in a frigid tone.

“Time is but an issue; those already exposed can be dealt with. They are persistently vile, leaving seeds, but at the very least, I can ensure they won’t raise their heads for the next three hundred years.”

At the sentence reeking of bloodshed, all three bowed down in unison.

“However, the timing is crucial. The empire’s long-held wish of placing the world entirely within our grasp remains. We still must receive the last fruit they promised.”

“!?”

Doubt emerged on the faces of the empire’s leaders—knights, nobles, and sorcerers alike.

“Yet Your Majesty, would those who have betrayed us keep their promises?”

“You are showing them undue mercy.”

“Rumors are already spreading from the small kingdom united. The prestige of the empire is being tarnished. You cannot afford to be patient, Your Majesty.”

Not just the Prime Minister Roktus Guspelt, but even the continent’s strongest sword and sorcerer could be easily dispensed with at the Emperor’s word.

The man before them, no matter if blood-related, possessed a ruthless disposition, willing to cut even family ties if necessary. It was the driving force that kept the empire stable and thriving throughout his reign.

While they all thought along those lines, they still voiced their opinions.

In response, for the first time that day, a small smile appeared on the Emperor’s face. It was this very demeanor that was the reason he kept them close.

“Your words ring true. However, if it allows us to endure a brief moment of anger to achieve our goals, then that is the righteous path.”

Though admonitions are the virtue of loyal subjects, it is the duty of the ministers to obey the Emperor’s commands.

Having spoken all they intended, the three lowered their heads again, pledging allegiance to a monarch who had never once disappointed them since taking the throne.

As if to meet their expectations, the Emperor collected his thoughts and continued calmly.

“Without knowing the enemy’s intentions, there is no need to wait. We must force them to act as we desire, no matter their schemes.”

What did that mean?

As the three bewilderedly contemplated, the Emperor followed up with immediate orders.

“Tris, Galen.”

“Yes, Your Majesty.”

“Yes, Your Majesty!”

“I shall give you the chance to recuperate from previous failures. Mobilize the elite of your families. I will assign half of the Imperial Knights and the elite of the Special Inspection Department as well. Go to the capital of Nobience.”

“We shall obey!”

‘This is war.’

A chilling resolve swept across the eyes of both transcendents who held that very thought.

Yet the following words seemed a bit odd.

“However, the excuse will be protection for Barros. With Max dead, you shall enter the capital under the pretext of succeeding him.”

“Your Majesty, that level of justification will not allow the kingdom to permit such a military presence internally.”

The Prime Minister Roktus raised a perfectly reasonable concern on behalf of the two transcendents.

“Of course, we will need a more substantial excuse. Tris, contact Jerome.”

“…Are you referring to Jerome and not His Highness Barros?”

Tris’s perplexed inquiry brought a cold smile to the Emperor’s lips.

“Yes.”

At that firm and decisive answer, the expression of everyone present slightly stiffened. In essence, it was tantamount to declaring that the succession rights of Prince Barros had been completely obliterated.

Regardless of their expressions, the Emperor’s calm voice rolled on.

“Send a final ultimatum to the black serpent faction through Jerome.”

A final ultimatum. The weight behind those words made the three even more rigid.

“Tell them to make the official announcement that the kingdom wishes to serve the empire as a vassal state. For that, they must pay the price for betrayal. Alternatively, it’s also acceptable for them to transfer the position of the Pope to the Emperor of the Empire.”

The eyes of the three widened, startled by the shocking statement.

“!?”

“Your Majesty, could it be…?”

“Is that even possible!?”

It was such an astonishing declaration. While the serpent faction claimed they could control the Pope’s mind, subjugating the kingdom was an entirely different matter. The elected Pope did not hold the power to decide the fate of the kingdom.

The Emperor was not unaware of that, yet his calm voice continued.

“I want you to make the impossible… possible. The deadline is one month from when you finish your preparations and arrive at Nobience. At that time, you shall become the envoys sent by the Emperor of the Empire to celebrate the kingdom’s subjugation.”

“…And if they refuse? No, even if they accept, what if they do not announce it?”

“Then the death of Max will be attributed to them.”

A chilling declaration followed. Understanding the implications behind that statement, the three’s eyes widened once more.

“…If the envoy sent by Jerome and the Inspection Department has yet to uncover the reason, then the probability of that being true will be significantly high.”

Galen Dikaid nodded, mentioning his grandson.

“The pretext of exterminating the empire’s enemy hidden within the capital or sending representatives to celebrate. Either way, they would suffice as justifications to enter the capital.”

Tris also nodded in agreement.

However, in the meantime, Prime Minister Roktus cautiously brought forth a fact that seemed to have eluded everyone’s mind.

“…However, there is no assurance that the leader of the black sorcerers resides within the capital.”

His concern was valid. Yet the Emperor’s extraordinary words continued unabated.

“Regardless of whether or not he is there.”

“…?”

“You three will first handle the cardinal known as Tracy, who has always been at the Pope’s side.”

“Yes!?”

Galen exclaimed, caught up in his shock, and Tris and Roktus widened their eyes to the utmost.

“The individual suspected of being the core of the Pope’s brainwashing. You will eliminate her and secure the Pope. It does not matter if he regains his senses or not after that. Once that is done, we can get involved with the kingdom freely.”

Nobody doubted the source of the Emperor’s intelligence.

If that were the case, it had to be true.

“Whether the serpent faction follows through with their demands or not, we will get what we need. However, if they uphold their promise, what will remain for the Sword God and the Sorcerer Winds to do?”

Was it merely his nature, or was it just how he behaved? Roktus identified the slight flaw within the plan and expressed admiration as he pointed it out.

But instead of the Emperor, it was Galen who answered.

“Why would we not have work? If they uphold their promise, we can enter as a congratulatory envoy and simply cut off that woman’s neck.”

A grim laugh accompanied his assertion.

The Emperor revealed his agreement through silence, clearly expressing that he carried no opposing view.

However, even with that understanding, Roktus continued to elaborate.

“However, if the leader of the serpents truly exists within, it could be an issue.”

Upon hearing that, the expression of Gale, the Winds of the Sorcerer glared back, seemingly losing composure.

“Ha, if the Sword God would accompany me, what could it matter?”

“What, you are coming along and what is the problem? Even if it is the Arch Sorcerer, what concern is there?”

Roktus, who had previously showcased great confidence, suddenly faltered under Galen’s steadiness, lifting his head at the comment made back.

“…I was more worried about the heavy loss experienced by the Sorcerer Winds back in the day.”

The remark drew a sour expression from Galen.

“Ha. So what issue is there with the Sword God accompanying us? No matter how great the Arch Sorcerer is…”

“There would be support for the assault as well.”

“Yes?”

The confident Galen, stunned, glanced toward the Emperor, but the oppressive atmosphere compelled Roktus to lower his head swiftly.

“The Black Serpents may possess a leader residing behind the gates of the capital. While the Sorcerer may be powerful, we cannot overlook the plausible support he will have too.”

Roktus spoke out with his severe expression.

Galen, channeling confidence, met the Prime Minister’s gaze, only to reveal the tension that, depending on the situation, the support might return in a pursuit.

“Then we should not needlessly lose forces. Hand over the order further away from me.”

Roktus quieted down once more, but the moment the Emperor’s words of consolation unfolded, the air became momentarily lighter.

“I will calm your worries.”

“Yes, Your Majesty.”

The stiff-faced Prime Minister nodded, showing both formality and affection.

The Emperor spoke with a sinking calmness.

“The descent into the capital and swaying of the sorcerers may not be the worst. My support shall cover that.”

“Your Majesty…?”

At the Emperor’s misplaced words, Roktus chastised after pausing but was caught unprepared for the Emperor’s follow-up.

“We should prepare for whatever comes ahead. Trepidation has no meaning, so rest assured.”

“…Yes, Your Majesty.”

The Prime Minister lowered his head once again, illuminated with apparent resolve.

He was uncertain of the Emperor’s intentions, yet the reassured tone kept his mind as calm as the water’s surface.

Ultimately, the air had shifted toward a strange unity, prompting the resolve to attempt action at some point.

At that juncture, however, the Emperor locked eyes with the remaining two, who held unyielding expressions.

“Tris.”

“…Yes, Your Majesty.”

The expression of the continent’s strongest knight lifted for a moment as he received notice.

“Prepare the numbers you deem necessary. The time has come for us to act once more.”

“…Understood.”

Roktus’s voice remained deep and resonating as he nodded, an air of determination stirring around him.

Afterward, the gathered people exchanged worrying glances, contemplating how much effort would be needed to follow through on all that was just discussed.

Seemingly satisfied with their responses, the Emperor leaned back in thought.

At that moment, all gathered could not match the Emperor’s tranquility.

As expected of them, their energy was once again upturned, while their loyalty never left their cores.

In a fleeting moment, silence enveloped the vast chamber once more, raising the emperor’s voice just a touch amidst the heavy thoughts.

“All who doubt must vanish along with the road ahead. Push ahead; unlike those who slack off, for this time, we will prevail!”

The voices of the three, affirmed their loyalty.

“Yes, Your Majesty!”

As they lifted their heads in unison, shining determination sparked within their gazes.

With determination guiding their breath, they believed they stood on the brink of a different future.



-chapter 354-

After dying painfully, I opened my eyes to find myself once again in my childhood.  

I thought it was a dream, but it was not.  

A cheer erupted from my lips.  

My second life had to start with different goals.  

Not only for myself but for my family and tribe as well.  

Logan’s hands trembled instinctively at a story he could empathize with more than anyone else.  

Fortunately, I had experience.  

Based on my previous life, I began to cultivate my strength from a young age, thinking that the root cause of the city’s downfall was the lack of a strong warrior to stop the Orc Shaman.  

Walking a path once trodden was not difficult, and in the process, I systematically organized the rough manifestations and developments of Force that I had experienced, spreading it to my surroundings.  

At a young age, I became a force strong enough to ‘surpass most mages,’ which drew many seeking to learn from me.  

However, unlike me, ordinary humans and even mages struggled to grasp the concept of the Force.  

No matter how simply I taught them, most failed to understand even the basic principles.  

In the end, the efficiently structured training methods could only be applied to myself.  

Logan felt frustrated.  

In the end, he had no choice but to train his disciples in the reckless manner his father used with him, risking their lives.  

Fortunately, due to their numbers, a few began awakening to the Force.  

Well-trained warriors grew strong enough to contend with Lizardmen and Orc warriors that used innate magic.  

Meanwhile, he continued to break through his own limits through solitary training and grew even more.  

When I became confident that I could match not only the Orc Shamans but also the Arch Shamans, I began to take action.  

And so, over a decade passed.  

Logan finally eliminated all the sporadic threats from the mixed-race tribes and became the ruler of a grand city that unified all the human races in the vicinity.  

The strongest and most prosperous grand city in the area, a beacon of hope for humanity.  

The city I built came to bear that name, and I was also honored with the grand title of ‘Great Warrior.’  

Then, strong humans who had scattered after the Magic Spear appeared began to focus their attention on Logan.  

Those from other factions, known as the High Priest or Mage, proposed training together with Logan.  

Logan did not refuse.  

He no longer wanted to see the sacrifices of his compatriots due to the oppression and invasion of mixed-race tribes and monstrous threats he had witnessed throughout his previous and current life.  

Thus, the ‘Alliance’ was born.  

The goal seemed achievable more easily than expected.  

The Alliance gradually integrated human tribes from the Central Continent, forming a massive force.  

As the number of united humans increased, the provocations from monsters and mixed-race tribes began to diminish.  

Logan and the alliance leaders failed to recognize the severity of the situation until it escalated dramatically.  

While expanding their forces against mixed-race tribes and monsters, they couldn’t have anticipated such a grave issue arising within the human community.  

As soon as the leaders of the Alliance, including Logan, began to dig into the events, the culprit was surprisingly revealed quickly.  

“Ha…”  

A sigh escaped Logan’s lips as he focused on the content of the booklet.  

That name again.  

It was more than just irregular at this point.  

They had sacrificed at least ten thousand human lives to prepare some horrific magic.  

Rather than conversation with the madmen, a direct battle began.  

But the outcome differed far from Logan’s expectations.  

The moment the battle commenced, the leaders of the Alliance were ambushed from within.  

However, it seemed that the variable did not yield a significant effect.  

The one who claimed to be their leader, a snake that swallowed the truth, was a powerful Arch Mage, who had become exceedingly rare in an age where mana was dwindling.  

And aside from Logan, no one could oppose that bizarre magic.  

At that moment, Logan felt a cold shiver run down his spine.  

If the young man really met such an end, who then wrote this account?  

The continuation of the text immediately validated that chilling premonition.  

“Umm…”  

Logan let out a low hum, momentarily averting his gaze from the booklet.  

Since reincarnating, some vague sense of unease, a feeling he had barely acknowledged, invaded his thoughts once again.  

Was all of this merely an illusion?  

If I died, would everything restart again?  

Was the struggle he was engaged in nothing more than a meaningless thrash borne from the primitive fear of being powerless?  

The booklet left behind by an unknown author seemed to manifest Logan’s anxiety into written form.  

“The fact that the magic of the Cassel Tower didn’t work…”  

It was a story that could not be easily dismissed.  

Logan temporarily calmed his mind with deep breaths before picking up the booklet again.  

Sure enough, the following content mirrored his thoughts.  

The young man failed to pull himself from the despair and feeling of loss.  

Eventually, he pondered the root cause.  

Why did he keep reincarnating?  

What was the cause of this bizarre situation?  

The young man sought out a wise man of the world to ask for guidance.  

He wished to discover the truth hidden behind his reincarnations.  

Yet, his doubts were far from resolution.  

His quest for truth continued, and eventually, after traversing deep into the southern wilderness, he encountered the wise man of the dragon tribe dwelling in seclusion.  

From this wise man, he received words that penetrated deeply into his heart.  

The young man, unable to comprehend, bowed down and sought to learn.  

Watching him, the wise man of the dragon tribe clicked his tongue in pity.  

First death.  

When the city fell, the warrior who fought until the end was none other than him.  

Hundreds of thousands of residents of the city had perished, staring at him until their last breath.  

Such was their longing.  

Second death.  

Those sacrificed to the descendants of Zibrick Cassel.  

The grievances and desires of tens of thousands of people.  

For the young man who was tormented by the emptiness brought by reincarnation, it was a shock that left his spirit in a haze.  

“Urgh!?”  

At that point, Logan felt a wave of goosebumps rise across his body.  

The desires carried, the resentment borne.  

Something flashed in his mind.  

Mountains of corpses piled high.  

This was not merely a metaphor; it was a heap of bodies composed mainly of the survivors of Grandia.  

Not in the thousands or tens of thousands, but in the hundreds of thousands, a pile of corpses exceeded that number.  

And within that mass, the one fighting against the empire and the emperor was him alone.  

With that realization, every piece fell perfectly into place.  

‘Zibrick Cassel claimed that he resurrected me with divine intervention…’  

More than those words, this record felt more credible.  

No, he wished to believe it.  

‘The power of golden desire. Yes, my ancestors did not understand my Force. That’s right.’  

With trembling hands, Logan continued reading the booklet.  

The words of the wise man rejuvenated the tired soul of the young man.  

What he added afterward was unimportant.  

It was enough for the young man to have that truth proven.  

“Ha…”  

Logan let out a sigh of relief.  

Miracles shouldn’t repeat; otherwise, they wouldn’t be miracles.  

Realizing that his reincarnation was not merely a mechanic of fate brought him immense solace.  

It appeared the author of this book felt the same way.  

However, he seemed to have come to that realization far too late.  

According to the memories of his previous life, he had met the wise man of the dragon tribe after the city had already perished.  

Having realized too late and feeling regret, the young man hastened back home.  

Focusing solely on the fact that he still had things to protect.  

Fortunately, he managed to catch the timing just right.  

The desire that first prompted his reincarnation, the battle for the city, was unfolding slightly later than before, yet in a slightly altered manner.  

However, bewildering changes were taking place.  

Those who had gone missing, no—they were being abducted.  

They were followers of the Magic Spear, Zibrick Cassel.  

They argued that they needed to consolidate the forces of humanity to bring forth the protector of mankind, Zibrick Cassel, back into this world.  

I was ignorant and knew not what they spoke of.  

Yet observing the bewildered Arch Mages around sparked doubts about their sanity.  

The descendants of Zibrick Cassel, whom Logan had deemed mere lunatics, turned out to be quite powerful.  

Once he regained his senses, he discovered that all the leaders of the Alliance had become adversaries.  

Despite his best efforts, he could only meet an unjust end.  

And then, I awoke once more in my childhood.  

Resentment? Vengeance? Such trivial feelings paled in comparison to the emptiness I faced.  

Why was my life repeatedly on a loop?  

If this cycle continued, what significance did my ongoing struggle hold?  

I, in my ignorance, could not comprehend. Thus, I began to wander, having departed from my tribe.  

Most wise men scornfully lashed out, claiming it to be mere ridicule.  

The Arch Mage I once found could only assert such feats were impossible by any magic. However, I did not give up.  

– That was what sent you back to the past. The last warrior who fought until the end.  

– Of course, those who’ve experienced it twice shall be rare. Kheh.  

My life was never futile.  

– Yet there is still time. The power of desire, that golden essence, still residing in you signifies that the grievances held by those looking upon you haven’t vanished yet.  

In my absence, they were present.  

The black serpents, the descendants of Zibrick Cassel.  

They were fighting against the tribes to protect my homeland.  

I was dim-witted and couldn’t sense mana.  

Thus, I lacked the courage to even attempt to learn magic—the strongest might of this world.  

To me, the Force represented a potential that those without talent could wield.  

So, I mistakenly believed common people could learn the Force just as easily as I did.  

Yet that notion was a misguided illusion.  

When I achieved the feats I had not in my previous life, I thought I had completed everything.  

An arrogant assumption.  

– Let’s rebuild the Empire of Man once more.  

– To ensure we remain unyielding against any provocation from all races.  

The gradually dwindling power of Mana—the dwindling influence was substantial.  

Monsters were seemingly moving further south while mixed-race tribes, sensitive to Mana than humanity, exhibited similar movements.  

While the progress was slow, one day all mixed-race tribes would completely relocate to the south or perhaps even beyond…  

Considering that supposition, the Alliance expanded its base northward.  

Inevitably, the north began to resemble a dominion for humanity.  

Yet, amidst it all, an unforeseen complication arose.  

The count of missing persons began to rise within the jurisdiction of the Alliance.  

The unjustly ascended Imugi, the wicked serpent.  

The leader symbolizing that mythical being called himself “The Snake Who Swallowed the Truth.”  

And he raved insane remarks.  

– We are the only ones who know the truth of the world.  

– This is the singular path to save humanity.  

– It is not enough yet. We need more humans! Sacrifice them!  

Initially, some leaders of the Alliance believed betrayal was in play.  

However, upon seeing their expressions, Logan realized it wasn’t an independent intention.  

The descendants of Zibrick Cassel.  

They manipulated human minds and summoned monsters from other dimensions.  

The sole fortunate aspect was that, for reasons unknown, their magic didn’t work on him.  

– God? Don’t make me laugh. If they are creators, then divinities born afterward are merely higher-dimensional forms of life.  

Well, they might be quite powerful, but they cannot interfere with time.  

Does that mean it’s utterly impossible?  

No, it’s feasible.  

– But even they require divine power, or rather the beliefs of sentient beings. Do you understand what that means?  

– It’s the grievances of sentient beings. It’s the miracle created from the innocent desires of the wronged.  

– The souls of the wronged coalesced into the sole hope that is you.  

– But what are you doing here?  

In an instant, my mind became blank.  

In that moment, the wise man of the dragon tribe once again elaborated.  

– They, too, yearned for vengeance. They trusted you, the one who fought till the end.  

– What? Meaningless reincarnation? You speak empty words because you cannot comprehend the immense grievance burdened upon your shoulders!  

Ergh, humanity…  

He stated that those like me had existed occasionally in ancient times. During the age when all races were close to the heavens, there weren’t many, but it happened from time to time.  

Such beings were referred to as ‘Those Who Change Destiny,’ and ‘The Power of Golden Desire’ that resided within me was cited as evidence.  

He also mentioned that the longer time passed, the rarer beings like me would become.  

As we drift away from the mythic era, the power required for reincarnation and the scale of grievances would amplify.  

Thus, for another like me to emerge, the scale of sacrifices unimaginable in today’s era would be necessary.  

In that moment, many things flashed through my mind.  

The family and friends who had wept and laughed with me.  

The tribespeople who supported me.  

And the laughter of the people as the steadily growing village turned into a town and then a city.  

They were all me.  

Every one of those hopes and expectations had sustained me.  

Yet now, after only two deaths and reincarnations, I believed that all of that was mere illusion and fled.



-chapter 352-

“I underestimated the Beast Realm too much.”

It was due to complacency. 

Logan had never imagined that he would find himself in such dire straits when he entered the Beast Realm, letting out wild screams for the insane Gile’s performance. 

No matter how strong the beasts were, now that he had reached the pinnacle of Aura Users, what trouble could he possibly face? 

Even if they were fierce beasts, he thought there would be no problem in protecting himself. 

He thought so. 

He completely forgot that the Beast Realm was notorious for devouring the entire army of the mightiest kingdom in the northern continent a long time ago. 

As a result, Logan was forced to confront a scene where the beasts of the Beast Realm, who were all tense from his powerful roar, swarmed in to eliminate this new competitor(?). 

It was the moment when Logan had just dispatched over ten two-headed monkeys. 

Something massive came rushing through the dazzling golden light generated by his Aura. 

Rumblings filled the air. 

As it charged, knocking down several gigantic trees, light began to stream into the dark forest, revealing its terrifying appearance. 

At first glance, it seemed to be a gigantic wild boar. 

However, its tusks, towering nearly 1 meter, and sharp silver-gray horns sprouting from its head to tail added to its impressiveness. Additionally, dark ominous energy swirled from its entire body. 

“Guueeeee!” 

Thud thud thud. 

The enormous wild boar thundered toward him, shaking the ground. 

It was undoubtedly a threatening sight, but Logan was feeling frustration rather than fear.  

‘Why are these things…?’  

How many hours had it been? 

He had clearly heard that beasts fought amongst themselves, yet, for some reason, these creatures were solely targeting him. 

“Guueeeee!”

“Shut up!!”

The golden Aura filled with irritation and anger spun fiercely in response. 

As the Aura gathered and compressed, it shot forth in a straight line like a spear, curving diagonally to pierce into the side of the charging boar. 

The “Devil Spear,” an application combined with the technique demonstrated by Greet Ainshein. 

The raging boar attempted to skillfully alter its course, but Logan had already leaped forward and deeply slashed its nape directly. 

Its massive tusks, sharp horns, and even its tough skin fell apart before the authority of destruction wielded by Logan’s Aura. 

“GUUEEEEK!!!”

Boom! 

When Logan landed back on the ground, the wild boar collapsed with a screaming howl that felt like it could rupture eardrums. 

Splash! 

Thick blood gushed forth from the nape, which had been sliced more than halfway through, bursting forth like a fountain. 

“Now, come at me! I will wipe you all out!”

His booming voice echoed. 

A superhuman who had completely abandoned the idea of hiding now scattered murderous intent in all directions. 

Was that the right choice? 

Or was it the sudden light that poured down between the trees felled by the monstrous boar? 

The attacks that had continued for hours abruptly stopped, leaving the forest silent as if nothing had happened. 

“…Huh?”

Startled by the unexpected situation, Logan finally recalled another saying about the Beast Realm. 

– Beasts don’t step back even before strong threats, but if one defeats the master of a specific territory within that territory, they won’t engage with the victor anymore. 

Logan, exhausted from the hours of constant fighting, could finally breathe a sigh of relief as the ceaseless assaults came to an end. 

But it was a misjudgment. 

Crack!  

Suddenly, the sound of something breaking echoed as a tree fell toward him from the side. 

Instinctively heading backward, Logan realized another tree was coming down toward him at an incredible speed. 

‘Eek!?’

Logan barely registered that the massive tree formed like a club was aiming directly for him. 

In his mind, a tree was no bigger than an arm; however, this tree had a girth of several dozen meters. 

Boom! 

Boom! 

The ground shook violently where the massive club splintered down. 

And at that moment, Logan finally grasped the cause of this upheaval. 

– Kyaaaah!!! 

The noise hit his ears, causing him to briefly lose his sense of balance. 

In the midst of his disorientation, a creature too large to comprehend lurked beneath his darkened vision. 

While it resembled humanoid form, it had to be about 20 meters tall. 

Muscles that looked filled to the brim peaked from its body. 

Leaves, vines—who knew whether they were from plants or bushes—guarding its vital spots made this creature look like a primitive tribal being, but it was a monster with two heads. 

Logan, astonished by the tremendous figure, recalled a familiar name. 

Ancient monsters rare on the continent, among them the fearsome creatures called ogres. 

‘An ogre? One with two heads?’ 

It was far larger than the legends depicted, and its two heads made this creature unforgettable. 

Fortunately for Logan, when he stumbled unexpectedly and presented an opening, the beast did not immediately attack. 

“Kyaaa?” 

“Growl.” 

The two heads seemed to converse in a strange manner, tilting their heads before bending down and reaching out toward Logan. 

Not swinging the enormous club that could be taller than a tower. 

‘Huh?’ 

As if to pick up something that had fallen to the ground. 

Logan took note of the certainty in its pose that seemed to suggest he would not be able to evade. 

That was peculiar, but Logan had no obligation to act as it expected. 

Zwhoop! 

“!!?” 

“Rawr?” 

An enormous hand that could encompass a person comfortably. As if to ignore the flesh and blood of the being in front of it, its thick finger was sliced off, with Logan leaping up along the monster’s arm. 

“Croaarrr!” 

“Gargh!” 

The delayed moment of pain caused the beast to unleash a roar of anger, but by then, Logan had already leaped into the air, swinging his Aura-infused weapon downward, ready to unleash the power of destructive golden energy. 

Gazing into the bewilderment and fear reflected in the enormous sets of eyes, Logan felt a surge of confidence in yet another victory. 

Then suddenly. 

“Rawr!!” 

In an instant, the eyes of one head turned completely black, and with incomprehensible voice, emanated an unusual wave all around. 

The wave rushed forth and abruptly halted Logan’s whipping Aura right in front of the creature. 

Boom! 

“Dammit!” 

In an instant, he found himself floating like a bird in mid-air. 

While disappointedly clucking his tongue, Logan gazed down as the gigantic club descended to smash the ground below. 

Mana and magic? He couldn’t still sense any of them. But the overwhelming weight and size posed a terrifying threat. 

‘Damn it.’ 

At that moment, he lamented the absence of his Wind God’s Boots left back in Grandpea due to Gairo’s disguise. 

Logan’s weapon sliced forward in precise lines, creating a golden circle of power surrounding him. 

Swoosh! 

The monstrous club swished past Logan’s body without noise. 

No, specifically, a segment of the club that had met Logan’s position was entirely erased from existence. 

As if a part of space had been excised. 

When that massive club struck the ground below. 

Boom! 

Rumble! 

A shockwave rattled the earth yet again. 

And at the same time, the club crumbled to bits, unable to withstand the force, scattering debris in all directions. 

Within the storm of debris, Logan bounded from the side, darting back toward the creature’s head above. 

“Rawr?”

“Rok!?” 

Again, showing shock and confusion, the beast’s eyes widened, but Logan shared the same irritation. 

‘Damn it.’ 

Suddenly, his power seemed to vanish by a third, leaving him feeling drained. 

He had sought to avoid using Heavenly Piercing as much as possible to conserve energy, but this strategy allowed unexpected retaliation from the beast. 

He could no longer afford to waste a chance to finish it off decisively. 

“Die!”

“Rawr!” 

“Croar!” 

The familiar black wave rushed against Logan once again, but the power of Heavenly Piercing that cleaved through space remained unyielding to such waves. 

No, it had to be. 

But… 

Click! 

Surprisingly, that black wave withstood the attack for just a moment. 

Swoosh! 

“Kreeeeek!!” 

In the end, it was intended to sever two heads rather than just one, but only one name remained as the final victim. 

‘Shit!’ 

However, it was undoubtedly a severe injury. 

Perhaps it might even lead to incapacitation. 

In the fleeting moment, countless thoughts stormed through Logan’s mind, ignited by the vague anxiety that had surged from that singular remaining head. 

“Croar!” 

A roar erupted from the beast, seemingly filled with a powerful resonance that would burst eardrums. 

As Logan’s vision blurred for a brief second, he saw the other severed head rolling on the ground. 

The monster’s entire body turned crimson—all red! 

‘Rampage!?’ 

The phenomenon where an injured monster unleashes a burst of power! 

Logan clearly understood that such an event could easily occur even in a common monster still living today. 

As he landed, Logan swiftly stepped onto the trunk of a neighboring tree and began leaping away to a place beyond reach. 

‘There’s no need to engage now. Just wait for it to collapse.’ 

He didn’t need to confront a beast with such bloodlust head-on. 

“Croar!” 

His prediction seemed to pay off, as behind him the monster unleashed a cacophony of fiery roars—intimidating sounds of destruction rumbled as trees began to shatter and fall around them. 

Just like that, Logan leapt from tree to tree, finally reaching the highest branches above. 

Rumble! 

“Croar—!” 

As he watched the tempest of destruction unfold below, Logan let out a sigh of relief, but suddenly he felt a killing intent that sent shivers down his spine. 

‘Above!?’

When he looked up in shock, the silhouette of the descending monster was cast down below as the area darkened. 

Three heads stretching from a lizard-like torso. A body three times the size of its torso. Wings massive and sharp protruding like a spear. 

Aside from its utterly crazed eyes, it resembled the legendary formidable creature known as a dragon. 

‘A Drake?’ 

If the ogre was the mightiest monster on the land, then drakes were the ultimate monsters of the sky. 

But he had never heard of a three-headed Drake before. 

Before Logan had time to be surprised, the gigantic Drake exhaled flames. 

Fwhaaaaaa! 

Flames erupted from all three heads, enveloping dozens of meters in radius. 

“This fucking hell!!!!” 

Logan, wrapped in his golden Aura, soared toward the air. 

Whoosh! 

But awaiting him was the gigantic club swinging downwards with fierce momentum. 

‘Damn it.’ 

How he wished he had the Wind God’s Boots. 

It was in that moment of longing for items he risked entangling in the Gairo disguise that he unleashed Heavenly Piercing once more. 

Slash! 

“Kyaaaah!” 

The tail of the Drake was severed like a lie. 

As a shower of monster blood and flesh rained down, Logan plunged toward the ground. 

Having demonstrated the best of his abilities consecutively, his power had now dwindled dangerously low. 

Clenching his teeth, Logan extended his whip blade to grab the tree trunk beside him. 

But then— 

Rumble! 

The ground rumbled as if an earthquake had struck, and suddenly his vision turned completely obscure. 

As he regained his senses, red filled his field of vision. 

At that moment, his eyes caught a glimpse of a colossal monstrous maw, whose size was beyond imagination. 

‘Shit, I’m inside a freaking gigantic serpent’s mouth!’



-chapter 356-

“Vision of the Divine Sword…”

A groan escaped involuntarily.

Upon reflection, the cover of the vision he received appeared particularly worn. It wouldn’t have surprised him if a letter or two had been erased.

However, he couldn’t help but wonder how such an ancient being could have anticipated this situation.

Fortunately, the answer to that question followed immediately.

As with every prophecy, Talon’s words were always vague, suggesting that both interpretations might hold some truth. Nevertheless, the best-case scenario, as far as Logan was concerned, was that no one else was looking at this book.

“Ah…!”

A sigh slipped from Logan’s lips.

His brows furrowed tighter.

The ancient superhuman who originated the Vision of the Divine Sword had not mentioned his name in the book. Instead, the name that frequently arose since the conflict with the Cassel Tower was that of Talon “Ares,” a friend of the author.

What troubled him more than the anecdotes related to that figure was the surname itself.

‘I hope it’s just a coincidence…’

Despite the creeping anxiety, Logan could not tear his eyes away from the book.

“Huh…?”

“Could it be… the very first knight of humanity?”

Logan read on, both amazed and apprehensive.

It seemed like an answer to the current situation was about to emerge.

However, the next words only compounded his unease, as they expressed sentiments that were incomprehensible to him.

And then, that anxiety revealed its true nature.

“Magical power…?”

Currently, it’s nearly impossible to find any records of the so-called Divine Sorcerer. Yet, if it’s related to a calendar named after that individual, it would be impossible to deduce just how far back that history stretches.

All he knew was that it predated the Great Migration by a considerable margin.

He couldn’t help but exhale in exasperation, and the following content was even more stunning.

The ‘willpower’ mentioned by the author seemed to imply that it was not merely about inheritance of intent. Logan felt awe once more as he concentrated on the writings.

He had seen enough of the misdeeds of the Cassel Tower in his previous life.

Nevertheless, one question persisted.

“Allocation?”

Logan looked around, bewildered; all he saw were plain gray bricks and a massive wolf.

Could it be that the undamaged bricks of the ruins indicated a legacy?

Or perhaps…

‘Could it be that guy?’

“Grrr…”

As Logan glanced at the wolf that suddenly turned towards him, it frowned, seemingly asking why he was staring.

It looked as if it held no fondness for him at all.

Feeling a sense of disbelief, Logan shifted his gaze back to the book.

“A little puppy?”

Logan regarded the wolf with incredulity.

The image he recalled before losing consciousness was of a colossal monster, but the creature before him was at least as large as an ordinary bull.

‘Could it be that in ancient times, this was considered small?’

That seemed improbable.

“Geez…”

“Rawr!”

The wolf must have sensed his gaze, as it shot him a stern look before growling.

Just by observing that, he knew something was amiss. Above all, the overwhelming power and roar that drove away the beasts of the mountains could never belong to a mere young divine beast.

‘If that were a young divine beast, then all the divine beasts from myth would have run amok…’

Even if the depictions of divine beasts passed down through legends were entirely accurate, unleashing such prowess from their youngest stage was impossible. Even the most renowned breed among divine beasts, the ‘Dragons,’ were at a disadvantage in their juvenile stages.

And as he continued reading, Logan found his thoughts validated.

“It seems… it may already be too late.”

Being weak against demonic energy was absurd, to say the least.

The twelve red eyes glimmering from the three heads. Furthermore, the currents of crimson energy pulsing before his eyes remained vivid in his memory.

That creature was already a fully matured divine beast, or rather…

‘A demonic beast…’

Considering the form he had seen right before fainting, that beast seemed to possess an aura of regality.

“Hmm…?”

As he reached that realization, another divine beast’s myth came to mind.

How long did it take for a divine beast to mature from juvenile to adult?

Wasn’t it a minimum of several hundred years?

A cold sweat trickled down his back.

And, just as expected, the following content served to corroborate that grim speculation.

Though the description of the realm was a bit vague, it likely referred to ‘Aura Master.’ In other words, it implied it was from an era as ancient as its reference.

Putting that aside…

“Essence, huh? Where on earth…?”

There was no sign of the essence that an ancient transcendent allegedly derived from life force.

As he lamented this, he noticed the wolf, which had only been scowling at him, now slowly turning its head away.

”You can’t be!?”

Logan grimaced, and the wolf turned away even further.

“Did you eat it?”

“…Grrr.”

It apathetically wiped its nose with its paw, pretending to doze off, as if it had a mind of its own.

It seemed to understand the inquiry perfectly.

This absurd scene left Logan letting out a long sigh.

“Ha…”

The ominous premonitions he’d had from the beginning were gradually becoming reality.

In haste, Logan flipped the pages backward.

What met him was indeed a genuine Vision of Force described in detail.

“…It’s just like mine.”

Whether it was misfortune or fortune, it seemed he had learned a complete version of the Vision of the Divine Sword, or rather, the ‘Vision of Sacrifice’.

The methods regarding form and manipulation were slightly altered, possessing their own merits and faults; however, overall, the version he had learned felt like a refined form polished by subsequent generations.

Even while sighing, Logan flipped through the previous pages, hoping there might be something additional.

Though there were alluring phrases within, all he could do was exhale in resignation.

“That millennium has already passed…”

As he imagined the passage of time, Logan felt a sense of emptiness flooding him.

Once more, he examined the map sketched on the next page, but after numerous years had elapsed, it was nearly unrecognizable.

The map of the ruins, allegedly created by the ancient archmage, held little significance.

However, he was able to trace the location he had visited once, the ruins of Zibrick Cassel. Following the flow of the great river slicing through the Crown Mountain Range eventually led to a city anyone in the present continent would recognize.

“…Aserian. Just as I thought, damn it!”

Truly, every bad omen had sadly come true.

“Talon ‘Ares’… Damn it!”

The room reverberated with his frustrated exclamation, causing the drowsy wolf, Tyr, to jerk awake.

“Grrr.”

Tyr frowned at Logan.

However, this time around, Logan did not back down.

“…I’m feeling an injustice, you know. Do you think you could possibly spit up what you swallowed?”

While he had fainted, he had no idea what it was that the wolf had consumed, but it seemed filled with vitality.

Given its current perfect state, it seemed sufficient to at least contend against the transformation he had previously witnessed.

Still, the beast didn’t appear willing to relent easily.

“Grrr.”

Perceiving Logan’s intent as real, Tyr began to grow larger, his fur taking on a dark red hue. Before long, two more eyes appeared atop an otherwise standard wolf head, and four crimson orbs glinted keenly.

It seemed quite serious about having a proper fight.

Logan, hit with such absurdity, even lost his fighting spirit.

“Okay, I get it. You’re still just a guardian, after all. Sigh.”

Logan sighed and slumped down on the altar, which prompted Tyr to tilt his head curiously before resuming its original form.

Now resembling nothing more than a very large ordinary wolf, Logan couldn’t help but feel annoyed at it.

“Why are you so riled up? Have I done anything wrong to you?”

As he shot the wolf his retort, it abruptly turned its head and scratched at something with its claws.

Upon investigation, it appeared to be fragments of some animal’s bones.

The remnants were so worn down that estimating their original shape was practically impossible. The small piece that Tyr had unearthed crumbled into powder almost instantly.

Seeing that, Logan began to understand what the wolf might be implying.

“…Has too much time passed? Was I late?”

A nod in return.

Who could he blame for this?

The master of prophecy? Or perhaps the one who made the prophecy?

Clearly, the beast that had consumed its master’s essence yet had now become a demonic beast appeared to blame Logan for arriving so late.

“At this rate…”

Sigh.

Looking dejectedly, he felt a deep sense of disappointment in himself.

After expecting great things, it seemed he had unwittingly missed the mark.

“Well, saving my life is something, right? I guess I was merely too greedy.”

As Logan consoled himself, the now near Tyr approached and playfully nudged his massive snout at Logan’s chest.

“Hmm?”

“Grrr!”

It appeared to be protesting as if to demand why he hadn’t gained anything despite being there.

However, a bull-sized wolf that could transform into a mighty demonic beast could not simply be brought into human society.

Yet why was he feeling hopeful?

As if guided by an inexplicable certainty, Logan suddenly asked, “Can you perhaps shrink?”

“Yeeow?”

It seemed to blink, astonished by the question.

It was far from surprising that the wolf’s various emotions were laid bare upon its face; this was no longer astonishing to Logan.

“If so, I could bring you along. But let’s also promise you won’t grow too huge recklessly…”

“Keee!”

Tyr seemed to combust with contemplation, its front paw clamping tightly over its head.

‘Could it genuinely be possible?’

As Logan stared in anticipation, suddenly…

Woosh!

A gentle light burst forth, and Tyr’s enormous size dramatically reduced.

Now it was no larger than a typical dog.

“Grrr!”

Was that a mark of satisfaction?

Logan, understanding its bark now, broke into a relieved smile.

Not long after, within the depths of the demonic forest ruins, a person and a wolf(?) swiftly exited, darting southward.

Meanwhile, at that precise moment when Logan encountered the ancient history within the demon’s forest, within the heart of what could be called the continent’s hub, the ruler of that land began to make his move.

While Talon spoke of a far-off future, what was certain was that the event was unfolding; he had no choice but to prepare for this arrangement. After all, his predictions had held a remarkably high accuracy rate.

Currently, it was the year 243 of the Magical Calendar, the thirteenth month since the Sorcerer declared the empire. Armed with this information, calculating and aligning the historical clock would be integral.

…Bring forth the arrangements I have left behind, disrupt their cadence, and obliterate the manifested Sorcerer. They are nothing but parasites in human affairs, so no hesitation is warranted against them.

To forge a relic that has become increasingly rare since the era of myth, that I have constructed with the ‘Demon Slaying Stone,’ infusing it with a portion of the essence drawn from Talon’s magic to weave a dimensional barrier. Within that barrier rests ‘Tyr’, an offspring of the ancient divine beasts, whom I acquired in my later years. And seize the essence sustaining the barrier.

While I could not ascertain your level of mastery, should you still be unable to manipulate space fluidly or interfere with souls, it will surely help bolster your strength significantly.

Though the odds of success may well be slim, if the person has mastered the Vision of Sacrifice, the method exists in the latter pages of this booklet. Those who have acquired the power of aspiration will learn faster as well.

And…

The existence of someone reading this conveys the breaking of the ruins’ barrier and, in turn, signifies that my aspiration’s disciples and descendants, those of the Sword God lineage, faced extinction.

What worries me more than anything is the unpredictability of when my prophecy may unfold. When that peculiar figure first encountered me years ago, they ominously prophesized, “The first knight.”

At that time, the term knight had yet to exist, so both the speaker and the listener dismissed it as nonsense. But thirty years later, everyone who knew me began referring to me as such.

While the term knight, which denoted someone protecting others with a sword, has come to be honored near my later years, its inception was quite amusing. People mistook me, who wielded the sword and Aura, as a mere sorcerer’s underling (Kniht) and altered the name to knight (Knight).

Regardless, I personally preferred the title of “first knight” far more than the later-bestowed label of Sword God. Although those around me had begun to resent the now-common usage of knights.

Anyway, while Talon spoke of a distant future, I could not ascertain when the era of the reader would unfold. For that reason, I set my own arrangements, just as Talon took his path.

Merely hoping, I wished for this to remain undiscovered, but should discovery occur, I only hoped it wouldn’t be too late.

To reiterate, if the barrier has breached, it signifies the severing of my wishes through my successors, then the one gazing upon this book would either possess the chance of ‘Vision of Sacrifice’ or have otherwise gained the power of aspiration.

Above all, it is my wish that my descendants fulfill their duties and thus allow their aspirations to wane. If that were the case, the power passed on through Talon would also fall to nothingness. But if not…

Talon had foretold of the divine lineage’s obliteration. Thus, the young and clever friend, Tyr, agreed to be sealed, intending to preserve the bloodline far in the future.

Though what troubles me about this sealing was the fact that it resided in a demonic forest since divine beasts are weak against demonic energy; should it be discovered, please swiftly bring him out of the ruins. Even a young divine beast, being able to perceive the flow of souls and understand human language, will serve as a grand asset.

Once you have gathered Tyr and the essence, depart the ruins. Then, seek out the remnants of Talon left upon the Central Continent. He too had prepared another arrangement for you, and the location is sketched in the next chapter. 

What he left behind was his treasure. Therefore, what lies within his ruins is known only to him. I merely hold the conviction it will assist against Talon’s eventual arrival.

Talon had sworn not just to himself, but vowed that his line would carry onward to maintain and safeguard the ruins. The great archmage’s oath would surely endure for a millennium.



-chapter 353-

“Damn it!”

Logan had no desire to gaze upon the monstrous snake’s insides, which were beyond his imagination.  

At that moment, he activated the ability he had saved for the absolute final moment.  

The Force Core of his heart expelled the ninth core, and golden light poured forth from his red eyes.  

At that instant, he felt his soul surge in elevation, bringing with it a clear understanding of the entire structure of the monstrous snake that was engulfing him, along with the surrounding environment.  

The Force, which had been depleted, began to rise beyond its limits.  

With a thrilling sensation of his soul heightened, a massive power began to flow within his body.  

Despite having used this ability countless times before, it felt strangely unfamiliar, transforming on a dimension entirely different from anything he had experienced until now.  

Through the act of piercing the heavens, he realized and fully grasped the ‘ability to interfere with space.’  

He felt certain that he could now wield that tremendous power as effortlessly as breathing.  

Moreover, the confidence arose that he could even slice through that which did not exist.  

And that meant…

‘Aura Master.’  

It indicated that he had briefly stepped into a legendary realm.  

Rumble.  

The space vibrated simply from focusing strength into his hand.  

He could vividly feel the power of the Force, born from his own vitality, dominating all surrounding space.  

While he wanted to savor that omnipotence and inscribe it upon his soul, now was not the time.  

– Gurururr.  

In the gullet of the monstrous snake, the sickening red walls writhed.  

First and foremost, he needed to escape this annoying space.  

Swoosh.

Logan’s sword, swung lightly.  

Immediately afterward, following its trajectory, a massive chunk of flesh was cleaved apart, and sunlight shone through as if mocking.  

– Kyaoo!  

A scream from a creature above, yet it felt so distant, as if heard from the sky.

‘Now, about three minutes.’  

Though his body brimmed with energy, his mind raced frantically.  

He needed to find a place to rest before his stamina gave out.  

In this zone filled with monsters.

Aura Master.  

That legendary realm capable of controlling space even with little power was manifested right at the heart of this desolate monster territory.  

Yet suddenly.

Kraaaaang!

For a brief moment, the enormous three-headed wolf stared him down.  

Then—  

Swish-swish.  

The overwhelming presence of the creature diminished before his eyes, revealing a silver wolf about the size of a calf.

For some reason, the wolf’s howl carried a strange resonance in Logan’s ears.  

‘Is it telling me to follow?’  

He chuckled at that thought, but the wolf, having glanced at him, promptly turned its head and began to move somewhere.  

The nobility and arrogance of the creature suited it unbelievably well.  

Logan stared at it in a daze before he hastily followed after it.  

‘The strength is…’  

Though the high spirit from earlier began to wane, and the Force ebbed away, the duration of his ability’s upkeep was drawing to a close.  

He had no choice but to trust this uncertain intuition now.  

As if voicing his thoughts, Logan landed on the ground, and his exhausted body called for his dues faster than he had anticipated.  

“Ugh!”  

He gasped, feeling his strength wash away like the receding tide, along with a constricting sensation in his soul.   

With that painful groan, Logan crumpled to the ground, and through a foggy consciousness, he caught sight of approaching crimson eyes.  

‘No, don’t. Damn it.’  

Is this how I die?  

It was an absurdity he could never have imagined.  

Then at that moment.  

– Aowwwww!  

The wolf’s howl echoed again as the crimson eyes surrounding him suddenly gasped, frightened, and fled.  

That was the last memory Logan retained from that day.

Thump.  

“Ugh…”  

Thump.  

“Mm…”  

Thump.  

“…Logan. Just a bit more…”  

A faint memory flickered within him.  

Logan tried to push away the hand that roused him, smiling.  

‘Fur?’  

However, the sensation that brushed across his hand felt a bit strange.  

As he thought it felt quite fuzzy like a beast’s paw, suddenly—  

Bam!  

“Ugh!”  

Logan found himself tumbling over the stone floor, head spinning.  

With the cool touch awakening clarity, Logan shot up in bewilderment.  

“Who are you?!”

He swiftly readied himself, drawing his sword, only to be met with a silver wolf, calf-sized, glaring at him with a displeased expression.  

It was astounding in itself that the wolf stared him down, giving off an air of frustration, yet strangely he felt no sense of discomfort.  

Perhaps it was because Logan was late to connect the dots.  

This was none other than the creature that had saved him before he lost consciousness.  

“Wait…”  

Logan did not question why the wolf had been so rough in waking him.  

However, speaking to the wolf seemed odd.  

“…Grrr.”  

After a moment of indecision, Logan could only furrow his brow as the wolf suddenly let out a huff and turned away, striding deeper into the cold stone chamber.  

‘Stone chamber?’  

Realizing where he was at long last, Logan hastily checked his surroundings.  

The chamber was a hard gray stone, its ceiling rounding high above, seemingly over five meters. The floor and walls were impeccably flat, devoid of any bumps.  

That meticulous construction led him to draw deep breaths of confusion.  

‘This isn’t a Beast Realm…’  

Feeling the smooth, crafted wall with his hand briefly prompted an uneasy sensation.  

The wall did not appear to be a regular stone.  

Bang.  

He lightly clenched his fist and knocked against it, and that sensation solidified.  

He recognized this kind of material; he had encountered something similar not too long ago.  

“Ruins…?”  

The wall resembled the material that constituted the Zibrick Cassel ruins.  

An unrecognizable structure, once protected by the power of the Holy Sword and housing ancient legacies.  

‘Is this place similar to there?’  

Logan’s thoughts began aligning the pieces.  

However, he still felt something was amiss.  

With no patterns or murals lining the walls like the Zibrick ruins, this space felt distinctly smaller.  

Boom!  

“Sure enough…”  

When he unleashed a shockingly light Aura impact against the wall, his conviction solidified even more.  

Walls that displayed no damage, immune to even the powers of destruction rumored as not easily found in ancient times.  

Parked deeper within a shroud of anxiety, Logan scanned his surroundings once more, and a sharp sound came forth from a distance.  

“Woof!”  

The silver wolf had vanished around the corner of the chamber, only to return and bark, as if beckoning him forth.  

‘Shall I follow?’  

There was indeed a compelling force driving him to follow the creature that had saved him.  

Clinging to that curiosity, Logan had no choice but to tail the wolf.  

An unadorned chamber stretched before them, emptier than the previous one.  

Here, they found only a somewhat larger pedestal.  

Sitting heavily on top was a single object resembling a book.  

“Woof!”  

The wolf barked once more, translating its wish for him to approach, though its displeasure echoed in the expression.  

‘The wolf seems to convey emotions quite clearly. Am I the one changing— or is the wolf?’  

These absurdities flooded his mind, but the moment he moved toward the platform, the wolf howled impatiently.  

“Do you have a problem with me?”  

Though unsought, the peculiar situation found its way into his words.  

Yet the wolf, snorting and turning its head, appeared to convey its own understanding.  

“Grrr!”  

It barked again, as if instructing him to read.  

Encountering such a bizarre chain of events, and seeing the book written so distinctly, an intriguing smile crept upon Logan’s face.  

He stepped forward toward the platform.  

The moment he touched the cover of the leather-bound book, he pulled unexpectedly from its mystique.  

The book contained not only curious text but omitted elements that shone callback to a more ancient era, resembling fragments of words he had encountered already.  

‘It resembles the style of the ancient scripts I deciphered once…’  

Realizing that this book transcended realms of previous encounters, Logan opened it and found it was speaking the tale of a life.  

A child born frail and weak from the beginning.  

However, miraculously surviving countless diseases even amidst vulnerability as an infant.  

The child thrived, coming through trials that would have crushed others.  

And the reason lay in a force, a power gleaned from the child’s father.  

A renowned beast hunter, the father trained from experience.  

Through grueling endeavors of hunting and battling by his father’s side, the child awakened his strength.  

In a world where the hunters protected humanity from beasts, the young boy became the guardian, despite the reality that overwhelming dangers lurked around his small village.  

But calamity struck without warning.  

The boy, now a warrior, fought fiercely, continuously protecting his people against the invasions of foreign races.  

Yet challenges piled on—invincible tribes, magic-wielding foes.  

When adversaries surmounted grew vast and powerful, even monstrous, the tiny settlement was engulfed in despair.  

The human spirit that had scarcely endured would never survive against such forces of chaos arising from beneath.  

That was remarkably his first death, the boy’s struggle echoing through the ages.  

With dragons vanished and humans beginning to rally; the return of the powerful magician’s protege sparked an unprecedented age of prosperity for mankind.  

Elves and dwarves—species that had once considered them lesser—retained their awe for that human wizard.  

Only after that prophecy of unity ignited hope for the wanderers—those fleeting from the clutches of monsters, tended by the land as stability blossomed anew.  

Logan began to realize the depths of the accusations and reflections he had encountered, leading to his next transformation…

“The Emperor has demanded either the official announcement of the annexation of the Holy Kingdom or a declaration to transfer the position of the Pope to the Emperor of the Empire.”

“What is that dog?”

Eileen, who was secretly welcoming her husband back, shifted her curiosity to the silver-furred puppy following behind Logan.  

With its unusually shining fur and sparkling eyes, its adorable appearance caught everyone’s attention.  

However, her husband’s reply was somewhat ridiculous.  

“…It’s a sort of secret weapon.”  

“A dog?”  

“Argh!”  

The puppy, Tyr, barked in irritation at being referred to merely as a dog.  

However, instead of an intimidating aura, the size that barely reached the height of a person’s knee made it appear merely cute rather than menacing.  

“Oh my, how adorable.”  

“Sniff.”  

Yet, the way Tyr turned its head with a snort as Eileen patted its head strangely seemed to convey satisfaction. 

‘It doesn’t seem solely because of the contract.’  

Recalling the agreement he made with Tyr before leaving the Demonic Forest, Logan couldn’t suppress his smile.  

Powered by the essence shared between ‘them,’ the contract was formed.  

Given that the essence took the form of its owner, which was freed from the seal, the reason Tyr had remained in the Demonic Forest until now—and that no divine beast remained in this world—seemed clear.  

The author left behind the vision of the Divine Sword, stating that the divine beast thrived on the power of aspiration, or the worship of souls. However, since the mythological era, the vitality of aspirations had rapidly diminished, and with the advancement of civilization, intellectual beings no longer venerated divine beasts.  

With those two changes accelerating, divine beasts had already been on the path of extinction even in the time of the Sword God.  

‘The end of creation, the end of the mythical age, was setup by the Creator himself so they would fulfill their role and disappear.’  

Moreover, the Sword God noted that divine beasts, being pitiful creatures bound for extinction, were worthy of care regardless of whether they brought good or harm. It seemed he hoped that if the pact was made through the inherited power of aspiration, Tyr would at least be able to live out its lifespan.  

However, the situation had gone remarkably awry.  

It was likely both the Sword God and Talon, who possessed the prophecy, had never foreseen that Tyr would consume the essence.  

In other words, Tyr no longer needed to form a contract with anyone.  

Despite that, Tyr still wished to follow Logan, even going as far as unilaterally offering to help, thus coming into the world.

And the reason was probably…  

“Do you understand my words? Wow, you really are clever.”  

“Kee!”  

Tyr nudged its head closer as Eileen affectionately stroked its head.  

Having shared the same aspiration, Tyr’s emotions unfolded to Logan from the very beginning, and even after forming an official contract, he could comprehensively read the puppy’s feelings.  

– I feel good. Warm.  

– My chest is ticklish.  

And then,  

– …I miss you.  

“Argh!”  

It reverberated with nostalgia for a far-off someone who wasn’t present here.  

The emotions from Tyr, displayed so vividly, tugged at Logan’s heart.  

“…You were lonely, huh?”  

While on the way back, he pondered if he should have stroked Tyr more.  

Reaching out with an understanding of the woeful yet warm feelings being conveyed, Logan decided to pet it alongside Eileen.  

Thud.  

“…Huh?”  

But he was stopped.  

Tyr had dodged to the side, raising a paw to reject Logan’s touch.  

…I thought you were lonely?  

“Argh.”  

It felt as if Tyr was communicating, ‘But not you.’  

Coldly turning his back to Logan, it once again rubbed its head against Eileen’s leg.  

Was it still upset?  

Logan, with his hand suspended in the air, remained frozen amidst an odd emptiness and embarrassment.  

Witnessing the scene, Eileen erupted into laughter.  

“Ahaha. Seems the pup prefers me over you.”  

“…Tyr.”  

“Yes?”  

With a light sigh, Logan smiled ruefully and continued,  

“That pup’s name is Tyr. And it’s not just a dog.”  

Logan slowly explained to his wife about the divine beast, who he hadn’t intended to be late in returning.  

“Really? That pup is that strong?”  

Eileen, upon hearing the explanation, found it hard to believe.  

It was evident why Tyr had expressed such warmth, lying contentedly atop her knee despite having previously acted so cuddly.  

“Absolutely. Even I would have difficulty claiming victory against it in a fight.”  

“Is it really that great…? My, you’re an impressive little pup.”  

As Eileen recognized that Logan wasn’t just joking, she patted Tyr’s head gently.  

In response, the physically groggy puppy buried himself deeper into her lap as if to display satisfaction.  

Logan felt a sense of bitterness realizing how much Tyr favored Eileen over himself, but soon he shifted the conversation.  

“While I’ve been gone, have there been any significant events? I did leave instructions.”  

“Any? There’s nothing but trouble while you were gone.”  

As she spoke, Eileen shot Logan a pointed glance. He felt tongue-tied with no justifiable excuse given the extended absence and pressing matters to attend.  

Fortunately, Eileen lightly sighed before she revealed the news he was eagerly waiting for.  

“Recently, two fortresses have been completed, and soon the installation of magic circles will be finished at those two places and three castles in the western front, including Kyle.”  

“Already that far…?”  

“The preparations you mentioned are nearly finished. Perhaps that’s why everyone seems to be even tenser now.”  

‘Everyone.’ It likely referred to the aides who knew the Empire’s invasion was looming ominously ahead.  

Not to mention Eileen’s expression subtly displayed slight tension alongside her joy at seeing Logan again.  

Hoo.  

Feeling the heightened anxiety passed onto him, making his heart race, Logan drew a deep breath before embracing his long-separated partner.  

“Don’t worry. Everything will be alright.”  

“Of course. It needs to go well.”  

While feeling supported by the affectionate touch of his wife’s hand on his back, Logan was met with an unexpected remark from her.  

“I’ve been alone at home for months.”  

Puhah.  

Logan burst into laughter at Eileen’s sudden joke.  

“Ahahaha.”  

“Argh!”  

Tyr, woken by the sudden commotion, groaned, causing laughter to continue echoing deep within the palace.  

* * *  

Just a few days after Logan secretly returned to the palace, the knight Viktor, who had disappeared around the same time, appeared at the royal castle soaked in sweat.  

“Open the door!”  

“Yes!? Is that you, Sir Viktor?”  

“Yes!”  

As the guards confirmed his identity, Viktor sighed deeply after catching sight of the fallen horse.  

He had initially felt sympathy for the collapsing steed, but as the circumstances compounded in rapid succession, that sense dulled.  

The results of the countless lives sacrificed and their indefatigable vitality served to forge a miracle spanning the continent in just fifteen days.  

The only side effect was the ten-kilogram drop in his weight; therefore no one would believe him even if he spoke about it.  

‘Damn!’  

But the one responsible for that miracle merely worried about the safety of the Saint and the unfolding events in the Holy Kingdom.  

Moreover, he couldn’t shake off his deep sense of helplessness to act in the entire process.  

His mind kept returning to the phenomenal power showcased by the Holy Sword a month prior.  

The ones bound to be heading towards the Holy Capital right now.

The guilt only deepened as he thought.  

“Your Majesty?”  

“Yes?”

“Of course. It’s during work hours.”  

The knight’s inquiry carried the unspoken question of why he even bothered asking.  

Only then did Viktor realize his urgency—he was indeed agitated.  

“Sir Viktor, please enter.”  

But the moment another knight’s voice rang out, he couldn’t remain composed and bolted towards the inner chamber.  

During that trek, he unexpectedly encountered familiar and unfriendly faces alike.  

“Viktor?”  

“Oh, Sir Viktor! Where have you been in such a hurry?”  

His friends, Ronian and the rival, Louisa von Aserian, walked next to each other, sharing an overly odd sight that greeted Viktor.                      

The perception was uncannily reminiscent of lovers.  

How precisely that scene could be understood was baffling; however, Viktor found little time to question it now.  

“It’s nothing you need concern yourself about.”  

While he might not feel this way if it were solely Ronian, he couldn’t utter every detail in front of Louisa.  

As Viktor tried to move past them, Louisa remarked with a curious expression,  

“If you’re sweating this much, it must have been quite hectic. Was it something significant?”  

In that moment, Viktor had no choice but to take on a deadly gaze, locking onto Louisa.  

It was supposedly classified information that he was superhuman, and one of the people who should not know that was undoubtedly Louisa.  

When Viktor’s fierce glare shifted to Ronian, the latter only shook his head with a worn-out smile.  

‘That expression doesn’t help.’  

While his eyes could be reasonably composed, they held an absurd indication that Louisa had discerned his status independently.  

What could he do?  

Having already formulated a dark outlook, Viktor found it tedious to assemble a concise retort to the ongoing provocations.  

Viktor was disappointed by how easy it had become to misinterpret the fact of his own status.  

Recent developments having taken their toll, he felt utterly worn out.  

Amid the dire circumstances, he now faced the possibility of admitting to being a superhuman in the midst of everyone.  

This strange horror was more than what had overcome Ronian, as Viktor required caution and was utterly incapable of sorting through the tangled strings laid before him.  

Which one was overstepping?  

“Though His Majesty may know, you need not glare so terribly. There’s no need for your eyes to be so deadly.”  

“Sir, can you…really not say anything?”  

“Unfortunately, His Majesty is aware. Therefore, I trust you wouldn’t show such a fierce countenance from now on.”  

Louisa’s voice brimmed with sarcasm despite Viktor’s reply tainted with sincerity.  

Caught off guard, the knight could only momentarily steal a glance.  

An air of temporary discomfort swept across the tense gathering.  

The taunt lingered too long for comfort, dodging responsibility with ease.  

In that context, the knight heard yet another contemptuous remark clash against his ear.  

“Patience is to be commended. No need for a loss of clarity.”  

Losing track of where he stood had marked the dire point of reckoning. Viktor could only growl as he forced aside the doubts about his current perception, leading to him inevitably being stuck in a bind.  

“Your Highness,” he exclaimed.  

“The King’s well informed simply because of you…Hah.”  

“Besides, it’s not like I have to listen to any implications thrown at me. Surely it can’t hurt.”  

Just before he could look deeper into it, Viktor was cut off, unable to confirm the source of the words that followed.  

“Since His Majesty is aware.”  

Viktor’s eyes widened and involuntarily shattered his breath, urging him to step back.  

He opened his mouth only to be interrupted, built cautiously, balancing between every possible interpretation and nonchalant appearance.  

He abandoned those tangled paths deciding otherwise, rationalizing,  

“Your Majesty is inside; I must go now.”  

Voices turned against Viktor yet emitted laughter at his efforts.  

Aware of Ronian’s laughter, he took a turn towards the center and swiftly made his way ahead.  

Alas…  

“The Emperor must be told.”  

Grasping just how little time remained in his judgment, Viktor understood that the moment would eventually arrive.   

So running might be the only answer left.  

A scowl twisted his face as he hastened toward the inner sanctum while struggling against intuition.  

Yet nothing was certain about the impact behind the command.  

As Viktor slipped through, an unpredictable confrontation lay in wait.



-chapter 387-

The Holy Kingdom expresses its gratitude to His Majesty, the Emperor of the Empire, for making the decisive step to end the war stemming from misunderstanding. We hope that no more meaningless sacrifices will occur, and that all in the Holy Kingdom will pray for peace on the continent.

We express our regret over the victims arising from the misunderstandings between our two nations and hereby designate the Black Serpent, the Cassel Tower, as a public enemy of the continent, thus activating an order for its extermination.

The consecutive announcements from the Holy Kingdom and the Empire once again sent shockwaves through the world. While it was anticipated that the Empire would cease its conquests against the Holy Kingdom, nobody expected it would occur so abruptly, particularly through a public declaration that seemed to compliment one another.

Furthermore, the swift actions taken by the Empire soon plunged neighboring nations into chaos.

– Intelligence reports indicate that mages from the Cassel Tower have infiltrated countries neighboring the Empire. We request cooperation from each kingdom to apprehend them.

In the late autumn, when the harvest season was coming to a close, the Empire’s legions began to move towards the borders, creating a cacophony across the continent.

* * *

“I refuse.”

Logan cut off the conversation with startling finality.

His resolute demeanor caused the Empire’s envoy standing before him to frown slightly.

“Are you sure you won’t regret this?”

Such provocative words were unbecoming for an envoy from another nation addressing a king.
