“Regret? That foolishness would arise only if I allowed their army into my kingdom.”

“…If you refuse, His Majesty the Emperor will consider Mackline as collaborating with the Black Serpent.”

The envoy was outwardly goading for confrontation.

His rigidly raised head seemed to be demanding death, as if showcasing his defiance.

‘Was it Count Mitra?’

The look of someone resigned to death was genuinely puzzling. How could a noble of such stature, worthy of an envoy, so openly risk his life?

Of course.

‘If I did manage to decapitate him, the Empire would likely retaliate immediately.’

-While there are three nations bordering the western part of the Empire, only our kingdom lies to the east. If the Empire intends to wage a war of conquest, they will first look to tidy up our kingdom before launching an attack on the west. For external observers, our military strength is merely on par with one of those three nations.

Damian’s words rang true.

The circumstances now differed from the past, but in his previous life, the Empire had indeed struck first against Grandia.

It was unlikely that sending the envoy back would prevent a declaration of war, but at the very least, it would buy them time.

‘We need to choose when to go to war on our own terms.’

Aileen and her group, who returned from the Holy Kingdom, were still not completely restored.

Though they were instructed to hunt the Empire’s supers and prioritize their safety, their reckless behavior led to numerous achievements, even risking lives, including wounding her brother gravely. To Logan, it was utterly baffling.

‘It’s fortunate they survived.’

Fearing that the Cassel Tower might play tricks after being attacked in the Demon Forest and wondering if the Sword Master there might recognize him, it was a regret he couldn’t shake.

Even so, they needed more time to fully recuperate.

“Mackline does not collaborate with the Black Serpent. We are willing to cooperate in the search and apprehension operations regarding the Black Serpent, but we cannot permit the Empire’s troops to enter. That’s all there is to it.”

“That’s contradictory! Are you genuinely not afraid of the Emperor’s wrath?”

The envoy was shrieking in frustration, prompting the ministers gathered in the Great Hall to regard him coolly.

His situation was so over-the-top that it looked as though he was begging for death, but Logan merely smiled and waved dismissively.

“Escort the envoy out. Ensure he is returned safely to the border. We must avoid any ‘unfortunate incidents.’”

At Logan’s words, the expression of Samuel Mitra, who had been shouting, momentarily hardened.

‘If I don’t kill him, he’ll be prepared to take his own life.’

In his previous life, there had been such occurrences in Grandia.

Thus, Logan had no intention of leaving any opportunities for provocation whatsoever.

“Your Majesty, this is against international convention….”

Suddenly dropping his proud demeanor, Samuel looked around with concern. 

But there was only silence surrounding him, and Logan shook his head resolutely.

“I can’t hold a welcome party for an envoy who suggests bringing in an army. Let’s have you return quietly, Count.”

Those with intellect would understand the Empire’s intentions.

However, based on the intelligence provided by the Flame’s Eye, disturbances were already bubbling in the western nations. Factions in favor of and against the Empire were clashing, to the point where signs of civil unrest were emerging.

Certainly, the nobles inciting unrest were not so foolish as to act without reason. They were merely opportunists who prioritized personal gain over national benefit.

‘The Emperor has made an astute move.’

Yet, such possibilities were entirely absent in Mackline.

“Is there anyone who wishes to befriend the Empire’s envoy?”

Logan’s gaze swept across the Great Hall, causing the gathered nobles to collectively bow their heads.

“None!”

“May it be as you will, Your Majesty.”

“Your Majesty’s wishes align with the kingdom’s desires.”

Logan smiled lightly at Samuel’s face, which had gone pale from fear.

“It seems so.”

The envoy, now completely devoid of words, could say nothing further.

* * *

“Is everything prepared?”

Once outside the Great Hall, those who had closely followed behind him gathered tightly.

Among them, Damian, who stood on Logan’s right, responded instantly to his inquiry.

“The 2nd and 3rd legions are already constructing defensive lines around key strategic positions centered on the fortress. The 1st Legion is also readying for deployment, while the 4th and 5th Legions are preparing for direct participation or support.”

“And what about the self-defense force?”

To this, Dwayne, who stood on Logan’s left, replied promptly.

“The harvest season has yet to conclude. We’re refraining from calling them up to avoid swaying public sentiment, but we have increased supplies of repeating crossbows. Liberation is bolstering production at the Mage Workshop, as well.”

“Good, good. And the Empire’s movements?”

“According to Philip’s report, supplies are beginning to gather for the Eastern legions. However, the amount is surprisingly large.”

“…Large?”

“Yes. It’s stated that it’s enough to mobilize not five, but eight legions, or potentially even more.”

Logan’s brow furrowed at these words.

‘While I didn’t anticipate it would play out identically to my previous life, starting out with such a divergence is unsettling.’

It was only natural, upon reflection. Mackline today was not on par with Grandia, which had crumbled so easily by just five legions in his past life.

“Damian, when is the anticipated invasion?”

“Even with a few more staged acts for public justification, it appears to be within a month. The Eastern legions are moving toward Lusbeldheim under the pretense of joint training.”

“…A month.”

Hearing the specific timeframe made Logan’s hands involuntarily clench into fists. The disaster they had been preparing for since the moment of his rebirth was drawing nearer.

The struggles of twenty years spent below the surface in his past life rushed back through his memory, blending with the days spent fighting like a cornered rat.

And those memories ultimately led to a horrific mountain of corpses. He could feel the lament of the displaced people from his homeland who brought him back to this past.

‘I must prevent such horrors from happening again.’

Logan took a brief breath to rid himself of the surging intensity of emotion and then asked about the final matter that needed checking.

“…What about Ronian?”

“The Count began training today.”

“Is that so? I suppose I should go see him.”

“Um, Your Majesty.”

“Hmm?”

After some hesitation, Dwayne had spoken. 

Worry was evident on his face, which was impossible to conceal.

However, Logan’s answer was unwavering.

“Of course.”

That response finally sparked a glimmer of hope in Dwayne’s worried expression, and Logan gave him a faint, reassuring smile while patting his loyal subordinate’s shoulder.

As he made his way towards Ronian, Logan found himself face to face with an unwelcome visitor.

“…Princess Louisa.”

“I hope you’ve been well, Your Majesty.”

Unmoved by her slightly creased brows, she greeted him with a courteous bow.

“What brings you here…?”

“Just on my way to meet my betrothed.”

“Oh….”

“I couldn’t help but worry, having not seen my betrothed for months due to his solitary training. I can’t help but wonder if he was gravely injured during that time.”

“…”

What on earth did this woman know?

Logan didn’t believe he had kept anything from her entirely, but he had guessed her awareness of some details of the situation could only raise questions.

“The Emperor has openly expressed his desire for conquest against the world and positioned the Cassel Tower as the pretext for it. The princess seems ill-suited to be lingering in such a situation.”

As a member of the Empire’s royal family and a mage from the Cassel Tower, she obviously should have been aware of the danger of acting so carefree.

Upon noting Logan’s words, the princess simply smiled.

“Then what should I do, Your Majesty?”

“…?”

“Have you forgotten the promise? My father and I agreed to assist Mackline in case of war. Surely, you don’t plan to send me home in this sensitive time?”

Returning would surely lead to her harm.

Such emotion was laid bare in Louisa’s tone, causing Logan’s brow to knitting together in unease.

‘The Cassel Tower is now a thorn everyone wishes to rid themselves of.’

Despite his immediate impulse to advise the princess to abandon her title and return to the House, Louisa instead seemed hell-bent on diving into the blaze.

Feeling that attitude was illogical, Logan could not entirely deem her assertions as mere empty expressions of purpose.

“Even if you kept your promise, there is no benefit to keeping it; if things worsen, you would risk everything—your status and lineage. Are you really prepared to countenance such a decision?”

“Even if I share information, you would verify it anyway. There’s nothing lost on my end.”

The fierce light in Louisa’s azure eyes held a firm resolution.

‘She truly doesn’t intend to return at all.’

An unsettling thought crossed Logan’s mind.

Could it be an edict from the Cassel Tower?

Or was it…?

“I heard that the princess has a strong hatred towards the Empire.”

That remark ignited a flame of emotion in Louisa’s azure eyes. The gray magic emanating from her entire body quivered slightly.

If it weren’t for Logan’s ability to see magic, he may have assumed that it was merely an act.

“…So it’s true.”

“…You’re quite the troublesome one.”

As Louisa’s relaxed smile dissipated, a serious expression overcame her features.

Logan’s mind began to race.

Why, of all things, would a princess from the Empire harbor such emotions?

Perhaps her father, the Eastern King, had suppressed her in a way?

Many convoluted speculations swirled within his thoughts, yet as the pressing specter of war loomed, this was not the time to dwell on them.

Advice still demanded to be issued.

“Very well. If you choose to keep your promise, then do so. However, Princess, it’s best to set any ulterior motives aside.”

“If I were ever to harm your kingdom, I would undoubtedly uproot both you and the Cassel Tower immediately.”

“…Please don’t. I’m feeling rather anxious now.”

Even after turning his back, the cold sensation lingered on him.

Pausing momentarily, Logan sighed deeply, shaking off the thoughts looming in his mind.

“Your Majesty.”

“Your Majesty!”

As he made his way down the hall, every attendant he passed bowed their heads respectfully.

They eyed Louisa, following closely behind him, with overt curiosity.

The sight of an imperial princess roaming freely in Grandpia during the Empire’s aggressive militarization was indeed bizarre.

It led to speculations among the servants of the Mackline stronghold.

“Did you hear that the princess is engaged to Count Ronian?”

“They say she won’t break the engagement nor return home.”

“Then…”

Rumors circulated among the servants in McLine Castle, bringing forth mixed hopes of war being averted.

While these whispers spread, the movements between the two nations barreled toward war at an alarming pace.

And it transformed into a solid suspicion after encountering Cardinal Tracy, the one specifically pointed out as the primary suspect. 

Just that alone weighed heavily on my heart, but to hear it uttered from an unexpected source made it that much worse.

The feeling of despair crept up my spine, tightening my fists without my consent.

It was a definitive statement.

His courteous demeanor began to soften Harmon’s troubled heart, for it implied he wasn’t here to instigate or jest. 

“If you have something to say, please do. I am all ears.”

If what I suspected was true, the Holy Kingdom was indeed on the brink of unprecedented chaos. 

Despite the youthful appearance of my opponent, there was a chance they might possess information I was unaware of, given his status.

For a prince of the Empire to display such formal manners was indeed surprising.

Barros, who had been speaking steadily, halted abruptly, suddenly overwhelmed by the grizzly memory that flooded his mind, causing goosebumps to raise on his skin.

The sudden thought unsettled him, but he chose not to linger on it. 

Survival was of utmost priority. 

Sweat dripped from his body, but his desire to live was unquenchable.

With that thought, Barros steeled his resolve.

Though his words weren’t entirely fabricated, the ease with which they escaped his lips surprised even himself.

“In any case, they go by the name of the Black Serpent, or the Cassel Tower, and it appears they have leveraged the power of ancient artifacts to seize control of the mindset of the new Pope.”

“… What did you say?”

Harmon’s aide, Line Harper, standing behind him, let out a bewildered scoff.

Such a reaction was justifiable. Until now, the psychotropic magics known to the world were confined to illusions or sleep spells, convincing people through manipulating their brains rather than their souls. 

Further complicating matters, the resistance against such internal influencing was believed to rank at the top alongside divine powers, surpassing even other kinds of mana.

“That’s utter nonsense…!” 

Line Harper interjected angrily at the borderline heresy, unable to hide his rage alongside the knights under Harmon who mirrored his ire.

However, when Harmon nodded his head, all those angered fell silent, shocked at their commander’s acceptance. 

“I had a rough idea.”

“Commander!”

“What do you mean…?”

In the back, the noise of confusion stopped when Harmon raised one hand. 

He himself had felt the content behind this story was oddly blasphemous, unable to discuss it with his subordinates. 

While apologetic to them, this moment wasn’t the time for sensitivity. 

“I was informed by the Saint and have recently verified the circumstance myself. Cardinal Tracy, is she part of that magus faction?”

“Impressive! You even know the players involved!” 

Barros recognized this as a crucial moment, understanding that coming to such an inference was all too obvious now.

Acknowledging the unsettling notion that Cardinal Tracy was the puppeteer behind the new Pope’s manipulation, Harmon focused on Barros’ next words.

“Indeed. To my regret, Cardinal Tracy is the very mastermind behind the brainwashing of His Holiness the Pope.”

Admitting to this uncomfortable truth cured the suspicions, revealing her as the primary suspect. 

As Barros praised the obvious conclusion, Harmon merely hardened his expression.

“… So, is your intent solely to inform me of this magus faction’s identity?” 

Such information alone wouldn’t suffice. 

With Barros maintaining a respectful gaze, he smiled slyly.

“Of course not. I have come here, brimming with information as I have pursued their very presence within the Holy Kingdom. Not only that, but my stay allowed me to grasp their organization deeply rooted in this realm. My abilities may fall short here, yet the reputation of the Holy Sword is more than enough to remove any hindrance they pose.”

Such confidence was surely a pleasant surprise for Harmon. 

Naturally, Tracy could not be the only influence at play. Once confirmed, how shocking was it that he had not considered more suspects?

Indeed confirmed by Barros’s mention, confirming Tracy’s influence alone became a monumental concern.

“…That’s a considerable help.”

“I’m glad to hear that. I had plenty of worries, so shedding it feels like a load off. Haha.”

Harmon regarded Barros’ face momentarily. 

It was excessively virtuous for a prince’s assertion, breeding some hesitation.

Yet even in the scrutinizing glimpse, Barros’s expression remained unwavering, almost zealously so.

“Oh, as a Crusader, don’t you have the authority to carry out instant adjudications against priests? We will eventually need to convene a trial for the average priests accused.”

“…That will likely occur. And when the time comes, the information you’ve provided, or that you intend to give, will be invaluable.”

“But wouldn’t that take a considerable amount of time?”

“It should be all sorted within the month.”

It was out of character for Harmon to divulge planning details to an outsider so openly.

Yet it was a statement underscored with determination to advance solely for cleanliness.

However, the follow-up from Barros surpassed all expectations terribly.

“That’s far too late. The damage they’ve inflicted upon the Empire is significant enough that Imperial troops are heading here. So, please leave the preliminary operations to me.”

* * *

A storm swirled within the Holy City. 

This was not merely a physical tempest.

“Have you heard? His Holiness…”

“I heard too.” 

“Me too.” 

Cardinal Tracy had maneuvered the ailing Pope and sought to command the Holy Nation herself.

Ridiculous word of such circulating news was indeed hard to digest nonetheless. 

Accusations surrounding the former Pope’s ousting, they now twisted towards Cardinal Tracy, was certainly another absurdity. 

She had barred anyone from entering the Pope’s mansion, allowing only herself to access it.

As the strangeness of these rumors compounded with verity, an increasing number began to believe in this actuality.

Adding fuel to the fire, it was clear that His Holiness hadn’t made a public appearance for an extended period.

In mere days, priests within the ranks started to stir with urgency aided by the situation at hand. 

Unusually promptly and fervently, as if some unseen hand had pushed them on.

“Reveal the truth, Cardinal Tracy!”

“I want to meet His Holiness!” 

“Hear our request for impeachment!” 

Groups of priests congregated, rallying before the Pope’s dwelling, creating waves of demonstrations throughout the Holy Sanctuary.

“A trial for the Cardinals will be conducted soon. All truths will emerge then, so return and await the Church’s instructions!” 

In the wake of the expulsion order from higher-ranking priests put in place after the Saint’s excommunication, they attempted to bring the general priests back into line, but the efforts proved futile.

Facts that should have remained a secret to only the high-ranking clergy were oddly dispersed among the general priests. 

“Let’s storm in! We must rescue His Holiness!” 

“Let’s save our Pope!” 

“Hooray!” 

Fueled by youthful energy, excited priests surged forward toward the Cardinal’s residence. The paladins guarding the area dared not impede their advance.

Until it came when turbulent priests approached the Pope’s presence, Cardinal Tracy emerged not from her chambers but from His Holiness’s citadel.

“Everyone, please go back! His Holiness is gravely ill! What you are doing right now is a crime!”

Gleefully reckless priests hesitated, even backpedled at her words.

“Is that so?” 

“If he’s truly unwell…” 

“Then we have to be cautious.” 

The overtly committed priests paused amidst growing concern, leaving the following group struggling in confusion to grasp the situation.

Then suddenly…

“Stop your nonsense!” 

Whump!

A voice rang out from the crowd, unmasking the astonished priests’ previously unwavering certainty.

“Exactly!” 

“Do you think we would harm the Pope?” 

“We only wish to ensure his safety!” 

Standing at the forefront, a dozen priests, lost in shock, could only stand mute as the mood swiftly transformed.

With the egg still dripping down her face, Tracy bellowed resolutely, “Very well! I’m proud of my dignity! A trial revealing all truths will take place shortly! Therefore, I urge you to wait—any disturbance won’t aid His Holiness’ recovery!” 

Meanwhile, a group of individuals watching this unfold from a distance clenched their fists in unison.

“We succeeded! With that statement, there’s no way they’ll prolong the period beyond a week.”

“Before that, we must observe Tracy and the Black Serpent’s associates to ensure they can’t escape.”

“If they attempt to run, we shall crush them! That’ll save us time from conducting trials too.”

While the leaders of the Crusader Knights cheered, the once-prisoned Ilia, awaiting release, bore a grim visage. 

Perhaps it was a facsimile of worry that influenced Harmon, who quietly approached her. 

“You 2nd Prince. Your means to implant influence is remarkable. It’s evident you’ve handled people well.” 

“Is that so?” 

“…Do you have something weighing on your mind?” 

“Yes, a little.” 

“What troubles you?” 

Having expelled vague suspicions towards her, Harmon now only bore trust in his expression.

Yet the revelation she offered carried disquietude.

“Why does the 2nd Prince assist us?” 

“Yes? The Empire’s adversaries…?” 

“However, the invitation extended post-Papal accord was after his brainwashing. Why then?” 

At this remark, Harmon’s face shadowed with doubt.

The conversation turned tense as if the focus had shifted to a closer target.

“The Army of the Black Serpent and Sorrowing Wind has heightened their advance speed?”

“Yes, that is correct.” 

“So when is their expected arrival?”

“Within a week.” 

With those words, Barros’s expression grew even more haggard.

The timing was suspicious indeed. 

“I’ve set the pieces, but this all remains a veiled strategy… What may be their intention?” 

“Apparently, they seem intent on a pretext to interfere in regards to His Majesty’s intention towards the Holy Kingdom.”

“It’s nothing I can manage…” 

“With the aid of the Holy Sword and the Saint, we ought to finish everything before they arrive.” 

“Why?” 

“To be candid about it…” 

“No, that can’t do! To state it so, ultimately diminishes my own power. The Holy Kingdom must remain beneath my thumb.” 

“Your Highness…” 

The serious atmospheres circling Barros and Leos shifted toward Jerome who was absentmindedly polishing the hilt of his sword, the waves of another war about to partake…

The Blessing of the Great Sea will allow you to endure any attack nine times.

After repelling the continuous ambushes from the ghosts, the Saintess spoke these words with a pale complexion, squeezing out the remaining divine power to bestow her blessing upon him.

Whirr.

Though he had long since exhausted all the arrows in his quiver, he had no cause for concern. All he had to do was pick up the fallen arrows littered along his path as he charged forward.

The arrows fired by the Holy Knights’ archers were subtly different in specification from those he usually used, but that posed no obstacle for him.

A distance exceeding 2 kilometers.

“Understand that there’s no time to waste!”  

As Harmon grimaced, clenching his teeth and moving his sword against the surrounding Imperial forces, Tris smiled in response to a silver sword strike aimed at his neck.  

“My choice was indeed the right one.”  

Just then, in reply to his words, another silver aura blade suddenly pierced Harmon’s side.  

“Not a chance!”  

KAAAANG!  

As Harmon gritted his teeth and strained for his remaining strength, a one-eyed knight was sent flying backward.  

A familiar face.  

‘Jerome Dikaid!’  

The reason he hadn’t realized another aura user was so close was due to the fierce battle with the Sword Spirit.  

He had anticipated this much, but…  

– For the Empire!  

The moment Harmon saw four knights emerge as if they were one, sharing the same voice, he couldn’t help but widen his eyes.  

A crimson aura blazed fiercely from all four of their bodies, unmistakably indicating they were aura users.  

The unsettling and bizarre sensation that they seemed about to shatter at any moment was indeed aura.  

‘Not just one, but five? How did I remain unaware of five aura users closing in?’  

Had he even caught the hint of this, he wouldn’t have engaged in such a decisive duel with the Sword Spirit.  

“I’m sorry, Holy Sword. You’ll have to die here.”  

As Tris’s grave voice pierced Harmon’s ears, the crimson energy collided dazzlingly with the pure white light below the wall.  

The clash of the two superhumans representing their respective nations erupted.  

Surprisingly, the one to collapse was Tris.  

As Harmon seized the advantage, cheers erupted from the castle walls.  

“Our Commander has defeated the Empire’s Greatest Sword!”  

“We won!”  

“Wow!”  

Of course, it wasn’t as if many soldiers stood idly staring elsewhere while their enemies battled in front of them.  

Just as some among them were audacious enough to shout out in celebration, others were already confused without grasping what it meant.  

Those who inadvertently cheered were soon struck by the reality of their own words and widened their eyes in shock.  

“Really!?”  

“Ahhh!”  

It was only natural that their morale began to soar after plunging to the ground because of unfavorable conditions.  

The outcome of one duel manifesting before them reshaped the battlefield’s fate in real-time.  

However, a select few powerful fighters who had been closely watching the duel couldn’t help but widen their eyes at the subsequent spectacle.  

The silver aura began to falter under the overwhelming pressure of the crimson aura.  

“No!”  

“Commander!”  

“Protect the Commander!!!”  

The elite knights of the Holy Sword Order, including Vice-Captain Ryan Harper, began to leap down from the walls, racing towards Harmon as if rushing toward a flame.  

“Aaah!”

“Cough…”  

“Commander!”

And the continuous surge of holy knights leaping down to his side showed no signs of stopping.  

“Commander, please!”

KAAAAANG!  

“Cough!”

It was increasingly infuriating how this Jerome seemingly filled the gaps with miraculous precision.  

Even while his subordinates kept leaping down from the walls, Harmon’s heart filled with dread.  

“Commander!”  

“Protect your Commander!”

There was no visible excitement of fierce combat nor any sense of desperation stemming from the violent sacrifices.

An eerily sticky feeling accompanied their monstrous aura, but their fighting capabilities remained exceptionally powerful.  

The swordsmanship also carried the mark of the Sword Spirit he had just dueled, indicating they had surely been properly trained by him.

He could spare no time to ponder deeply about their strange behavior.  

Would the Imperial forces that had cornered Harmon act as if they were still alive, preserving their anger?

‘This can’t continue.’  

Recklessly, Harmon felt a distinct gaping hole in their formation due to his subordinates’ reckless abandon.  

It was time to take a risk.  

“Hah!”  

Taking a deep breath, Harmon turned his body towards the enemy frontlines instead of the walls.  

While those noble knights certainly appeared shocked, one of the four, blocking his path, advanced towards him without hesitation.  

Calmly, totally unfazed by the unexpected move.  

‘He truly resembles a doll clearly imprinted with techniques.’  

How could an aura user be a mere puppet?  

The power of aura was a privilege only when souls transcended their limits to fully control their flesh.  

Nevertheless, there was no time to waste on unfamiliar feelings.  

Harmon observed as the red aura around the enemy’s blade approached him, ready to pierce his chest.  

He could feel the moment approaching as he thrust his own sword toward his attacker.  

Dodging just slightly to escape the heart’s target meant nothing.  

Thus, he focused solely on stabbing forward.  

Puuush.  

An overwhelming heat flooded his right chest. Harmon clenched his teeth, mustering the strength to endure, as he pushed forward.  

The vague sensation he anticipated came at last.  

His enemy froze as if unsure what to do next in response to his strike.  

The slight pause sealed their fate.  

Harmon’s sword pierced the chest of his foe and cut cleanly through to strike at the waist.  

Chop!  

The upper body and lower body were separated cleanly.  

“!?”  

CLICK.  

If a sound ever existed to describe that sensation, this was it.  

The remaining three knights, along with Jerome, appeared caught off-guard by Harmon’s unexpected brutality in the midst of the skirmish.  

No, they seemed noticeably stunned, almost taking a step back.  

‘It’s done!’  

Harmon commanded the remaining enemy aura to seal itself within him.  

With the wildly raging adrenaline overshadowing his pain, he aimed for the true gap that had opened in the onslaught.  

In that instant.  

Thud.  

An unforeseen hand caught Harmon’s ankle.  

“Ugh!?”  

It was the hand of the enemy’s upper half that remained.  

An inconceivable sight startled Harmon into widening his eyes, as a voice rang from the inside of the helmet.  

“Emperor. Your Majesty. Long live…!”

‘What?’

the enemy’s body below him exploded in a devastating blast.  

KAAAAAAANG!  

Rumble!  

The explosion was utterly sudden yet painfully potent and swept away even the surrounding knights of the Holy Legion.  

The relentless chain of explosions continued in succession, all triggering three more blasts.  

KAAAANG!  

Boom boom boom.  

The dust erupting into the air blocked out the sky while the ground beneath splintered, instantly halting the advancing Imperial forces charging toward the Holy Legion.  

It was a catastrophic explosion that could abruptly end the fierce battle unfolding at the Eastern walls.

“Indeed. They say just one of those costs over 100 million gold. It’s a pity it’s a single-use item.”  

“One hundred million…?”  

Could they be struck dumb?  

“How many more like that do the royal family have?”  

“…I don’t know. But surely not many. Even if they wield great power, the aura dissipates rapidly after engaging, and their cost is incredibly high.”  

Power. Cost.  

Those inhumane terms pressed down on Jerome’s lips.

“Ah, no.”  

“Don’t fret. And remember one thing. It’s all for…”

“Exactly.”

“Those were engraved with perfect immunity to mental magic alongside my baseline swordsmanship. Weapons employed to catch the serpent engulfing the truth. Holy Sword, you were truly a magnificent being.”  

An individual who had to resort to other tactics after failing to defeat him with swordsmanship.  

Tris thought that he would never forget the Holy Sword for the rest of his days as he honored his memory.   

However, as the dust slowly began to settle, a beam of sensational brilliance shot upwards into the sky.  

“What is that?”  

“Hm?”  

Resplendent light seemed holy, yet now he recognized he was the enemy of the Sacred Country.  

In that shocking moment, Tris’s expression hardened.  

“Charge immediately! Resume the battle!”  

“Commander, but the ground…”  

“Cavalry, flank the enemy, and the mages, fill the ground! Capture the sacred capital!”  

Once again, Tris bellowed to shatter the air.  

As the Imperial forces followed his order to reform, amidst that settling dust, a female figure began to appear within the projected light.  

A beautiful woman, dressed entirely in white judicial robes wearing the holy judge’s wreath above her head, floated gracefully above the crater opening created by the explosion.  

– It is not yet time for you to rest.  

Her voice reverberated eerily, reverberating across the ground now lit by beams of light.  

Amongst them, a man still stalled in fainted or deceased condition surged into view along the castle walls.  

‘Holy Sword!!!’  

Tris’s eyes widened in horror.  

“No! All forces charge! We must kill the Holy Sword!”  

His voice rang out thunderously.  

Yet the Imperial forces’ knights and cavalry, flanking on either side, found themselves struggling as they swerved their way around Tris, ultimately losing sight of their target as the Holy Sword vanished atop the castle wall.  

‘Saint? Did the Saint wield such power? Damn it! Why didn’t we have such intelligence…!? No, this isn’t the moment to panic. We still hold a colossal advantage.’  

With his lips firmly clenched, Tris pressed his men onward.  

“Holy Sword can’t fight anymore! The enemy’s leader has collapsed! Charge now!”  

Though his command was grounded, it was not devoid of merit.  

Yet, despite that precise reasoning, a sudden message rang from his mind.  

[Commander, the magic circle has reached its limit unexpectedly fast. The holy barrier is recovering at an alarmingly rapid rate. You may want to observe the situation and act accordingly.]  

The frenzied army of the Empire could only come to an abrupt stop.

### We Are Right

Such thoughts or justifications, or claims—namely, a righteous cause—are one of the most significant factors in warfare, especially in the case of an invasion.

Soldiers serving an invading army never consider themselves invaders. Everyone wants to embody the punisher of injustice rather than be seen as the villain attacking innocent victims.

A soldier who must wield a sword and thrust a spear at someone they have never met before can only cling to that rationale to safeguard their own heart. Therefore, without a righteous cause, it is only a matter of time before even the best-trained army crumbles.

In this regard, the Empire’s cause was quite plausible.

– Mackline thoroughly rejected the cooperation regarding the search for the Black Serpent, a public undertaking that incited the tragedy of the Holy Nation War across the continent. 

– “To preserve the peace of this land and realize justice, we shall eradicate Mackline.”

Of course, anyone with a sense of decency would consider such statements mere excuses.

However, when a propaganda announcement is combined with a modicum of truth and fitting manipulation, plus the overwhelming display of military forces that seem incapable of losing, the morale of the Imperial Army soared to the heavens.

– Mobilization of the entire Eighth Legion from the East.

– Mobilization of the Imperial Central Army. Over 150,000 troops, comprising three legions.

– The Imperial Guard, including the Swordmaster, and six superhumans will set out.

– Including the Mage of the North Winds, five mages from the Seven Great Mage Towers will initiate their sortie. 

This was a scale far exceeding what anyone had anticipated.

* * *

“The First Legion has established a garrison at Kyle Fortress under the leadership of Sir Francisco. The Second Legion, led directly by the Swordmaster, has entered the northwestern fortress, Shield, while the Third Legion has completed garrison at the southeastern fortress, Armor, under the command of Duke Patrick.”

“What about the Royal Coalition?”

Demian Nadal calmly continued as he gazed at the young monarch in armor who sat upon the throne of war.

“According to the agreement, the reinforcements from Liberty and Teronan are also en route to the western border along with the Fourth and Fifth Legions. From Liberty, the superhuman, Count Gunther, and from Teronan, the unyielding Latin Lawrence and the Mage of the Tides, Gustav Clement, will join simultaneously.”

“Three? Mobilizing all the superhumans? This is beyond expectations.”

“The Empire’s intentions are clear; thus the Royal Coalition is in urgent need. Our partnership has been fortuitous.”

The news of war preparations proceeded as expected, yet the faces of the noblemen gathered for the council remained grim.

Whether they sensed the atmosphere or not, Logan inquired again, tone steady.

“What’s the difference in strength compared to the Imperial Army?”

“When purely counting manpower, our force stands at the level of seven legions when adding our own five and the Royal Coalition. However, this is clearly insufficient compared to the eleven legions of the Imperial Army, including the Mage Legion.”

“So, are we at a disadvantage?”

“Absolutely not.”

Demian’s response was resolute against Logan’s doubt.

The puzzled gazes of the nobility focused on Demian.

“We can mitigatively address the numerical disadvantages with our vigilantes, new weapons, and the ‘contingency plan’ prepared by His Majesty. Our kingdom is sufficiently strong. The Empire shall not occupy an inch of Mackline’s land.”

At this, half of the gathered nobles displayed a glimmer of hope on their faces, thanks to Demian Nadal’s assurance alongside the prominent civil officer, Dwayne Filzner. 

However, those who bore such optimism were a paltry few. The remaining half could not help but harbor skeptical thoughts despite Demian’s confidence.

– What ‘contingency plan’ could possibly remedy that deficit in troop strength? Or what about the superhumans?

This unvoiced concern transmitted through the anxious gazes shared among them.

Klan Loop, a noble from a small territory in the western region, entertained similar thoughts.

‘Am I to prepare for asylum in the Empire?’

Despite being called to attend the war council under the king’s decree, he had no inkling of victory for the kingdom. 

‘The summons must be to request offerings of property for the war.’

The territory mattered, yet not more than life itself. Following royal orders was necessary, but subsequently, he could flee with the remaining assets of his family.

As he ruminated on various thoughts, the conversation took a sudden turn when he saw the king spring up from his seat.

“…Thus, I know many of you feel anxious. However, there is no need for concern.”

Clang!

Suddenly drawing out a sword.

‘What does he intend to do with that?’

Gazes from many nobles, including Klan, fixated on the king.

“Behold! The power possessed by your monarch!”

Woooooooon.

Brilliant golden light erupted from the blade, piercing the roof of the Great Hall, resonating in waves that echoed throughout the space.

Those with even a hint of understanding could recognize the radiant aura symbolizing the ‘Sun of Mackline.’ 

Just as the red sun cast its golden rays, the golden light pouring forth from the red-haired king pierced the eyes of the gathered nobility.

Squeak.

Then followed a light, paper-like sound, akin to a thin sword slicing through parchment.

Yet, despite its subtlety, the outcome was monumental.

Kraaaaaak.

From the throne’s ceiling through the entrance of the Great Hall, extending towards the portal of Grandpia’s main temple—an almost 300-meter stretch—was sliced open at identical angles.

Miraculously, not a single pillar was disturbed, simply leaving behind the marks of the sword, resembling a three-dimensional stroke engraved into the beautiful murals of Grandpia.

This unbelievable sight sent shivers down the spines of those nobles gathered.

Not one among them had ever seen, or even imagined, a display of overwhelming force like this.

They stood agape, dumbfounded, unable to muster a sound of awe in astonishment.

Witnessing this, the king emanated a blazing golden aura from the throne and spoke in a measured tone, “The Empire’s superhumans can never surpass me.”

As silence descended, applause finally erupted from the assembly.

Clap. Clap.

“Uwaaaaaah!”

Having just activated the ‘Up’ trait, the depletion of force within him made him feel as if his body was a hollow can.

So.

Despite everything, Logan’s heart swelled with reassurance at the sight of those noblemen.

For his final training prior to the campaign.

‘Yes. Prepared—thoroughly.’

‘Even if word of today’s performance reaches outside the palace, the Empire will hardly believe it. I hope the Swordmaster receives my challenge for a duel, though…’

While envisioning a showdown with the Swordmaster, maintained on the words of his wife and Viktor about his prowess, Logan slowly lifted his blade.

According to them, the Swordmaster could wield cutting abilities that effortlessly divided space itself.

Yet at this moment, Logan felt quite a distance from that plateau. Having reached the peak of mastery without necessarily utilizing the Vision of the Divine Sword’s second technique, the Vision of Space Cutting, he still required several seconds to gather his strength.

Loading power into each of his strikes felt hazy.

‘Though utilizing a trait guarantees victory…’ 

If he could defeat the Swordmaster without resorting to that, it would truly be advantageous. 

Far more than being exhausted from the fight and leaving the battlefield.

‘But I could die too in that case.’

Fortunately, he had another solution.

He had recently managed to sense the eighth type of the Vision of the Divine Sword.

If he could unleash that not only in the training grounds but even on the battlefield, he would undoubtedly be able to prevail against the Swordmaster without the need to utilize traits.

Wooooo.

Logan’s focus sharpened, centering his mind as the sword tip rose.

Yet in that very moment.

Suuuuu.

An unpleasant sense of unease began to intrude upon his heightened perception.

Logan Mackline, the King of Mackline, challenges the Empire’s greatest sword, Tris Honsby, to a one-on-one duel!

“He’s gone mad, hasn’t he?”

Murmurs filled the air.

Although the Imperial army was known for its strict discipline, the clamor was quite unlike them. At that moment, their leader was offering up his head as if he couldn’t distinguish the impending war.  

A moth diving into flames, unaware of its fate.

In their eyes, Logan was just that—a foolhardy moth.

However, the young aura user, who had lost one eye to a similar situation, couldn’t dismiss him.  

“Master, you need to think carefully. Logan Mackline is no fool. He must have some hidden strategy to confront you.”

Tris’s eyes darted around the tent, surveying the superhumans present—Gallen, along with four other mages, Jerome, and himself.

Yet, should they manage to kill the opposing commander at the onset of battle, that would truly be the cherry on top.

Considering all possible risks, there was but one path forward.

Before Tris could even respond to her statement, a disapproving cluck of the tongue was heard.  

“Again, you charge into needless trouble alone.”  

The middle-aged woman, who seemed dissatisfied, shook her head. The mage of Earthquakes, Selene Bowter, boasted a robust figure completely uncharacteristic of her superhuman status, and as she often did, she stood opposed to Nelly.

Although his tone was composed, a razor-sharp intensity accompanied his words, and Selene’s face blanched under that pressure.

Ultimately, Jerome stifled his words, resigning himself back to his spot.

Atop the battlements of the castle, a lone vigilante pressed his crossbow into waiting hands, with other vigilantes stacked behind like a staircase, each aiming down range carrying their crossbows prepared.  

Seeing them might appear comical at first glance, yet their faces wore serious expressions.  

The large figure at the bottom, weighed down more by foreboding than pressure, was fixated ahead with flaming cheeks.  

It was Kyle, one of the largest cities in the Kingdom, but even with such a massive size, it was impossible for hundreds of thousands to occupy its walls at once.

A necessary yet forced measure.

The remaining vigilantes stationed behind lined up, clutching magazines and crossbows, stationed next to regular troops hiding their heads under the battlements and knights holding red stones as they faced the depths below the walls.

A thundering roar accompanied by war cries surged forward, sending tremors across the land.

Nonetheless, the sheer scale of knights approaching—at least 10,000—sent a shivering wave of pressure through him.  

Logan too had restructured the criteria for knight selections, successfully mass-producing many knights; however, only the Second Legion, grounded firmly in the territory of Mackline, could boast a proportionate knight count to soldiers—certainly not to this overwhelming number.  

If it were they’d had just a few more years, the scenario might have changed.

That anxiety wasn’t solely his.

All resulting in an unthinkable success!

-chapter 390-

**Chapter Title: Assumed Advanced Aura User…**

The man, who had lost his name and was only referred to as the Dark Blade, clicked his tongue inwardly as he recalled the information about his target. It seemed that the preliminary investigation had been exaggerated.

It was already a miracle that a young man, not even thirty, had reached the level of an Aura User.

But to think he had reached the advanced stage?

Even among the Empire’s army commanders, this was a level typically only achieved in old age according to common standards. It couldn’t help but make him think the situation was overly cautious.

Even with Jerome Dikaid’s testimony, it was hard to accept as common sense. He was once called the Empire’s Saint, but he had lost credibility by aiding a traitor.

Of course, ignoring this completely was also out of the question. There had been only two superhumans within the Special Inspection Department, besides himself, who had already faced defeat at the hands of this target.

‘He must be strong, at least among the intermediate ranks.’

That was the limit of his imagination.

Even that was an incredible achievement for someone of his age. He could be considered a genius of the century.

However, this operation was set with an advanced Aura User such as himself and an intermediate boss. Given the nature of assassination, if both he and the boss put their lives on the line, it might be worth aiming for an advanced Aura User. Yet, overestimating the enemy would only lead to unnecessary tension.

The Dark Blade combined the information he had heard with basic common knowledge to reach this conclusion. After sending a signal to the boss, the Shadow Blade, who was following behind him, they sprinted silently down the corridors of the unfamiliar kingdom.

None of the palace servants, soldiers, or knights were able to notice their movements.

This stealth technique, enhanced by the power of artifacts and a special force manipulation skill, had earned the Special Inspection Department the name “Ghosts,” making it impossible for the soldiers of a small nation to even sense their presence.

However, he was somewhat concerned about the odd mana that lingered around the bodies of the knights and soldiers.

‘They can’t all possess artifacts, so the presence of a magic circle means that Mackline had that ability? This will need reporting.’

As he checked the unexpected information, he found himself momentarily halting his steps as he approached the palace’s heart.

‘A trap?’

His eyes, hidden beneath his mask, narrowed with abnormal detection. The training he had received for decades as an assassin allowed him to sense the faint magical energy.

Magical traps spread irregularly across the floor, walls, and ceiling.

These were traps absent from any previous intelligence.

‘Not bad…’

This was a highly advanced level of traps that might have caught agents below the special tier.

Perhaps the last failed mission had instilled a sense of caution, he thought.

‘But even so.’

To him and the Shadow Blade, they were merely a slight inconvenience.

– Move cautiously. Advance while avoiding traps.

They exchanged signals with each other, performing acrobatics to pass between traps.

Creating even a slight sound during this process was only natural for them.

Shortly thereafter, the two reached the location of their target.

‘The training ground at this hour.’

Relying on the schedule, it was convenient to have someone alone.

‘The king’s death, one day before the scheduled departure, is perfect.’

As he signaled to the Shadow Blade, he, as before, began to merge into the training ground without sound. The knights stationed at the entrance, meant for royal use, were nothing more than scarecrows in his eyes.

As he brushed past the shadow of a knight, the Dark Blade contemplated.

When would the target truly realize that they were upon him?

‘Right before death? Or just before the blade touches him?’

A superhuman and the king of a nation. He was one of the most formidable figures in a lifetime of assassinations.

A deep smile, reminiscent of a born killer, spread across the faceless mask of the Dark Blade.

‘Ghosts! Two, perhaps?’

Logan’s red eyes quivered slightly.

He could feel an indistinct presence coupled with stealthy hostility.

Two years ago, they bore an uncanny resemblance to the filth that had invaded his private chamber.

However, with complete concentration on the sword, the movements of the assailants now felt nothing like those from before.

More accurately, it was about their level.

‘Could they be at least that level?’

Even back then, when he had been confident in his heightened senses, he hadn’t sensed the threat until the foe’s blade appeared before his eyes. Ultimately, that encounter had become the turning point for his wife’s awakening.

Clearly, that foe had been threatening.

If he could barely perceive the movements now at his level, perhaps they might truly be at that standard.

‘Assassins, yet Aura Users.’

If such beings existed, it would be extremely perilous.

‘If this were two years ago… the Empire…’

A cold smile flashed across Logan’s lips.

In his previous life, the Empire had not revealed their typical invasion strategy until they had nearly dominated the continent.

Just before the war’s commencement, an assassination would typically target the king if he were a general or benevolent ruler and would leave the prince alive if it was someone as tyrannical as Grandia, aiming instead to eliminate those ministers with skill and favor.

A nation’s leadership collapsing just before war inevitably leads to confusion within the army, and they could quickly be overtaken by Imperial forces that had initially been incapable of conquering them due to improper resource management.

The rumors about the Empire’s Special Inspection Department, colloquially known as “ghosts,” began to circulate in the populace around this time.

‘Good they won’t change.’

Officially, there were still thirty-two known superhumans within the Empire; now, as four had died, there were twenty-eight remaining. While it was uncertain how many hidden superhumans existed beyond those, even the Empire would not easily possess superhumans.

Thus…

‘If they are Aura Users, and especially as ghosts, dealing with them here would significantly benefit us.”

Logan focused fiercely on the two assailants approaching him while maintaining his sword-drawing stance.

The news of their tactics had aided in this situation.

He lightly employed the force, checked the status of his exclusive artifacts.

Vwoosh.

The Boots of the Wind God, Gloves of Herculean Strength, and the Shoulder Armor of Protection activated in succession, boosting his agility, strength, and durability to extreme levels.

Excluding additional functions, it was surprising how much the spec-up effects even applied to an Aura User’s highly enhanced physique. The artifacts previously assessed at merely class four revealed overwhelming efficacy.

He had named them personally later, but it seemed a peculiar treasure comparable to treasures formed by either a group or an individual.

‘Relics from the Sword God Ilmak.’

The artifacts resonated solely with the Core of Power, and they all came seeking him as if drawn by fate.

In the legends of the Sword God, it was recorded that a set of nine armaments consisting of such artifacts, headgear, upper body armor, lower body armor, left shoulder guards, bucklers, and swords had shared a collective effect.

When gathered, their efficacy would be eye-poppingly impressive; however…

‘…It would be excessive.’

An incredible two thousand years had passed. The wonder of even three of these artifacts still existing and being in his possession astonished him.

At that moment, when his mind momentarily wandered…

As if sensing his distraction, a black dagger suddenly emerged from behind his neck.

Simultaneously, a brilliant golden light erupted from Logan’s sword, elegantly arcing to strike the dagger behind him.

Bang!

A loud clash echoed as the shadow was sent tumbling back.

Though the mask obscured his expression, the flowing blood seeping through the shaking aura and black gloves made it clear he had sustained significant damage.

‘Impressive!’

With a menacing smile spreading across Logan’s face, he charged forward at once.

His sword thrust forward as if to pierce the neck.

Even as the attack’s trajectory was felt, the shifting gaze of his enemy behind the mask was apparent, seemingly deciding on something as it ignored the strike aimed at its throat and instead lunged to pierce him with its dagger.

Simultaneously, a gray Aura surged upward.

The attempt to die together was clearly seen, making Logan’s brows twitch as the enemy’s movements met his.

Then, another dagger leaped from behind him.

At the same time, Logan’s sword brushed against the gray Aura, and the radiant golden light surged forth, curling in mid-air to envelop the assailant coming from behind.

Khadang!

The assailants rebounded with a loud crash.

Once again, there were no shouts or screams, but this time, the knights who sensed the anomaly began rushing inside the training ground.

“Your Majesty!”

“An assassin!”

Faces pale as sheets, the knights who allowed the assassination to breach their defenses rushed desperately.

“Fall back!!”

With thunderous cries reverberating, the golden beams burst forth, pushing against the two black shadows systematically.

It was an overwhelming display of power.

In the storm of the radiant golden Aura, bursts of gray Aura sporadically radiated, resisting against the onslaught.

Skrip.

Bang!

Crack!

The knights struggled to keep up with the frantic movements of the three, each collision sending shockwaves that resonated through the air.

“Th-this…!”

“Impossible…!”

Overwhelmed by the explosive sounds of colliding powers, the knights realized their helplessness, breaking into a sprint outside to raise the alarm.

“Intruders!”

“Surround the training ground!”

Their alarm echoed frantically, and as the chaos unfolded, the Dark Blade sensed that his mission had already failed.

‘How could this happen…’

Everything stemmed from the target’s unexpected power.

What he had assumed was exaggerated turned out to be the opposite. 

A complete anomaly—a manifest of an aura user of the highest caliber, or perhaps… 

‘Could he possibly be the best? At his age?!’

A monstrous existence that seemed like a creature from myths or legends now stood before him.

The moment he recognized that, the Dark Blade quickly made a decision.

He urgently sent an escape signal to the Shadow Blade, whose demeanor was visibly shaking.

– Mission failure. Retreat. Cause a detonative distraction to cover your escape.

Receiving the signal, the Shadow Blade’s momentum faltered further, but there was no choice.

Within the Special Inspection Department, agents were fundamentally coached to self-destruct upon mission failure. In the bygone days, when the Empire’s royal family and the Black Serpent temporarily aligned to create the Ghosts, they were designed from the start as terminatory “resources” against enemies.

However, superiors who had reached the level of superhumans were not permitted to self-destruct due to the “scarcity value” of those resources. Although their failure was uncommon, if there existed even a possibility, the highest-ranking orders encouraged a tactical retreat instead of sacrificing their worth as resources.

But the situation was different now.

Blocking that monstrosity was impossible through normal means. Sacrifice was necessary.

And he had to survive for other reasons.

‘The Sun of Mackline. I need to inform the Empire of his level. The world was deceived…’

The information surrounding the Empire’s first objective was completely wrong.

To reveal that fact, he had to live.

“Get lost!”

For the first time since their encounter, the Dark Blade shouted, his gray Aura exploding as he attempted to push back against the golden serpent’s assault.

And in that moment, instead of swinging his sword again, he threw something from his bosom onto the ground.

Boom!

With a loud explosion, dense black smoke erupted forth.

From within it came a roaring golden voice, filled with fury.

“Poison!?”

Correct.

The Special Inspection Department’s unique poison pellets were top-tier paralysis poisons, capable of incapacitating even the strongest knights in an instant.

However, they had little effect against Aura Users. For now, he resorted to merely muddling vision and senses.

Within that haze, his body seamlessly vanished from the watch of the golden Aura.

“Where do you think you’re going?!”

As the golden Aura began slashing at the spatial boundaries where he had been, he once more faded into the void, evading its reach.

“…For Mackline!”

Rising from the depths of the Chaos, the Shadow Blade indomitably stood in front, taking the full brunt of the golden Aura.

Seeing his body swell and receive the golden strikes, the Dark Blade wasted no time and swiftly dashed away, putting every effort into darting externally while still veiling himself in invisibility.

Boom!

As soon as he burst from the training grounds, a thunderous explosion resonated, seeming to make the entire palace tremble.

That impact would surely suffice to leave a mark on the monstrosity, wouldn’t it?

An advanced Aura User could manipulate space, but that youthful figure hadn’t yet shown any signs of such authority, even during the entirety of the ambush.

‘Could he still be too immature? Or is he merely outstanding among the advanced? Could he be dead?’

Such thoughts crossed his mind, but stepping back now was a gamble with his life.

‘Shadow Blade. I will not forget your sacrifice.’

As he sped off, gnashing his teeth internally, the palace entrance suddenly appeared before him.

While passing through a corridor marked with a strange slash, just as he was about to exit…

Szzzz.

‘Urk!’

The Dark Blade collapsed, feeling as though his very soul had shattered, unable to emit a sound.

Thud.

His invisibility slackened, and he was unable to stabilize himself.

‘What is… happening…?’

He felt no presence behind him, and he managed to find nobody following.

In reality, there was no one around him in this moment.

‘What has happened…?’

But he was not granted the time to ponder.

“Ch-intruder!”

“Capture him!”

Amidst his fading consciousness, the Makline soldiers just ahead appeared. Still, he couldn’t harness the will to continue thinking.



-chapter 398-

“What on earth happened here…?”  

Jamie Gilan muttered with a mix of fury and despair as he staggered back.  

The new fortress bore clear signs of dry earth, remnants of the fierce battles that had taken place.  

And there was the attacking army of 200,000 soldiers.  

The northern expeditionary force of the Empire, comprising four legions and seven superhumans, had been utterly decimated.  

The rain of Quarel, completely blocking the line of sight, had been expected, but the pouring red stones raining down was a whole different disaster.  

Witnessing the scene where explosive magic of the 2nd circle blew across the fields like a carpet was beyond comprehension, to the point that it sent chills down his spine.  

– Aahhh!  

– P-Please, save me!  

– Kwasaaaah!  

The screams of the Empire’s elite still echoed in his ears.  

‘This makes no sense. It’s completely incoherent.’  

Thinking back to the reckless amounts used for scrolls for a single skirmish made it particularly ridiculous.  

Never in history, whether from the Empire or any other nation, had there been such a waste of consumable artifacts in a war.  

Such actions were unfathomable unless one intended to bring ruin upon their own nation after a single battle.  

Even the knights of the Empire, who had to somehow breach the enormous assault, had fallen before even reaching the castle walls, pierced by the ‘Red Aura Arrows.’  

Knights who barely managed to climb the walls felt an inconsistent weakness, often collapsing helplessly.  

The seven superhumans who had leaped onto the walls to turn the tide faced unexpectedly powerful resistance in the form of bizarre magic.  

For instance…  

“This damn beast…!”  

“Hoo-hoo-hoo! How do you like that, slippery one? I’m no longer the same as I was back then!”  

“Oh, the audacity of speaking so confidently while benefiting from magic!”  

“Aren’t you two being rather shameless by ganging up? Still as cheeky as ever, you slippery bastard!”  

A hulking giant stood before the two Legion Commanders, Jephen and Blake.  

“This is a new script I’ve never seen before. Which faction are you from?”  

“I am Gunther Liberty of Liberty! Remember my name well, Empire superhuman!”  

An elderly knight, who stood firm against the elite guard of Chaperville.  

However, even conceding that much, it was not the biggest issue.  

The most concerning matter stood right before him.  

A graying man, whose white hair outnumbered his blond locks.  

Jamie knew exactly who he was.  

The strongest superhuman in Mackline, known to be over seventy this year: Felix Esperanza, the Sword King.  

“A monstrous old man…”  

Jamie had been transferred from the Imperial Guard to the commander of the Eastern Army after the death of the spear master, Greet Ainstein, as he was a powerful aura user capable of filling that void.  

Yet now, his armor was practically in tatters, and his body was riddled with battle scars.  

Among those injuries, the most grievous was his abdomen.  

A gaping wound that needed to be plugged with his hand, steadily oozing blood as if his insides would spill out with the slightest movement.  

And his opponent, who had caused that damage, stood there in relatively pristine condition. Although pale, he only bore a few scratch-like wounds on his limbs.  

Even that was the result of a combined effort from Jamie and two other superhumans.  

“Jamie, retreat!”  

“The damage is too severe. Fall back!”  

Old comrades from the Imperial Guard, Miles and Melvin, desperately stood their ground, protecting the injured Jamie.  

Yet even knowing this, he found it hard to move.  

If he retreated like this, one of his comrades, or perhaps even two, would surely lose their lives.  

The reason they struggled so fiercely was the bizarre magic that even weakened superhumans, but more than that, the sheer power of the enemy far surpassed the known intelligence.  

‘The Sword King was said to be among the lowest of the higher ranks…’

Crash!

Splat!

It was as if they aimed to destroy any space left for the Sword King to evade.

Kwa kwa kwa kwa kwa bang!  

‘What is that energy…?’  

Even the superhuman sight could barely keep up with the incredible movements.

Jamie poured all the energy he had been using to stop the bleeding from his abdomen into his spear, rushing forward with the sheer force of his desperation.  

He left his beloved steed behind, focusing on all the martial skills of his lifetime, letting adrenaline give strength to his legs as he charged.  

The explosive speed he unleashed with his legs was more powerful than that of a horse.  

Everything that was Jamie Gilan—the Lance Master—transformed into a red meteor racing behind Melvin, aiming to pierce the Sword King’s back.  

‘Success…!’  

Boom!  

As Jamie’s face rapidly paled at the outcome, a faint smile emerged.

“Melvin!!!!!”  

Melvin?

What appeared before him next was Melvin’s pale face, pierced through by Jamie’s spear.  

The shock of having killed a comrade knocked the breath from him.  

The mental impact was heavier than all the vitality stolen away. In an instant, he was frozen, unable to think.

‘Goddamn this!’  

Slap!

Understanding that, the reality of the matter changed the very essence of his fears.

Was he dreaming?  

Madness coursed through Matt Dickerson’s veins as he cried out in frustration.  

First, he had seen the wind itself fuming around.  

He couldn’t deny the presence of those wild rivals within combat, conspiring with a certain aspect that smothered them all below.  

And now, standing at the center of it all lay only a common “son-of-a-bitch.”

Kwakwaakwaakwaak!

In the northwestern region of Mackline, at the fortress established at the juncture of ‘Hunter’s Way,’ Shield.

Constructed under the pretense of maintaining peace along the North Road and protecting merchants, the fortress functioned solely as barracks and storage for food and weapons inside. The castle walls were undoubtedly thicker than ordinary structures, and the internal roads were designed for direct access from the walls to the gates.

Anyone who stepped inside this war-like fortress could instantly recognize it as a site for battle preparation.

The elite troops of the Mackline’s Second Legion gathered within this stronghold.

“Attention!”

As Louis entered the commander’s office in the heart of the fortress, the Swordmaster merely nodded and gazed out the window.

“Ah… Really? Hoho.”

A smile appeared on the Swordmaster’s face.

The magic circles installed in the fortress were a well-kept secret.

A 30% increase in vigor along with improved stamina recovery rates were merely ambiguous figures for knights confident in their physical control, turning it into something that could be merely seen as a ‘condition’ problem.

“Thanks to keeping our secret weapon hidden, the morale has risen unexpectedly. This is quite an unforeseen gain.”

“It’s good news for us.”

“Indeed. What about the other side?”

“Nothing in particular. For now….”

Louis’s responses were confident.

Having prepared for war for years, and with everything going smoothly, everything felt aligned for the impending conflict.

The second and third legions surrounded the Shield Fortress in the north, while the first legion gathered in the central area around Kyle Fortress, with reinforcements from the fourth and fifth legions on standby to assist from the north and south.

In addition, should the signals for war be raised, a self-defense force of over 500,000 would gather in strategic locations with repeating crossbows on hand.

Of course, the self-defense force couldn’t be compared directly to regular troops, yet the firepower they exhibited would be on par with one or two legions. Moreover, it could be anticipated to exhibit even greater efficiency in a defense battle, maximizing the effectiveness of the crossbows.

“That sounds good.”

“Yes.”

“Make training minimal, but keep morale high. The fate of the nation hinges on this impending war.”

“I will keep that in mind.”

“And concerning the information passed on by His Majesty, you should keep that to yourself for now.”

“Yes? What’s happened?”

“This situation seems beyond anything the Emperor anticipated.”

“??”

“When the war starts, the priests of the temple will treat the soldiers in the fortress. They will pretend to be a healing guild.”

“Yes!?”

That was indeed shocking news.

Under the pretense of noninterference in worldly matters, the temple had not provided assistance to any nation or territory during wartime. Hence they were conveying their intent to break this unspoken rule that had been sustained for hundreds of years for the sake of Mackline.

Though it was stated that the priests would disguise themselves as a healing guild, if they weren’t going to treat a select few, rumors would inevitably spread. It would surely disrupt the reputed neutrality of the temple.

“…Why?”

While it was surely good, Louis found himself bewildered by the motives behind it.

“Apparently it’s due to a debt incurred in the past.”

“Yes?”

“That’s how it is. In any case, since it’s been decided, keep the center of the barracks empty while conducting formation training. Ensure to have a unit for defense.”

With another major move set in play to exploit the Empire, a smile appeared on the Swordmaster’s face.

And at that moment—

– Your Grace, urgent news!

A frantic voice echoed from outside, signaling the start of war.

With a numerical advantage of more than double and a quality of forces that were incomparable, it seemed to be a reasonable expectation.  

However, once the battle commenced, the results were entirely different. The Imperial Army was completely overwhelmed on all three fronts.  

It took only a single day for the Imperial Army to lose over twenty percent of its total fighting strength and retreat. What’s worse, among the rumors that spread after this defeat were some that were utterly unbelievable.  

The Swordsman had died at the hands of Mackline’s Sun, despite being ambushed.  

Just a few months earlier, the Swordsman had been defeated by Sin-Kwon in the Nobians, causing a loss of prestige. Yet, facing the Swordsman again, there was no guarantee he would lose.  

At least, that’s what the Empire thought.  

However, if he were to die completely, the situation would be different. It would be a fall from which there was no return.  

The strongest swordsman on the continent had been defeated.  

Mackline’s Sun was now the strongest in the continent.  

The devastating loss, coupled with the rumors that spread afterward, further diminished the Empire’s standing.  

Though the retreating Imperial Army was still stationed in front of the enemy fortresses and castles, no one believed any longer in the Empire’s complete victory.  

* * *  

“There are three main reasons for our defeat.”  

A heavy silence that had engulfed the hall was broken by a weary voice.  

“First, Mackline’s superhuman capabilities far exceeded our expectations, or rather, they surpassed common sense.”  

Though it sounded like an excuse, many in the audience found themselves nodding unconsciously.  

Mackline’s superhuman strength had been shockingly astonishing.  

Completely incomprehensible.  

“We received reports indicating there would be hidden strength, and we dispatched 19 superhumans, including the Swordsman and the Gale. Even so, they were defeated.”  

The Prime Minister, Roctus Gusfelt, waited quietly for the Emperor’s reaction, but there was no voice from the upper seat.  

Calmly, he continued speaking.  

“It’s beyond common understanding that Logan Mackline has become strong enough to defeat the Swordsman, but what’s even more surprising is the beast that has already defeated three superhumans including Maxwell the commander from the southern fortress.”  

He refrained from mentioning the swordsman who had killed two superhumans at the northern fortress. In comparison, his power was not even worth mentioning.  

“The military has concluded that its true identity is a type of divine beast that vanished a millennium ago.”  

There was a voice from the upper seat for the first time.    

“… Divine beast?”  

In a calm but powerful voice that took charge of the hall’s atmosphere, Roctus swallowed hard.  

“Yes. We concluded there was no other possibility.”  

“Details.”  

“Yes. After researching ancient records, it seems that a beast or monster capable of facing three superhumans requires sacrifices of dozens of lives daily just to maintain its existence.”  

An invisible chain tightened around everyone’s necks.  

Feeling their lips dry and their skin growing tight with tension, Roctus quickly moistened his dry lips and continued speaking.  

“Even if there is a monster tamer or beast master from legends in Mackline who raised that creature, it is impossible that no rumors would have spread. If so, then the remaining possibility, however low it may be, is just that.”  

“Divine beast… Ah, divine beast…”  

The atmosphere grew quiet enough to hear the sound of finger taps against the armrest of the throne, as Roctus and the ministers silently awaited the Emperor’s words.  

After a moment, the Emperor spoke again.  

“When I visited the Empire over four years ago, it was merely a promising young pup who defeated the Swordsman, and the divinely rare divine beast served him due to his command, killing the Empire’s generals… ha. Is he some kind of hero granted by the gods?”  

None dared respond to the Emperor’s smirk.  

The revealed outcome was simply too outrageous to refute, and agreeing would imply admitting the Emperor was the enemy of a god-bestowed hero.  

The suffocating silence once again enveloped the hall until the Emperor’s voice broke the stillness.  

“And the second reason?”  

“Y-yes!? Ah… Yes. The second is the disposable artifact they call Liberatio. The bombs they’ve unleashed have overturned the tide of the battlefield by their inexplicably cheap production costs.”  

“Liberatio? Liberation… So, it means they would liberate the enemy’s souls? That’s dreadful.”  

Is he really expecting me to laugh at that?  

“Hmm, hmm. Initially, there were relevant reports, but I judged them too far-fetched to bring them before Your Majesty. Therefore, the responsible parties…”  

At that moment, a startled Roctus coughed and attempted to continue speaking when a calm voice suddenly cut in.  

“Capital punishment.”  

“… Yes?”  

“Compile a list of those who neglected that report and execute them all, regardless of rank.”  

Upon hearing this, Roctus’ expression darkened. Despite the calm tone, the Emperor’s intense rage was unmistakable.  

‘Of course, that’s only natural. His Majesty would be most enraged… but…’  

That rage, if excessively released, could further decrease the morale of an already low military.  

Roctus forcibly swallowed his heart’s voice that had risen to his throat.  

Speaking such foolish advice at this moment would mean a worthless death for both the Empire and for the Emperor.  

“… Yes. I shall do so.”  

“And the third?”  

“The third reason is the great magic circles that have been installed around every city and fortress. They have created a drop in combat effectiveness among Imperial knights and soldiers by nearly 30 percent, no matter their rank.”  

“And Gale? What did he have to say?”  

“There is said to be a genius mage in Mackline. Baron Galen has reported that he met a magician who hasn’t even reached adulthood. It’s highly likely that the magic circles were the work of that mage.”  

“A minor mage in this era? Huh…”  

After finishing his report, Roctus bowed his head.  

However, he felt a serious internal conflict. The fact was he had another piece of information he needed to report.  

But…  

‘Is it right to share this with His Majesty now?’  

Fearful that he might ignite a trigger in a volatile situation, Roctus bit his lip.  

The Empire belonged to the Emperor. He believed he shouldn’t decide on their direction.  

“And, there is an uncertain fourth reason.”  

“Uncertain?”  

“Yes. There is no proof, only speculation; thus, I did not include it within the previous three reasons.”  

“Speak.”  

“… Before that, I wish to ask if others could be excused.”  

At that moment, a peculiar light flickered in the Emperor’s black eyes. Requesting a private audience during such a perilous atmosphere could be interpreted as Roctus putting his life on the line.  

The Emperor waved his hand.  

“I will give my instructions through the Prime Minister later. All of you, leave and wait.”  

“Yes, Your Majesty!”  

The ministers replied in unison as they carefully exited the hall, their footsteps echoing like receding tides.  

Once the door to the hall closed, the Emperor nodded slowly, and Roctus quickly continued to speak.  

“It seems that the horrific outcome of the initial battles largely stemmed from the three reasons mentioned.”  

“Additionally, the civilian army assembled in the center played a role as well…”  

“Get to the point.”  

Roctus, lengthening his words in an attempt to ease the Emperor’s psychological shock, suddenly held his breath.  

In that moment, he swallowed and slowly opened his mouth.  

“From what I can ascertain, the superhuman forces deployed on all three marching routes were perfectly positioned to target our superhumans. While the legion’s deployment may be unknown, the positioning of the superhumans, particularly those of the Imperial Guard, is classified within the Empire…”  

“… There are traitors among the high-ranking officials?”  

“I am merely offering a conjecture that such a thing is possible.”  

As Roctus’ words shifted from speculation to suspicion, the Emperor’s gaze grew increasingly sharp.  

“Traitor, traitor…”  

Tap, tap, tap.  

The Emperor’s fingers drummed against the throne’s armrest for a long moment.  

‘What should I do if he intends to overturn the Empire’s leadership during this period?’  

Before him, Roctus felt as if he could barely breathe.  

After a moment, a calm voice emerged.  

“I have focused too much on the holy nation. Ultimately, it is all my fault.”  

Stunned by the unexpected statement, Roctus hurriedly bowed his head.  

“Such a ridiculous statement! How could it be Your Majesty’s fault? It is the faults of the incompetent ministers! Please withdraw your words!”  

Thud. Thud.  

Repeatedly banging his head, Roctus’ forehead quickly turned a bright red as the Emperor calmly continued.  

“Who do you suspect to be those rat-like traitors?”  

“Unfortunately, it’s the Dongwangbu. Princess Louise is still within Mackline’s royal castle. They secretly aided in the construction of Mackline’s fortress under the pretext of their engagement.”  

“Gerard? The fellow’s daughter is still in Mackline… It certainly is suspicious. But if he were the one behind this, he wouldn’t operate with such clumsiness. He’s not that foolish.”  

“I am merely stating suspicions. There is a previous case.”  

Though it seemed plausible, the Emperor didn’t accept it outright.  

“Above all, the fellow lacks the guts to betray the royal family. He killed his own wife to protect his seat.”  

“As I mentioned earlier, I’m only suggesting possibilities as rumors have surfaced.”  

“No, that’s enough. Fine, we can investigate.”  

The royal family’s special investigation department is not solely specialized in assassination attempts.  

With that statement, the Emperor dismissed the controversy around the traitor and unexpectedly raised another topic.  

“Do you know how divine beasts are treated in holy temples?”  

Though the question seemed odd, the Prime Minister recalled his knowledge.  

“Ah… There are records indicating that the ancient orders did not acknowledge divine beasts. The records state they hunted them for invading the sanctity of the Nine Gods. However, the reestablished order post-Resolutium no longer mentions divine beasts at all.”  

“Indeed. By that time, they had ceased to exist.”  

“Correct.”  

Why suddenly mention the temple?  

Ah, could it be…?  

“Convey to the holy nation that there are rumors of a divine beast appearing in Mackline, a divine beast that wields power transcending the Nine Gods. Inform that we’ve confirmed it in the name of the Empire.”  

“Ah!”  

“This isn’t the first time there’ve been issues regarding ‘The Forsaken Ones’ in Mackline. If we link that with this divine beast, the holy nation will surely intervene.”  

Surely, the holy nation wouldn’t ignore the Empire’s intentions to invade their jurisdiction.  

Rodie certainly wouldn’t doubt that they intended to wield the holy temple for the sake of warfare.  

However, Roctus felt a sense of foreboding that he could stake his life on.  

Fanatics place faith before rationality, that is precisely why they are called fanatics.  

‘Using a single ancient record to maneuver…’  

Roctus was inwardly amazed when the Emperor spoke again.  

“After that, I will personally march to conquer Mackline.”  

“Your Majesty!?”  

“Mobilize all Imperial Guards and the palace’s central army. I will personally rectify the deviated grand plan.”  

Roctus’ eyes widened in disbelief.
