“Here they come!”  

Thud thud thud.  

Stephan Royer grit his teeth as he looked towards the large army approaching from the front.  

With his white hair and white eyebrows, and appearance that glimmered youthfully despite being of the age of sixty, he was a true aura user. His meticulous nature added to his clean appearance. He was known as the Knight of the Holy Spirit, a fitting title for one who symbolized the purity of the gods.  

Having lived more than half his life battling the monstrous creatures, he had faced countless crises, but never had he felt such overwhelming despair.  

Yet he couldn’t show his feelings. After all, he was the deputy commander of the Holy Knight Order, the largest and most prestigious knight order on the continent.  

“Stay calm and wait for orders!”  

Stephan tried to project confidence as he felt the gazes of the soldiers looking at him. Then he glared at the rear of the Western 2nd Legion charging ahead.  

There stood a single knight, gradually increasing speed and momentum as he watched the rushing forces.  

He was a massive figure, riding a horse far larger than normal, shouldering a gigantic axe lance.  

He was Miles Boykin, the general of the Western 2nd Legion, one formidable foe whom Stephan was tasked to confront here at the North Gate.  

‘They say his nickname is Guillotine.’  

Just glancing from afar at the towering figure that appeared to exceed two meters swinging a massive axe lance, he understood why such a fearsome moniker was given.  

That man was likely waiting for the clash of the two armies, planning to jump into the fray at the point of weakness.  

And it was Stephan’s responsibility to stop that monster.  

Imagining the flow of combat in his mind, he suddenly felt the man’s gaze lifted towards the walls.  

Even from this distance, it was strange not to see the eyes beneath the helmet, yet Stephan was certain he was smiling brightly inside that helmet.  

‘Didn’t he say he took pleasure in executing criminals? If it’s true, he’s truly insane…’  

In the battlefield, such a warrior would fit perfectly.  

As Stephan stared at him with increasingly heavy eyes, he heard a voice from the farthest eastern gate.  

– The Nine Gods bless us! Smite the enemies of the gods!  

It was the voice of the only superior he acknowledged, the commander of the Holy Knight Order, the Holy Sword.  

On the sprawling walls of Nobiense, which could hardly be described as merely wide, the voice echoed even when it shouldn’t have reached Stephan’s ears, but the superhuman sensed it clearly.  

Thus, he shouted even before the flag signals were given.  

“Crush the enemies!!!”  

As soon as the command left his lips, a barrage of arrows rained down from the walls.  

The arrows shot by the soldiers of the Holy Legion pierced through the enemy’s ranks like beams of light.  

“Ugh!”  

“Argh!”  

“Advance! Advance!”  

The first effect of the divine barrier covering the city of Nobiense, amplifying the power of projectiles shot from the walls, came into clear view on the battlefield.  

The arrows shot from standard longbows easily penetrated the armor of the Imperial soldiers.  

Among them, the 300 rapid-fire crossbows that had recently been hurriedly supplied under the name ‘Mack’ showcased even more explosive power.  

“Ugh!”  

“What is this?!”  

As the quarrels shot from the rapid-fire crossbows pierced through the armor of the approaching knights, many fell from their horses.  

‘Huh?’  

The striking power was shocking enough to widen Stephan’s eyes, yet despite such aggressive displays, the majority of the thousands of knights at the forefront managed to close in on the walls through the torrential rain of arrows.  

Heavily armored knights leapt with ease from the ground as they charged towards the walls.  

Watching them, Stephan waved his hand towards the priests positioned at the back of the soldiers.  

“The Barrier of the Gods!”  

“The Barrier of the Gods!”  

The knights on either side chanted in unison as they fervently waved their flags.  

In an instant, as the command spread across the entire wall, the priests stepped forward, joining their hands and kneeling before the walls.  

At a glance, it looked almost like a form of suicide, but only for a brief moment.  

White beams of light erupted from the bodies of the lined-up priests, forming a brilliant hemispherical barrier that enveloped the entire wall. This divine force should have been invisible to the eyes of ordinary people but manifested as a protective barrier thanks to the priests.  

This too was a function of the divine barrier—the amplification of divine power.  

The knights from the Empire, having reached right before the wall, crashed into an invisible wall and fell without understanding what had just happened.    

And seizing that moment, soldiers from the Holy Legion, bursting forth from behind the priests, hurled spears imbued with white light towards the Imperial knights.  

“Die!”  

“Divine Retribution!”  

Not every soldier of the Holy Legion was at the level of elite knights, but this too was part of the barrier’s effect, a combat enhancement granted to equipment sanctified with holy water.  

Of course, this didn’t make their ordinary spears turn into divine weapons, but the brilliance of the spears and the holy light’s shield took the soldiers’ morale to new heights, yielding destruction beyond their usual capabilities.  

Swish.  

“Argh!”  

“Gah!”  

“Come, monster!”  

Several knights, unable to maintain their balance in the air, were skewered by the spears launched by the soldiers.  

Their screams echoed in the air, but the damage they inflicted was not significant.  

And crucially, there were a few strong individuals who could not be obstructed merely by the soldier’s fierce struggles backed by the holy shield.  

“Die! Get away!”  

A short knight wielded an axe lance even larger than his own body.  

Yet, the head of the axe glowed with a brilliant red aura, making its blade appear twice as large from a distance.  

The Proof Blade of a supreme knight.  

Just the sight of him allowed Stephan to identify the knight’s identity.  

‘Jaxen Flo.’  

One of the elite commanders of the Western 2nd Legion, his attack sliced through the priests’ protective barrier and struck down five priests and soldiers at once.  

“Argh!”  

“He’s broken through!”  

Damn.  

His hands trembled with fear, but Stephan couldn’t move.  

The knight had positioned himself right at the wall’s edge. With the superhuman, Miles moving below the wall, he couldn’t recklessly move from the middle of the wall.  

But with that as a basis, the remaining four knights were following suit, eagerly breaking through the protective barrier and surging onto the walls.  

They split to either side with a taunting display.  

“Hahaha!”  

“All of you shall die!”  

An articulated bloodbath stirred unmistakably on either end of the wall where Stephan stood.  

His face twisted with tension.  

‘They can’t be…!?’

In an effort to stop them, numerous leaders from the Holy Knight Order rushed towards the end of the wall.  

Red auras flickered from their weapons while holy light danced around their bodies, amplifying their physical power, but it seemed frivolous when compared to the solidified Proof Blade they were about to clash against.  

And sure enough.  

“Argh!”  

As soon as their weapons collided, one leader fell, blood spraying from their body.  

Damn it.  

Cursing to himself, Stephan gritted his teeth.  

While the holy knights who had honed both holy power and force were compared to other knights in their class deemed powerful, there were tragically few top-tier fighters among them.  

Moreover, the commanders capable of standing against top-tier knights from the Holy Knight Order were mostly concentrated at the eastern wall, where the enemies were.  

Facing a commander by his lonesome, even six or so leaders could barely withstand the effects of the barrier.  

‘How dare they!’  

Even as he had a strong desire to rush in and slice them into pieces, his gaze was still locked on the Guillotine, Miles Boykin.  

Moving would not be so easy. If the enemy took advantage of his movement, the whole defense line could collapse.  

But ironically, Miles appeared to be slowing down just below the walls.  

‘Is this really…?’  

Both the elite commanders and Miles seemed to be operating upon the assumption that these scenarios were already anticipated.  

Stephan’s white eyebrows quivered lightly.  

‘If I just stay idle, I will only be a fool.’  

A multitude of scenarios rushed through his mind, and the sight of the enemy commander’s figure below the walls only solidified his thoughts.  

It almost seemed to challenge him, saying, if you want to fight, come down here.  

“Argh!”  

Amid the sounds of battle filling the air, Stephan finally drew his sword.  

‘I have no choice.’  

However, if he moved to one side, the commander was bound to gamble on the other flank.  

Thankfully, there was a way.  

This northern gate was given to him most importantly because there were nearly no responsible holy knights present to guard it.  

‘Now is not the time to worry about what’s behind me.’  

With determination, Stephan clenched his jaw and raised his sword.  

“God! Bestow your strength upon this place!”  

With that cry, white light surged from his body.  

Soon, a brilliant sacred light began to spread around him, encompassing the wider northern wall in its glow.  

Woosh.  

Suddenly, all allies within the sphere of light felt energized.  

Minor wounds healed instantly, minds cleared, and fatigue dissipated. Even the heavily injured holy knights began to rise with a blush on their otherwise pale faces.  

The Knight of the Holy Spirit, Stephan Royer, possessed a unique characteristic: ‘Blessing of Light.’  

In a battlefield where formidable forces collided, this trait was evaluated as having an effect greater than even the Holy Sword.  

“Ugh!”  

“God’s with us!”  

“Perish!”  

For just an instant, the leaders who were on the defensive against the incoming assaults began to push back against their enemies.  

“You fanatic bastards shall all die!”

“Be the one to die!”

“Don’t retreat!”  

With a swift execution, he held the slain knight’s head aloft, boldly proclaiming.  

However, in response, a fearsome knight unveiled himself on the opposite wall, pouring a stream of red aura.  

“Here I come!”  

With a bizarrely comedic line, the enormous knight wielded the axe lance upon reaching the wall, simultaneously shredding through several knights and soldiers clustered nearby.  

“Urgh!”  

“Monster!”  

“Ughha!”  

Stephan’s vision turned a furious hue upon witnessing the scene.  

That vile creature!  

Fury blazed in Stephan’s eyes as he charged towards him, ignoring the Empire soldiers who approached.  

Upon the encounter, the massive knight smiled beneath his helmet, revealing a maddening grin.  

“At last, I’ve been waiting, White Knight!”  

He stood atop a pile of the corpses of several allies.  

“You monster!”  

Rumble.  

“Urgh!”  

Each clash of the towering axe lance against his smaller, lighter sword should have been to Stephan’s disadvantage; however, they didn’t follow normal logic in battles of superhumans.  

“Ugh, as expected….”  

It was the Guillotine, Miles Boykin, who staggered back significantly.  

Still, his expression didn’t appear particularly disgruntled.

His words hinted at something dark. It was as if he was aware that one of the greatest disadvantages of the Blessing of Light was the severe consumption of divine power and stamina.  

Yet, Stephan’s voice remained unwavering.  

“I won’t fall until I kill you!”

He utilized his tremendous size and strength to deflect Stephan’s attacks while consistently wielding the axe with unmatched ferocity, purposefully avoiding any opening that would allow Stephan to land a hit.  

He relied entirely on stalling for time.  

‘He really is mad,…’  

It was glaringly different from the rumors he had previously heard.  

After all, obtaining the position of commander in the Empire was not something that one simply received.  

But Stephan too held pride and resolve as a holy knight.  

‘I will not fall until you regret your actions!’  

Although the Blessing of Light now continued to drain his holy power and force, this was within a barrier. His divine power was gradually recovering, and he was confident that he would not fall easily as Miles anticipated.  

Above all,  

– Sir Stephan. We’ve purposefully stationed the weakest forces behind you. It’s because we believe in you…. I’m sorry.

The idiotic genius junior who once refrained from taking the commander position just because he was deemed a senior by that all-encompassing genius.

“I will not fall!!”

The knight’s gaze behind the visor shook with uncertainty.  

That sensation was surely detected elsewhere.

“Stay away! I’ve got this!”

Yet the situation beyond the northern walls didn’t appear as favorable.  

“Block them!”  

“Argh!”  

“The enemies are too… many!”  

Screams erupted from all directions.

Originally, when considering the lineup, he had only planned to include these two and Burdel.  

It would be a selfish decision to send his wife, yet it seemed she had quite a different perspective.  

“The lineup is perfect, isn’t it? What’s more, I have the clear advantage in survival. I also have ample experience with cross-dressing from the kingdom’s alliance.”  

“…No.”  

“You keep glancing at Sir Viktor and Count Ronian, but those two risk potential problems due to their distinguishing appearance. That leaves no one more suitable than me.”  

“…Hmmm.”  

Her logic was flawless.  

Ironically, Logan, the selfish and pathetic husband, was left sincerely desiring for approval from the household’s elders.  

At that moment, the Sword Saint coughed politely and stepped forward.  

“Your Majesty, I believe it’s highly unwise for the queen of one kingdom to participate in warfare for another kingdom as a mercenary…”  

“My, Chancellor. I’m not going as the Queen of the McLain Kingdom but as Ahmud Hassan the ‘Guardian of Terronan.’ Ah, if anything goes wrong, it’d be best to maintain a separate identity altogether.”  

The Sword Saint found himself at a loss for words as dismay washed over his features. This time, the father-in-law joined the fray.  

“The foundation of a kingdom is its royal family, and at the helm of royalty, there lies the safety of the royal family. The king and queen must guard their positions if the kingdom is to remain steadfast…”  

“The king has vacated his seat numerous times. Besides, thanks to that, we’ve cultivated a solid backup. You needn’t worry, Father.”  

“…What?”  

Padric’s apparent astonishment displayed his previous ignorance concerning Logan’s covert activities in McLain territory.  

Witnessing such a reaction brought Logan to his knees in utter despair. It seemed no one bothered to care about what he was dealing with.  

Eilen’s glare set upon him with a facial expression of exasperation.  

“Is there something odd about that? Are you implying that I cannot step in where only Ahmud can?”  

“Ah, Hahaha, surely you wouldn’t want your wife to be on the battlefield wielding a sword.”  

Eilen’s immediate reaction was an unamused scowl, while Logan, who knew all too well how flawed such an inference sounded, swiftly dismissed it.  

The stern queen was hard to ignore and appeared as if she was about to blow up.  

If one fell toward the depths of that scrutiny, creating justifications to act would be a necessity.  

Slowly developing a bleak frustration, he glanced at Viktor to see that he was shaking his head fervently, a clear indication of his disapproval.  

Yet, Clayton nodded cautiously, as if assessing the risk.  

As if intending to proceed with this profound conversation, Logan’s mind boiled frantically.  

With hidden determination, he finally proclaimed,  

“Right. But let’s take Ronian, Viktor, and Burdel along as well.”  

“….Yes?”  

Everybody froze upon hearing those words.  

“Your Majesty! That is excessive…”  

The Sword Saint hurriedly added, warning Logan of the impending disaster.  

But, undoubtedly, those astoundingly hopeful words baffled every individual present.  

“Sir, do you really think we can stretch ourselves so thinly?”  

“No. Our opponent is the Empire. We need to take every feasible measure. Let’s use all the unknown superhumans we can.”  

So flowing was the hope within that royal atmosphere, it seemed like the only feasible direction to proceed.  

“For if the Holy Kingdom defeats the Empire in war, that would be the best of all outcomes.”  

Everyone appeared contemplative hearing those words, whether it be filled with hesitant smiles or uncertainty.  

The outcomes seemed alarmingly optimistic considering their known disadvantages, thus consensus began to effortlessly give ground before Logan’s persuasive words.  

The kingdom’s upper echelon was sealed at last with Logans’s proclamation, despite the risk Symphony Mages were grumbling about previous specifics of target drill grounds.

As though she had never faltered at all.

“Yes. We did. It’s just a feeling…it’s probably just that.”  

Like a single stone tossed into a well, thoughts swirled around in his mind.  

“I feel uneasy…”  

However, upon glancing at the serious expression on Ailene’s face, he could not suppress a smile. Who would lighten his mood could not be any soul but hers.  

“… It’s settled now.”  

“Really?”  

“My worries are gone, so we should head inside.”  

“… I didn’t do anything?”  

“You did. Quite a lot.”  

“Huh?”  

She understood little of his words, but her confusion was undeniably charming. He simply took her hand, feeling warmth rush over his chest.  

Yet it looked as though Ailene’s thoughts did not remain inconspicuous.  

“The 2nd Prince… Why is he in the Holy Kingdom?”  

Suddenly dropping that line right before they reached their quarters made Logan halt.  

“Pardon? Why are you…?”  

“You’ve felt uneasy about the Holy Kingdom’s situation.”  

“Ah…”  

It seemed she misunderstood him.  

What he was troubled by was the Emperor’s ulterior motives, yet…  

Having her concern for him was appreciated. Thus, he answered with a smile.  

“Simply, it’s because of the 2nd Prince. He was probably trying to gain a foothold within the Holy Kingdom, but somehow, he fell out with the plans.”  

“Why is he remaining in the Holy Kingdom instead of returning to the Empire?”  

“Well, if he simply returns, he would be in a tight spot, you see?”  

“Then wouldn’t staying there mean he won’t be cornered?”   

Such trivially uncommon dialogue between a king and queen seemed overly casual, and at that moment, Logan’s battered mind seemed to clear.  

“That’s… not really the case.”  

He pondered briefly before responding.  

“Now, if he leads the Holy Kingdom like that, it may become untenable.”  

“Then he cannot merely remain there to evade trouble?”  

“Well… no, that’s not the point.”  

But suddenly, a thought looped inside his mind.  

“Perhaps he keeps the position to gain grounds— to establish justification if the Emperor seeks to swallow the Holy Kingdom.”  

“Is he calculating strategy in such a manner?”  

Logan’s thoughts tangled again.  

“Now wait a minute… If the Crown Prince remains stranded there… and dies for no apparent reason, that would make the justification for the Empire to advance upon Holy Kingdom sound.”  

“What? No way!”  

“Yes— it becomes a rationale for the Empire to conquer the Holy Kingdom.”  

As if she too had suddenly felt the cruel layers of reality weave, Ailene grasped her mouth, recoiling.  

“… But that can’t happen. Even if such a plot exists among the nobles, surely not from our Emperor.”  

“Right?”  

“You can’t just suggest he would…”  

“He could, yes?”  

Even if it seemed suspicious, Logan felt that intuitive fear surge up again.  

“Do you think he could care less? If the Empire’s might weren’t to play and was drafted with the intentions of sacrifice…”  

“Speculating so certainly, no one would be able to act…”  

“But let’s not ignore it.”  

Eventually, Logan found himself forced to turn rigid, tight-lipped as their conjectures headed deeper still.  

“Can we contact the Saint right now?”  

“… Well, try.”  

“Damn it…”  

Without further hesitation, Logan dashed to the communication room in a frenzy as if going mad through the night.



-chapter 366-

Cardinal Tracey appeared at the religious trial.

In just one week, the Holy City had been swept by urgent changes, causing the gazes of the citizens of Nobens to converge once again on the central shrine.

“It hasn’t even been a few months since His Holiness ascended to the papacy…”

“Doesn’t it seem like too many incidents have occurred lately?”

“What in the world is happening…?”

Due to the nature of religion, it inherently tends to become conservative as time passes. People lean towards stability rather than change. 

The residents of the Holy City possess an unwavering faith, yet recent events—including the impeachment of the previous pope—have left them feeling as if an unprecedented calamity had struck.

Adding to this unease were whispers of an impending military presence.

“I heard an army from the Empire is coming?”

“Who said that?”

“That’s nonsense!”

Initially just a rumor, the alarming news—that nearly 10,000 Imperial troops were rushing towards the Holy City—spread among the locals.

During this anxious time, one noble individual present was trembling with impatience.

“Not yet? It’s still not here!?”

Inside the spacious study, a young man paced back and forth, his anxiousness now familiar to his companions.

“…Your Highness, preemptively advancing the trial three days from now seems unnecessary.”

Leos’s reply was drenched in deep concern.

“And the forces of the Swordmaster and the Sorceress of Sorrowing Winds?”

“At this rate, they should arrive in two days.”

The prince’s expression tightened further at the words, while they both failed to notice the one-eyed knight standing quietly in a corner, squeezing his eyes shut.

Even if he had cared, he would have considered that they shared the same feelings.

‘What am I supposed to do?’

In Jerome Decade’s heart, a storm was raging.

—Before the troops of the Swordmaster and the Sorceress arrive, kill Barros and disguise it as the work of the Holy Nation.

The secret command that weighed heavily on his conscience was delivered in the names of the Emperor and his master. It weighed down upon him like a great burden.

It was no ordinary command; it was directed at none other than the prince, someone he had sworn to support in becoming the next Emperor.

The loyalty of a knight clashed with the orders of an Emperor.

The internal conflict continued to deepen, and just as he tightly shut his eyes, hurried voices echoed in his ears.

“Isn’t it just an excuse to associate with Max?”

“Yes. For now, Triss and Galen are planning to visit the Holy City under that pretext.”

“Pfft, bringing an army? Who would believe that?”

“But it’s quite a vague number. It doesn’t seem like they have any intention of launching an occupation.”

“True. However, if the identity of the Black Serpent is revealed during the trial, they’ll rush in claiming they’ll kill the Empire’s foes. There’s justification concerning Max involved as well.”

“But Cardinal Tracey seems to be cornered now. Given how things are, isn’t it possible that His Majesty might accede to the Emperor’s demands?”

“What? Hand over the authority of the Holy See or serve the Empire? Not a chance. It’s not Cardinal Tracey who is cornered—it’s the Black Serpent that’s in danger. That old man isn’t even present in the Holy Nation.”

While Leos optimistically expressed his ideas, Barros dismissed those hopes.

Indeed, the statement was objectively true.

Despite the gravity of the situation that risked his own fate, he displayed cold judgment.

And this made Leos feel all the more frustrated.

‘If it weren’t for that incident with Mackline…’

Had he not faltered back then, he would have overcome the imperial succession war without issue, instead of quivering in anxiety in a place that was not even the imperial capital.

However, he could not afford to wallow in such regret now.

“Then how about we keep Cardinal Tracey detained? If we’re going to reject His Majesty’s will, we should at least cover our tracks…”

“No. I was the one to involve them in the first place. Cutting off just one of their tails won’t absolve me.”

“I heard Prince Klyd also made a significant mistake concerning them. If everything is handled well…”

“They’re the ones behind that mistake, so ultimately it means I’ll bear the brunt.”

“If we assist Lord Triss in taking control of the Holy Nation…?”

“That would just be borrowing someone else’s plate for my meal. They wouldn’t recognize even the spoon I added to the meal.”

Their conversation continued to hover aimlessly without reaching a definitive conclusion.

The fiery sunset cast a crimson hue through the window, as if the tension in the air were coloring the room with anxiousness.

Jerome, unable to summon the courage to interrupt, absentmindedly gazed at the shining red light when Barros’s voice jolted him from his thoughts.

“Jerome, do you have any ideas?”

“…Uh, yes?”

“I’m asking how to halt the army of your master and your uncle.”

The clear intent behind the inquiry struck Jerome. However, what he could say had its limits.

“…I’m sorry, Your Highness. Those are individuals who do not act based on personal connections.”

“I see. But just throw out any ideas. Sometimes good ideas emerge when one is tossing thoughts around.”

“Ah… yes.”

What could he possibly think of?

He couldn’t shake off the turmoil within his heart.

“Therefore, if there is a strategy that comes to mind, speak it directly.”

“I will, Your Highness.”

“Good.”

The weight of the hand on his shoulder felt akin to a burden that crushed him.

Jerome perceived his own face hardening like stone.

Suddenly, a voice interrupted.

—”The Saint has arrived.”

An unexpected visitor entered.

“An audience? Suddenly?”

The sudden appearance of the Saint raised eyebrows due to the urgency of her business.

“Yes. I have something important to discuss with you, just the two of us.”

Barros felt perplexed.

Herstian had raised a matter that required him to be cautious in light of ongoing issues with the Black Serpent. Thus, he had been trying to limit interactions with her as much as possible. Now the crux of the matter was coming to meet him herself.

And a private audience at that?

‘What does this mean?’

He scrutinized her, but the enigmatic figure of the Saint, with her silvery hair and white robe accentuated by striking azure eyes, gave nothing away. 

Her beauty was stunning, but it was her composed demeanor that left a lasting impression.

Having no valid reason to refuse, Barros could only nod in acquiescence.

“…Understood. You may leave us for now.”

“Yes, My Lord.”

“Yes, Your Highness.”

Leos and Jerome complied promptly without hesitation.

However, even after their departure, the Saint continued to gaze at Barros without uttering a word.

“…Saint?”

In this awkward atmosphere, Barros reluctantly broke the silence, only for the Saint to deliver an unexpected remark.

“Ah, it seems someone has not left yet…”

Barros widened his eyes in surprise and released a brief sigh, realizing there was no option available to him now.

“Number One, are you present?”

—”…Yes, Your Highness.”

A voice resonated from the empty space.

However, the Saint seemed unperturbed by the presence, revealing no surprise at all.

‘Even a ghost that I could hardly detect without using my characteristics…’

As the weight of the term ‘Saint’ pressed heavily upon him, she suddenly closed her eyes and clasped her hands together.

Instantly, she began murmuring something under her breath.

In a flash, a sphere of pure white light enveloped her form.

‘The Sacred Barrier!’

A unique art among the two main branches of divine magic, the Barrier Art, which required substantial divine energy—there were few priests capable of weaving it. Even Barros had never seen it manifested by an individual before.

“Now we can speak freely.”

“…Impressive.”

Barros couldn’t help but express his surprise, amazed that such secrecy was achieved just for a private conversation.

However, the Saint’s forthcoming words exceeded all his foresight.

“Barros, how much do you trust His Majesty?”

“…What do you mean by that?”

His inability to grasp her intent sent a ripple of unease through Barros.

“…I’ve heard tales from those surrounding me, and while they may merely be presumptions, if they ever materialized, the ensuing chaos would be tremendous.”

The lengthy introduction suggested the seriousness of what was to follow, which sufficiently unsettled Barros.

As the words continued to spiral through his mind, the seriousness of the matter loomed large.

“…Wow. What absurdity… Could the Emperor wish to eliminate me…?”

A sound escaped him, muffled like a groan.

The tension in his clenched fists betrayed his helplessness.

“I understand this may sound absurd and highly disrespectful as an assumption. Yet, as I mentioned earlier, if by any chance this happens…”

“No. That can’t be.”

Barros shook his head vigorously, as if to dismiss the thought while muttering like a lunatic.

“Very well expressed. That truly clears my mind.”

Despite his words, his face was pale, and his gaze was frightened.

“Forgive my insolence, but…”

“Absolutely not! That speculation holds a high probability.”

Barros’s conviction remained resolute.

“Yes?”

“If I were in the Emperor’s shoes, I would likely act in the same manner. That would indeed be the Empire’s best course of action.”

The ease at which Barros accepted this assumption caused the Saint’s eyes to widen.

While she merely pondered the ‘potential’, he nonchalantly embraced an idea that horrified her.

“What on earth do you mean…?”

“Before you respond, allow me a moment to raise my voice.”

Suddenly, Barros sprang to his feet, a flicker of madness coursing through him.

“Argh! Damn it! This is ridiculous!!!”

A shriek erupted as he yanked at his hair.

“Am I meant to be sacrificed?! ME?!”

Thud! Thud!

He slammed his head against the magical shield with a heavy thud, proving that he truly had lost touch with reason, and during this moment, Ilia couldn’t help but worry for him.

Yet at the culmination of his breakdown, Barros fell silent.

“Haah, I apologize for that.”

With disheveled hair and bleeding lips, his flushed face bore witness to the fraying edges of his composure.

“I thought I viewed the situation impartially, yet I had underestimated the reality. Thank you for opening my eyes, Saint.”

“Oh, no. It’s nothing. But truly…?”

“Yes. I have squandered my time idly. That speculation indeed holds the highest likelihood. And if it is true, then the one executing it shall likely be… Haah. How wise that you decided to have a private conversation. Thank you, Saint.”

For Ilia, who only intended to discuss the risks of the encounter, it felt bewildering just how perilous the essence of his words truly was.

At that moment, she immediately grasped the concealed meaning hidden in Barros’s conversation.

Her expression stiffened, akin to that of Barros’s own.

“Then…”

“It would be best to take your leave now. Without delay, I must devise an escape plan. This way, Saint, it should suffice for you, yes?”

His darkened, sharp gaze implied intention beyond mere words.

The revelation enveloped Ilia, choking her with the magnitude of her shame.

Wordlessly, she turned to leave, and the returning companions were taken aback by Barros’s sudden transformation.

“What? Your Highness!?”

“What on earth did the Saint do to him!?”

As Leos and Jerome expressed their rage at Barros’s pitiful state, he simply waved them away.

“Enough. Don’t worry. I’ve gained immensely important intelligence. It seems I need to revise my plans.”

“What do you mean by that?”

“I’ll first strike at Tracy.”

“Excuse me?”

Taken aback by this sudden proclamation, Leos hesitated.

Yet Barros did not offer a lengthy explanation, seemingly unwilling to elaborate.

“Number One, are you still there?”

—”Yes, Your Highness.”

“Retrieve that ‘item’ from Cardinal Tracy. Use any means necessary. Time is limited. I’ll allow you two days; set out immediately.”

—”…Yes, Your Highness.”

Upon hearing that response, the still squinting Barros let out a long sigh, noticing his companions’ confusion in their gazes.

“Jerome, could you see if Number One is still in the vicinity?”

“Yes? Ah, yes.”

The moment his single remaining eye shimmered subtly with silvery light, he swiftly scanned his surroundings and shook his head.

“There’s no one.”

“Really?”

Nodding in affirmation, Barros then beckoned Leos and Jerome to come closer, leaning in to whisper.

“It seems His Majesty intends to kill me. And if that is to occur, the likely executors will be ghosts.”

Their brows furrowed deeply—a statement that left both subordinates overwhelmed.



-chapter 370-

Have you ever experienced the feeling of complete exhaustion, only to find a sense of pride and fulfillment within that weariness?

Have you ever felt like your body was about to collapse while your spirit sang with joy?

Harmon, known as the Divine Sword, had encountered such moments in the distant recesses of his memory.

‘The first time I held a sword.’

Back then, watching himself improve day by day had brought him immense joy and happiness. During those times, he had often felt more delight from his personal growth than from the will of the gods.

However, after reaching a certain level of mastery, those feelings faded. There were no longer any challengers around him, and it had been years since he had reached the pinnacle of his training.

He felt no regret over the conclusion of experiences that pushed his body to its limits and beyond that barrier.

As his soul ascends, so does his strength, leading to the rise of his mastery. Superhumans are defined by their transcendental abilities; meaningless physical abuse does not contribute to training.

At least, that’s what he had believed.

Until just a moment ago.

‘That wasn’t the case!’

Shudder.

The exhilarating aftermath of their recent clash lingered, filling him with bliss.

Though he had suffered no injuries, the impact had left a significant mark on both of their bodies due to their auras.

Both he and his opponent would spend some time recovering their forces, but it had been worth it.

The energy, squeezed to the limit for the first time in over ten years, along with his exhausted body, had drastically elevated his spirit. After years of dismissing physical training, the path on the other side of the wall he had long felt was impassable began to reveal itself before him.

It seemed the ‘rival’ visible through the settling dust shared similar feelings. The trembling energy exuded from them conveyed a mutual sense of exhilaration.

And the fact that this battle took place in Nobiense, within its sacred grounds, was a tremendous fortune for him.

‘I may have suffered a bit, just a tiny bit.’

The difference was negligible.

With just one mistake or oversight, the tide could easily turn.

Still, in the intense exchanges between superhumans at the highest level, such errors were virtually impossible. Thus, if the battle between them persisted in such a near-exhausted state, he would ultimately have faced defeat.

This, however, was the center of the sacred city. Unlike the sword master, who had only brought six Imperial knights with him, there were Holy Knights in abundance surrounding them.

Most of the approaching auras reflected that of the Holy Knights.

“…It’s unfortunate. I suppose I shall plan for our next encounter.”

The Imperial Supreme Sword, glaring at Harmon, must have seen the wall that lay beyond too, yet his gaze was more reminiscent of disappointment than expectation.

A seasoned warrior, boasting remarkable power even as he aged.

He was able to manifest an aura that eclipsed even Harmon’s unmatched recovery and endurance using sacred aura—an astonishing monster.

However, the time left for him was not long. The window for reaching that adjacent realm they had just experienced together would soon close.

Harmon interpreted the feelings of disappointment evident on the sword master’s face.

“This matter…”

Before Tris could say anything, Harmon bowed his head first.

“I believe we’ve been rather hasty. I too hold some blame, so let’s just bury this matter.”

Once he shed the excess energy, the pride that briefly ignited within him subsided.

‘That was reckless.’

Though he gained much, it was merely personal acclaim. As a representative of the Holy Kingdom, it was nothing but a hasty blade clash.

That also applied to the sword master.

Nonetheless, their outward attitudes could hardly be the same.

“May I take Jerome with me?”

“…Very well.”

“Ha.”

Both of them implicitly understood that, in that hastily commenced battle between representatives of their nations, Harmon had much more to gain.

Above all else, it wasn’t that Harmon didn’t hold back for face-saving reasons, nor did Jerome’s fate weigh heavily in his mind.

Thus concluded the first encounter between the strongest beings of the continent, marked by such a ruckus.

* * *

“…What did you think?”

Startled by the sudden question from his silent master as they exited the city gates, Jerome quickly responded, having already replayed the events in his mind.

“It was an incredible duel. I felt as though a blind person had gained sight.”

“…So that’s your take? Well then, do you think you could participate in such a duel?”

“…I don’t think so, not yet.”

Jerome’s candid answer prompted a heavy sigh from Tris.

He braced himself, fearing he had again said something wrong, as his master followed up with a lament.

“Ah. If only we had met ten years earlier…”

“…Master?”

With that, Tris held his silence until they were nearly at the Imperial encampment before finally speaking again.

“Remember this clearly: if war breaks out between the Holy Kingdom and the Empire, the Divine Sword must die first.”

It was a reasonable statement, as the stakes made the implications all too clear.

“By any means necessary.”

However, those words weighed heavier than Jerome could manage as he wore a grim expression.

“What do you mean by that, Master?”

“I mean it plainly. If war breaks out, you must do what it takes to kill the Divine Sword. If the Empire ever conquers the Holy Kingdom but doesn’t manage to eliminate him, then the Empire will invite calamity upon itself in the years that follow.”

“…”

“A catastrophe of unprecedented proportions, embodied in an aura master with saint-level divinity.”

Tris’s mention of a being that had never existed in human history was serious business.

* * *

– The Holy Kingdom is not responsible for the death of the legion commander and the disappearance of the prince.

The official stance of the Holy Kingdom was unchanged.

However, the Empire’s response to that claim had subtly shifted.

– Cardinal Tracy, a key figure of the Holy Kingdom, colluded with the Empire’s foes, the Black Serpents, to orchestrate the Prince’s abduction.

– The death of Commander Max Irelia was also connected. The Empire will hold the Black Serpents and the Holy Kingdom fully accountable.

“The Black Serpents? What in the world are they?” 

“They’re enemies of the Empire, apparently.”

Unknown to the general public, the tale of the mages who used symbols resembling the Black Serpents, emerging from the Cassel Tower, began to surface.

Moreover, the Empire publicly declared them as the masterminds behind the horrendous terror that had struck Aserian, possessing the nefarious ability to manipulate human minds and command grotesque monsters.

– The abduction of the prince aimed to use him to generate chaos within the Imperial Family. Regrettably, he is now designated as having been expelled from the Royal Family.

– They now demand an explanation from the Holy Kingdom for the turmoil it has instigated alongside its enemies.

Of course, the Holy Kingdom would not remain silent.

– Cardinal Tracy is nothing but a con artist who deceived the world. She is merely a Black Serpent mage, not a true priest.

– Furthermore, she plotted to manipulate the Pope to deliver the Holy Kingdom to the Empire. The prince’s abduction was merely a botched deal between them and the Empire, and we demand an explanation concerning this backroom maneuver.

The Holy Kingdom highlighted the earlier amicable movements toward the Empire under Pope Austin’s ascendancy as evidence.

But the Empire wasn’t budging either.

– The legion commander is dead, and the prince has gone missing. There could be no clearer evidence than this.

After exchanging statements aimed at establishing justifying narratives, the silent Emperor finally spoke.

– As one representing a human nation recognized by the Holy Kingdom, I shall punish and cleanse the tainted divine temple.

This declaration essentially amounted to a war proclamation.

Consequently, the Empire’s western legions began their march toward the sacred city of Nobiense, and the world’s attention understandably shifted toward the Holy City.

“The Emperor is finally revealing his ambitions, isn’t he?”

“Was that not anticipated?”

At Iliya’s voice, which carried a hint of concern as she gazed out the window, the middle-aged knight beside her responded calmly.

“They may be underestimating the need for time, but we are in the same boat here.”

It appeared that his confidence somewhat eased Iliya’s worry, and she swiftly regained her composure as she turned to Harmon.

“…What of the preparations?”

“The Holy Knights across various regions have begun donning disguises and are arriving in droves. The volunteers for the Holy Legion are also in abundance. Everything we’d initiated from that day is proving effective.”

Indeed, since the day the Second Prince had vanished alongside Tracy, they had been preparing for war.

“The Emperor will launch a war anyway… It was wise to heed Logan’s counsel once again.”

“…May the gods continue to bless him.”

At Iliya’s words, Harmon drew a circular sign of faith and clasped his hands together, prompting her to slightly bow her head eastward in response.

In that moment, both sensed a subtle vibration of the divine energy within them. Their gazes met, and they realized that it was no mere illusion—if the great deities were observing, then the steadfast faith they held rendered them devoid of fear.

At that moment, a voice rang from outside.

– The Pope approaches.

“The Pope?”

“No, it couldn’t be… just yesterday…”

In their bewilderment, they exchanged glances, but before they could utter more, the door swung open, revealing the frail yet pallid face of an elderly man.

He seemed even more haggard than before. Upon entering the room, he promptly coughed, stunning those who were watching and prompting them to rush toward him.

“Your Holiness!”

“You must not strain yourself!”

“Haha. It’s fine; cough, cough! …I can’t stay in peace when I’ve caused calamities for the faith.”

As Pope Austin spoke, his expression was one of profound remorse.

“You must rest until you fully recover. Just regaining consciousness is a miracle in itself.”

Iliya could genuinely see the truth in her words. It had been over three months since he had exhibited any emotions at all, like an automaton trapped in a spell that manipulated the mind of a human, and the ascetic priests accustomed to healing the mentally distraught had concluded that the Pope would never return to full health, even upon the dispelling of the unknown magic.

Yet, even under such squalid conditions, he clung tenaciously to his sense of self, earning him the respect he rightfully deserved.

“Indeed, Your Holiness. Please focus on recovering your health. You need to lead the Holy Kingdom again.”

Austin shook his head persistently in response.

“No, it should have been the Saint, not me, overseeing the faith. Had she assumed responsibility, these mishaps may have been avoided…”

“Your Holiness, such a statement…”

“Please withdraw such words.”

The extent of his proclamation rendered the two onlookers unnerved, prompting them to kneel simultaneously, overwhelmed by the sheer gravity of his remarks.

Then, with a bitter smile, Austin lowered himself in front of them, kneeling in a gesture that shook the very essence of their beliefs.

“Your Holiness!”

“You cannot do this!”

Neither the two nor the Holy Knights who had accompanied him could help but become startled as Austin let out a poignant sigh.

“…This is how it should be. As sinners, the heroes who have saved the Holy Kingdom should never kneel before me.”

He then removed the pure white regalia he was adorned with, offering it up before them.

The pope’s staff, regarded as one of the nine holy relics, was none other than Sententia.

But the moment Iliya’s face met that wondrous holy light, she tensed and recoiled.

“Is it possible…?”

“I, Pope Austin Flute, hereby relinquish this position and pass it on to the Saint of Amundah, Iliya Gabbón.”

“Your Holiness!”

The shocking announcement found listeners at a loss, and all whom it concerned doubted what they had just heard.

Yet, the individual who had made this declaration wore a smile of relief.

“No official ceremony is required, given the circumstances. This is the final command from Pope Austin Flute. Accept Sententia, Sister Iliya.”

“…Can I, am I truly able to?”

“The relic that sustains my fragile spirit lies within the saint’s grasp. Once you accept, your closeness to the divine will allow you to hear the divine words more clearly. Proclaiming the will of the deities to humanity is the true duty of a pope. I should have offered it long ago, yet I fell short…”

With those words imbued in remorse and regret, the brief transfer ritual transpired.

Although the recipient wore a solemn expression, those observing assumed it was a burden of immense responsibility after taking on such weighty duties.

In truth, however, Iliya felt an inexplicable uneasiness bubbling within her.

‘Why does holding this relic feel so off?’

It was a sentiment the saint could not dare to verbalize.

The divinely crafted apostolic staff radiated divine light, but rather than feeling blessed, Iliya could only sense it as a heavy load hanging over her.



-chapter 368-

“I will hold you accountable for the death of Commander of the Western 7th Corps and the disappearance of the Second Prince.”

The justification for the Empire’s troops, who had camped in front of Nobiense, was clear.

But.

Galen Decade shared Tris’s incredulity. If they were to flatly reject such a perfect justification, then the Empire would not be able to contest their invasion, should they proceed to attack.

In their analysis, the wisest course for the Holy Kingdom would have been to accept the troops and then prove their innocence during the investigation.

However, outright refusal at this juncture was tantamount to confessing guilt. This was a dead-end path, directly leading to war without leaving even a sliver of possibility for resolution.

And what if he spouted nonsense like—

‘For instance, saying the Emperor tried to kill him?’

That would indeed be the worst-case scenario imaginable.

‘We need to ascertain whether he was kidnapped during the execution of that plan or if it happened beforehand.’

If it were the latter, then even if the Second Prince was alive, it posed no threat.

Galen’s expression shifted to one of shock, but Tris held firm in his stance. The knowledge of the Emperor and his secret—a matter no one could discuss with others—was an undeniable burden he bore.

Accompanied by only a few of his knights, Tris moved toward the castle gate.

“Imperial Duke Tris Honsby, along with six escort knights, requests entry into the Holy City to investigate the unfortunate incident!”

His resonant voice rang out loudly.

As the representative of the Empire who had come with ten thousand troops, and backed by the name of “Sword Master of the Continent,” the Sword Saint, news of his arrival reached the castle towers.

“Is that… the Sword Master of the Continent?”

“What continent? Surely, it must be the Empire!”

“Well, isn’t that the same thing?”

“No! The title of the best belongs to Lord Harmon!”

“Silence! In any case, is that old man, or rather, that man truly the Sword Saint?”

With an unexpected figure stepping forward, a commotion arose even among the commanders, the foremost of the Holy Kingdom.

“Is he a lion or not? Did the Sword Saint come in person?”

“Is this madness? What are they thinking?”

And the one who could quell this uproar was just one individual.

“Open the gates.”

“Captain!”

“It was an anticipated occurrence. Only the individuals are different.”

With a dull yet confident response from the Sword Saint, the knights obeyed, instantly giving way.

Creeeeeeak.

As the eastern gate of Nobiense creaked open, the glimmering sight of knights clad in immaculate white armor could be seen lining up within. 

Even at a glance, the nearly thousand knights radiated an overwhelming presence.

Observing the scene, the Sword Saint felt a sense of admiration.

‘Indeed, this is the pride of the Holy Kingdom—the Sacred Knight Order.’

If all of the holy knights scattered across the world were gathered, their numbers would likely surpass ten thousand, making it the most formidable unified knight order under a single name. Moreover, they were hailed within the Holy Kingdom as the best knightly order in the world, reinforcing that realization.

‘Even the average knights appear quite skilled. Not only their presence but also their divine power will certainly prove to be a challenging opponent for typical knights.’

He was confident that in a straightforward confrontation with a similar-sized knight order, they could reasonably overrun them.

However, it would be foolish to simply admire those who would stand against him, so Tris composed his expression and stepped into the castle.

Then, while being welcomed by fervent gazes, he chuckled lightly.

“Is it customary to welcome guests so ferociously in the Holy City?”

With a light jest, the atmosphere became thick with cold sweat streaming down the faces of the surrounding knights.

It felt as if a giant were pressing down on their shoulders, and momentarily, their knees buckled, forcing them to straighten up and glance at each other, realizing their companions were equally rattled.

The hundred-strong frontline knights uniformly felt their hearts shoot up into their throats.

– Is there really such a monster?

As the front line teetered on the brink of collapse, a voice managed to break through.

“A guest is still a guest, is he not?”

An unassuming man with a gentle demeanor emerged from within the ranks of knights.

His presence caught Tris’s attention immediately.

Standing just over 180cm, he was smaller among the knights. Although his face was usually found in any crowd, he had effortlessly quelled the atmosphere around him.

There was no other individual like this in the Holy Kingdom.

“Are you Lord Harmon, known as the Sword Saint?”

His voice conveyed a mix of mild admiration and certainty.

At the unexpected show of friendliness, Harmon smiled gently and bowed his head.

“Indeed. It is an honor to meet the renowned Sword Saint of the Continent.”

“It is I who is honored. The Sword of the Divine, one thought to be merely a frog in a well. However…”

Tris, once again entranced, greeted him with genuine respect.

If merely sensing his aura was enough to convey such power, it left him in awe, contemplating how mighty this man who wielded divine power might actually be.

He began to wonder if perhaps this man could even surpass him in strength.

As he entertained such notions, Tris shook his head almost reflexively.

‘No way, that’s impossible.’

Aura users age rapidly once they surpass their limits, while he maintained his prime combat prowess even in his current form.

This existence itself was a testament to a mastery that far exceeded the limits of ordinary aura prowess, boasting unparalleled insight into the essence of life—force.

He took pride in the realms he had achieved.

‘He mentioned he is at the end of his forties?’

Although he had heard of the unique nature of divine aura from literature, he never thought himself inferior.

However, to be compared at such an age was astonishing in itself.

“…Your talents are indeed remarkable, Sir Harmon.”

As compliments rolled fluently from Tris’s mouth, Harmon could not maintain his tense demeanor any longer.

“I, too, am glad to meet you, Duke Tris. Though it is regrettable that our circumstances are not ideal.”

“Indeed. However, mere stalemates are meaningless. Might I arrange a meeting with my disciple?”

“…Of course.”

At those words, the knights formed a tight formation, creating a clear path.

While there may not be explicit power dynamics in politics, the Sacred Knight Commander held the authority over the martial strength of the Holy Kingdom, and given that Harmon was praised as the best among all commanders throughout history, his influence distinctly stood out.

Seeing this unfold, the tension in Tris’s eyes firmed once more.

* * *

“…What exactly happened?”

Upon seeing his disciple ensnared in bandages, the surprise on Tris’s face darkened into a cold glare after scanning the condition of his student.

“To think you sustained such severe injuries… what on earth happened?!”

Instead of providing solace, his reaction boiled with fury instead.

And Jerome, as if anticipating such a response, tightly shut his single eye in resignation.

“…It appears I cannot fool the gaze of my master.”

“You foolish boy! What did you do?!”

Bam.

“Whoa!”

Clang!

Startled knights around them drew their swords while Harmon simply raised a hand to halt them. The rising red aura merely formed a protective barrier surrounding the Sword Saint and his disciple.

‘This is a conversation that cannot be allowed to reach outside… no matter what, even if it is not merely a shield but an aura of this magnitude!’

They didn’t even require a power upgrade of the aura since there were only two possible scenarios explaining the exchange he witnessed: either an outrageously small resource consumed or a substantial surplus of force maintaining such an extravagant display.

‘…Or both?’

These were abilities requiring flawless mastery over one’s energy to execute such magical feats.

Since the beginning, the essence of the man had conveyed feelings of a true monster.

‘…Where do I compare against him?’

A surge of competitiveness ignited within Tris as he started to wonder just how his strength stood when compared to Jerome.

Taking a moment to gather himself, he diffused the overwhelming tension around him while regaining his footing as he compensated for Jerome’s defeat.

“In that instant, the secrets our God would never allow me to share out of my eagerness threaten to advance into conflict once more.”

“What is it that Barros knows?”

Jerome, too aware of the vacillation in the Sword Saint’s tone, let out a heavy breath.

“His Highness Barros, it seems, was aware.”

“How come?”

“Our saint had imparted a hint to him.”

“You foolish child! You must understand the severity—”

Tris, flowing with indignation, felt that he was spiraling into a futile rage over the meaningless exchanges.  

The indirect deception as previously intended had ultimately dwelled upon his disciple’s ability to remain hidden from an aching truth.

“Believe me, I merely meant to keep him off the other’s watch!”

While Jerome couldn’t fool the intentions Tris sat patiently to argue, one thing was certain—it wouldn’t make a difference whether the Emperor struck first or the rumors slipped into the confines of their ear.

As the consequences unreflected expand, already questioning Jerome’s answer successfully weighed heavy within each of his troubled thoughts.

Then inevitably came the heaviest sigh.

“…Perhaps the nature of his intentions was greater than my own.”

For Tris, no longer possessing the allowance of pettiness, felt the fleeting nature of their harsh reality.

“Think. What may have inspired this action?”

Biting his lip, Jerome wore a guarded expression.

“It must be… the choices I made weighed heavily, yet…the clash with your kin was initiated out of respect for the Holy Kingdom.”  

“The knights should endure, for the sovereign my experiences have entrusted. Trust that.”

Jerome paused only to find that even he commanded respect as a bearable pleasure.

Feeling the corners of his raised lips would betray him, Jerome struggled to understand this revelation while forcing the growing despair against his very own chest.

“Say I disbelieved—how would you gauge how many lives linger in our hands, my pride might be an illusion despite the healthy face?”

Harmon sought Solomon’s guiding light, urging Tris to speak in rationality rather than chaos.

“…Even if I knew despair awaited, I would have endured humiliation. Saving those precious lives… It is an acceptable cost.”

Tris remained adamant using sharpened words edged with reason collected from every corner of holy light.

“So it is fit upon us to yield… to share nothing but our despair between the two of us—”

On those words wrapped within tranquility, Harmon reverberated, “—No chance shall they pass beyond our walls of divine light.”

Calling upon all available forces wouldn’t be an overstatement.  

Yet, against 250,000 enemy troops and over 15,000 knights, not to mention five or more superhumans including the Sword Saint, it was overwhelming.

Two of the main figures he had met right after arriving in the Holy Kingdom recognized their identities outright.  

Having already gotten his head tangled from the strange words he heard from the Saint earlier, Viktor found himself glaring at his sister without meaning to.  

And she, in turn, understood her brother’s intent purely through a glance.  

“That’s not true!? The Saint and this person, ah, no, this gentleman is the strange one!?”  

Victoria flared up, and Harmon chuckled lightly while nodding.  

“It’s not that I saw through your magic. I simply remembered your force and aura. But it seems that McLain was involved back then, too. I truly appreciate the help you’ve provided.”  

Remembered his force and aura?  

Was that even possible?  

Eileen merely sighed as she gazed at the Holy Sword with a face that indicated she had given up on understanding it all.  

“So many can recognize us, it makes me very worried about whether we can truly perform our roles well.”  

Back in the United Kingdom of small nations, they could perfectly disguise themselves just with artifacts; here, even with the added concealment magic from Vargas, their identities were exposed.  

It was a situation that could only make one sigh in frustration.  

But the Holy Sword dismissed the party’s concerns.  

“You don’t need to worry about that. Among the Imperial forces, only the Sword Spirit would be able to recognize you. Moreover, even if someone figures it out, they would have no way of knowing who you truly are, right? I don’t suppose anyone here has personal ties with him?”  

At that remark, the party members shook their heads in unison. Logan was the only one who had met the Sword Spirit of the McLain.  

Upon seeing that, Harmon sighed softly and nodded before moving directly to the main topic.  

“Once again, I appreciate your coming to the Holy Kingdom. However, even with your assistance, the situation remains dire on our end. For that reason, I have a request.”  

At his following words, a look of shock appeared on the faces of Eileen and the party.  

* * *  

The Emperor’s attack restarted exactly two days after Eileen’s party arrived.  

In the meantime, the Holy Kingdom had started to guess what the Empire was aiming for amid their delays.  

The Grand Barrier, known as the strongest divine enchantment said to have been ordained by the gods, was indeed an essential part of taking down the capital.  

“The Empire seemed to push for it from the get-go.”  

The Holy Sword had not yet fully recovered from his injuries, and the overexerted Saint, trying to save him and recover the barrier, had also depleted her divine power.  

The fact that the two most significant forces of the Holy Kingdom could no longer participate was indeed a devastating blow, yet the expression on the leader of the Holy Kingdom remained calm, for they had plenty of alternatives now.  

Among them was Viktor, who had taken the alias Miller, smiling faintly as he took Ilya’s words.  

“The Holy Sword asked me to get the Saint out if things reached a worst-case scenario.”  

“Such a pious individual. However, if it comes to that, wouldn’t it be better for you, Captain Harmon, to survive for the future of the Holy Kingdom rather than me?”  

Is that truly how you feel?  

Casting a look at the calm face of the Saint, Viktor internally voiced his doubt.  

The sword of the kingdom and the spiritual anchor of the Holy Kingdom.  

If only one of them were to survive to rebuild the Holy Kingdom, it should logically be the spiritual anchor.  

Even when setting aside his personal feelings, Viktor believed it was correct.  

“…So please refrain from thoughts like last time, and look after yourself. Of course, we won’t let things fall easily with us here.”  

“Last time… you say?”  

“Yes. The last time I spoke with you…”  

Viktor trailed off and stared intently at the Saint’s face.  

The pretty face filled with curiosity that was looking at him felt strangely unfamiliar, entirely different from the shabby look he had seen days ago.  

“…You mentioned repeatedly that you were sorry for being a burden.”  

“Ah… I did, didn’t I? I always appreciate what you do for me, Sir Viktor.”  

Only now did she seem to remember, nodding her head.  

Yet, upon seeing this, Viktor’s expression soured drastically.  

‘Does she… not remember?!’  

It shouldn’t be something easily forgotten.  

At that moment, feeling a chill running down his spine, he noticed Ilya frozen with a strangely stiff expression.  

Viktor scrambled to think of how he could explain what was rapidly spiraling away when a sharp sensation emanating from nearby caught his attention.  

Swoosh.  

Crash!  

Out of nowhere, a black-masked figure appeared, his chest pierced and spewing blood.  

“Saint, step back!”  

“Ugh! Yes, yes!”  

Though it was unwelcome, the moment the battle reignited, the expectation that the Empire would target the disabled Saint and Holy Sword proved to be accurate.  

Whirrr.  

The gray aura blade tore through the air like lightning.  

While Harmon, the master of weapons, hadn’t reached the level of Logan McLain yet, he had begun to sense the presence of specters, even if just a little bit.  

Right now, he was almost relieved by their attack, as it meant that he wouldn’t have to wrack his brain for an explanation any longer.  

Yet, he felt disturbed.  

‘What on earth is happening right now to you?’  

In Viktor’s mind, worries about the Saint hiding behind him swiftly swelled.  

And as that occurred, outside, the two armies had begun to collide in earnest.  

However, the onset was quite different from what most people, especially the Empire, had anticipated.  

Swoosh!  

Bang!  

A powerful resonance rippled through the barrier held at the back of the Imperial formation where the massive magic circle was being maintained. The sudden onslaught was repelled by the shield.  

The force behind that attack was no ordinary level; Galen, the one guiding the flow of magic, naturally shifted his gaze toward the barrier. Though weak, the force was far beyond that of an ordinary aura blade.  

‘Is it an aura?!’  

It was an utterly incomprehensible fact.  

The magic circle was located at the far rear of the Imperial formation.  

Yet now, to have an aura-laden attack suddenly strike the barrier?  

Moreover, the perpetrator was nowhere to be seen, and even the escort unit remained unharmed.  

Only one amongst them, the 5th Legion Commander, Arhen Tussart, appeared to have an inkling of what had occurred as he glared at the empty air.  

“Could it be…?”  

Galen thought it was possible for a top-tier assassin to exist within the Holy Kingdom.  

Such an absurd notion flitted through his mind.  

And yet, he soon realized he had made a grave miscalculation.  

Bang!  

Another powerful impact struck the barrier. He was able to catch sight of its true source now.  

Yet the result was indeed absurd.  

A sleek arrow that had soared with astonishing speed from a distance, hitting the shield—a common object he had seen countless times on the battlefield.  

“An arrow?!”  

Could someone actually launch an arrow infused with aura!?!  

Unfathomable words left Galen dumbstruck, eyes wide with shock.  

“How many more could the royal family possess?”  

“…I’m unsure. Surely not many. The power expenditure for the aura wanes rapidly, and the costs are incredibly high.”  

Power. Cost.  

Those inhumane terms pressed heavily upon Jerome’s lips as he recognized that he’d been unsettled by their lives being exploited.  

“Ah, no.”  

“Don’t worry. And remember this one thing: it’s all for…”  

“For the Empire!”  

Pleased with his apprentice’s response, Tress smiled and raised his head to the clouds of dust.  

“To think they have developed weapons immune to mental magic along with my baseline swordsmanship. Tools designed to catch the serpent hindering the truth. Holy Sword, you truly were a remarkable being.”  

One who had to resort to other strategies after failing to defeat him with swordsmanship.  

Tress knew he would never forget the Holy Sword for the rest of his days.   

Yet as the dust slowly began to clear, a beam of sacred light soared upwards.  

“What is that?!”  

“Hm?”  

The light appeared divine, yet now he recognized his role as the enemy to the Sacred Kingdom.  

In that shocking moment, Tress felt his expression harden.  

“Charge immediately! Resume the battle!”  

“Commander, but the ground…”  

“Cavalry, flank the enemy; mages, fill the area! Capture the sacred capital!”  

Once again, Tress rose with a thunderous voice.  

As the Imperial forces followed his command to regroup, amidst the settling dust, a female figure began to emerge from the shining light.  

A beautiful woman adorned in pure white judicial robes with a holy wreath above her head floated gracefully above the crater left behind by the explosion.  

– It is not yet time for you to rest.  

Her voice reverberated eerily, echoing across the ground now illuminated by beams of light.  

Among them, a man still in a state of faint or dead came into view along the castle walls.  

‘Holy Sword!!!’  

Tress’s eyes widened in horror.  

“No! All forces charge! We must kill the Holy Sword!”  

His voice rang out thunderously, yet the knights and cavalry of the Imperial forces, flanking both sides, struggled as they swerved around Tress, losing sight of their target when the Holy Sword vanished atop the castle wall.  

‘Saint? Could such power come from the Saint? Dammit! Why didn’t we have such intelligence!? No, this isn’t the time for panic. We still hold a colossal advantage.’  

With tightly clenched lips, Tress pressed his men onward.  

“The Holy Sword can’t fight anymore! The enemy’s leader has collapsed! Charge now!”  

Though his commands were sound, they were not without hazards.  

Despite his reasoning, a sudden message rang in his mind.  

[Commander, the magic circle has reached its limit unexpectedly rapidly. The holy barrier is recovering at an alarming rate. Please observe the situation and act accordingly.]  

The frantic army of the Empire came to an abrupt halt.

Stripping away the goodwill shaped through interpersonal relationships revealed a sensation akin to interrogating allies who were here to assist.

Her fists clenched instinctively at that familiar voice.

“I must refuse.”  

“…Such a shame.”  

Before the last syllable of “shame” left his mouth, the Sword of Carnage, as if teleporting, appeared right next to her.  

The clean horizontal slash drew a clear red line across the center of her throat.  

However, the vibrant red hue merely brushed past Eileen’s head, which instinctively lowered in anticipation of the attack.  

Then, true to form, her posture propelled her upward into the Sword of Carnage’s chest. The counterattack, a retaliation of desperation, met only air as he simply repositioned, deflecting his sword into the ether.  

For a while, they continued an exchange of nearly brush-to-knife threats.  

Bam, bam, bam!  

The sounds of breezes being cut resonated in succession through the air as superhumans clashed.  

“Have you been hiding your prowess?”  

Amidst the cascade of red afterimages, the Sword of Carnage’s voice dripped with rage.  

“I simply changed my approach.”  

Eileen’s nonchalant reply caused Triss’s brows to twitch.  

Yet, despite her seemingly relaxed demeanor, Eileen too was sweating profusely.  

‘Every move is a narrow margin. Focus!’  

Against powers that could split dimensions, the Unyielding Bastion became as defenseless as a bare body—unless she reached the realm of equal footing with the Sword of Carnage.  

She knew that there was no way to block a lethal strike. So why clash swords at all?  

Focusing entirely on dodging, she would retaliate minimally.  

Giving up even on defense and concentrating solely on evasion allowed her to improve her agility remarkably.  

Still, she couldn’t let her guard down.  

The sight of the minuscule aura leaking from her opponent’s body hardly provided any comfort. Instead, it fueled her growing rage at her own inability to evade the attacks of a wounded opponent.  

Before long, it felt like her limits were nearing. At this point, avoiding direct hits was becoming ever more challenging given that her opponents weren’t even attempting to engage fully.  

Eileen clenched her teeth as she noticed the blade aimed for her neck zooming in like a predatory raven. Ignoring it entirely, she thrust her sword toward the Sword of Carnage’s chest, showcasing a strike that seemed to declare mutual destruction.  

That willful counterattack made the Sword of Carnage’s blade adjust abruptly, clashing for the first time since the fight began.  

Boom!  

“Ugh?!”  

Eileen was struck back with a powerful impact, soaring into the inner walls.  

Yet her expression remained composed and resolute. What she had anticipated was happening—she was neither crushed by the force of impact, nor had she lost a limb as she had feared, despite having rolled within the confines of the fortress.  

‘…Did he have his limits?’  

Though the Sword of Carnage had been unleashing top-tier powers effortlessly, it seemed there was some degree of restraint.  

While it was surprising, given the injuries from earlier, it was something Eileen could easily calculate.  

This had been a calculated approach, one reliant on only conditional attacks.  

Sudden situations or unexpected changes were deadweight; the moment he deviated from his ‘normal course,’ the aura gathered with difficulty dissipated.  

To that end, it was evident that during this confrontation, the Sword of Carnage’s complexion had indeed paled even further.  

Then, the long-awaited voices echoed in the air.  

“Lord… Aran!”  

“Aran!”  

“I’m sorry for being late!”  

With the arrival of three reliable allies, Eileen couldn’t help but smile despite her pale face.  

“Haha, not just an archer, but also another aura user and a mage? What on earth are you people?”  

The Sword of Carnage looked at them in disbelief, his incredulous laughter spread across the battlefield.  

As he spoke, his blade seemed to lower slightly, reflecting a sense that he was losing combat will.  

However, Eileen remained entirely composed.  

“Do not clash with his aura. Focus on improvising! We must capture the Sword of Carnage here!”  

If they could subdue him now, the war would become infinitely easier—not merely in this battle, but in future conflicts against the McLain as well.  

Her party’s thoughts perfectly aligned in that moment.  

But the Sword of Carnage was certainly not a trivial opponent.  

“Hehe, that is what I should be saying. Please don’t run away.”  

Even in the presence of four superhumans, the fierce glint in the Sword of Carnage’s eyes grew only sharper.  

‘Is he fooling around?’  

It was apparent to anyone that he was in substandard condition. Faced with an aura incongruent with the title of the continent’s best sword, any bravado felt more like a desperate bluff.  

Then, with a sudden glimmer in his eyes, the Sword of Carnage straightened his sword before declaring,  

“Looks like I’ll have to reduce my lifespan a bit. The price shall be…”  

Flare!  

A crimson haze flickered dangerously around him, followed by a ferocious flame-like aura bursting forth.  

“Your lives!”  

“Focus!”  

Upon hearing Victoria’s startled cry, a powerful force pressed upon him. At that moment, a rain of arrows sent forth by Burdel fell like a barrage.  

Eileen charged straight toward the Sword of Carnage alongside Ronian.  

Boom!  

The moment their feet hit the ground, part of the wall erupted.  

Victoria’s gravitational magic plateaued at that very moment, yet even that did not deter the Sword of Carnage from appearing mere inches away, swinging his blade down toward Victoria’s neck.  

Instinctively, she tapped into her magic, causing a massive golem to emerge behind her, which effortlessly intercepted the onset of his slash.  

“Ugh!”  

As the golem shattered under the impact, Victoria staggered backward, her breathing ragged as she steeled herself against the blow.  

‘A golem?’  

The Sword of Carnage appeared startled for an instant.  

This was not mere stone craftsmanship but a tangible manifestation of magic. Even when cleaved, it had ended up resisting injury from his strike.  

And as the arrows changed course mid-flight, Eileen and Ronian pressed his back, following the unexpected turn of events.  

Boom!  

The flames coursing from the Sword of Carnage’s body lessened in a heartbeat, while two superhumans were propelled forcefully outside the walls.  

“This monster…!”  

Burdel poured arrows like madness, and while Victoria, bleeding by the mouth, set up spells to subdue him, the Sword of Carnage continued moving forward, relentlessly hunting after Victoria again.  

In those fleeting moments, the glimmers of magic echoed with malicious intent as he caught sight of a young girl with distinctive blue hair and glaring red and blue eyes.  

His focus sharpened—not only was her distinct appearance striking, but she appeared far younger than he had anticipated. His blade hesitated for a fraction’s time—just enough to spare Victoria’s life.  

“Stop!”  

“Hold on!”  

Just before he acted, Viktor charged forth, unleashing wave after wave of pulsating aura.  

The brief moment of distraction the Sword of Carnage faced allowed Viktor to reopen the battlefield.

“Sir Lof, I look forward to working with you.” 

After two days stationed on the southern wall, Ronian bowed his head at the unfamiliar voice he heard for the first time.

A slender knight riding a radiant white horse, wielding a spear that flickered with a peculiar blue light.

‘Commander of the Western 3rd Legion, Malton Heights.’

With the presence of this superhuman, who had almost captured the southern wall just ten days prior, Ronian began to mentally prepare himself.

‘He is said to have a specialty in relentless, lightning-fast attacks.’

Astor Heizen, known for his robust defense and extraordinary recovery capabilities, was mentioned as someone who faced advantage over equivalent opponents, yet claimed to struggle against the master of swift assaults.

But Ronian felt confident. And that confidence stemmed from a clear reason.

Even now, merely recognizing the enemy’s presence felt like his brother’s voice echoed in his mind.

– Malton Heights is not specialized in speed. That remarkable velocity is merely a reflection of his martial arts proficiency, but that martial art…

The superhumans of McLain, particularly Ronian and Viktor, had nearly memorized information regarding the commanders of the empire by force.

While most of that analysis focused on the eastern commanders, they had also acknowledged the specialties and characteristics of their western counterparts just in case.

Countless times, they were toyed with by the likes of the eastern 3rd Legion commander, Blake Evendoor, in these simulated duels.

‘Especially that damnable afterimage.’

After enduring such relentless torment, Ronian involuntarily learned how to handle those faster than himself.

– This should be sufficient preparation against speed. Now, let’s utilize your strengths.

What Ronian felt most assured about was the difference in information.

‘Does he even know I exist?’

Among the superhumans of the 3rd Legion, only Malton Heights stood firm. Just his presence alone sufficed to erase any previous disadvantage Astor had shown.

Moreover, if he could take down Malton Heights, they could manage the numerical disadvantage against the 3rd Legion comfortably.

First, there were the human bombs he had heard about from the Divine Sword. Fortunately, though, he had also learned how to deal with them.

This was a conclusion derived from a crisis that nearly cost the Divine Sword his life, so it was undoubtedly valid.

The problem lay in the second variable.

‘Sister-in-law…’

Only his sister-in-law and Burdel remained on the eastern wall where the Divine Sword and the 1st Legion commander were stationed. While the Divine Sword had not yet fully recovered from his serious wounds, there was no way Ronian wouldn’t worry.

Burdel’s ranged sniping ability was indeed remarkable, yet he had a strikingly extreme flaw; he couldn’t guarantee superiority even against two top-tier knights in close combat.

Additionally, the elite troops of the 5th Legion were supposedly escorting the legion commander and the most formidable of mages created by the raging winds. In the worst-case scenario, his sister-in-law might have to confront the Divine Sword, the 1st Legion commander, and the 5th Legion commander all by herself.

It was true that, given her attributes, she would not collapse easily under pressure, yet he couldn’t help but worry.

‘As soon as I finish dealing with Malton Heights, I’ll head east.’

He and Victoria were stationed in the south and west, aiding the vice captains to quickly take out the enemy commanders and then assist the eastern wall.

That was currently their fundamental strategy.

“Aaaaah!”
