Unfettered, the imperial forces leaped up over the wall.

Amidst the chaos and cacophony of madness, Ronian furiously cleaved through the imperial knights, searching for Malton Heights.

And soon, he confronted the blue lightning that lashed out at Astor Vice Captain.

Boom! 

In the midst of the superhumans battling fiercely, only the sounds of weapons clashing and explosions filled the air; no other noise could break through.

Even the common battle cries were swallowed in that space filled with sheer intensity.

Like Astor, who had been unusually quiet for the past few days, perhaps the enemy thrived in this kind of style as well.

As Ronian mused thoughtlessly, he stepped into the realm of the superhumans, their unique world.

Thud.

Dodging a helmet hurled toward him by the force of a collision, he advanced closely, immediately recognizing the attributes of the two fighters.

Astor held his white-shimmering shield to deflect the torrential blue bolts raining down upon him. Behind the kite shield that covered most of his bulk, heavy eyes remained alert, evaluating potential gaps.

Nonetheless, the mace in Astor’s other hand rarely found a target; it was entirely consumed by the frantic onslaught of the polearm fighter, who moved with unrelenting speed, practically teleporting across the battlefield.

The movements appeared almost as though he had four bodies and eight arms, a sumptuous display of combat that vividly demonstrated why he was called “the spear that emitted flashes.”

Unquestionably magnificent as well was Astor, managing to defend against all those strikes.

If the enemy had four bodies.

Boom, boom, boom!

Bang!

“Who the hell are you!?”

That arrow should not have appeared here.

Shwraaaang!

-chapter 386-

Title: The Vision of Baros Spread Across the World

Of course, there were those who doubted the authenticity of the simultaneous announcements from the Mage Towers. However, even they could not help but nod at one undeniable fact.

– At the very least, it seems true that the Empire has been preparing for war in advance.

When the 5th Legion was mobilized to conquer the Sacred Kingdom, it hadn’t felt particularly strange. 

Yet after the Emperor decided to send additional troops, the swift mobilization of the central army, completed in just a few days, felt unusually quick.

The fact that an army of over two hundred thousand could prepare for deployment in only three days, and that there was nearly no movement of additional supplies heading towards Aserian, meant one thing. 

– The Imperial family had stockpiled the resources necessary to move such an immense army.

For the neighboring countries around the Empire, this fact outweighed the justification and outcome of the war occurring in the Sacred Kingdom.

Naturally, from the moment the news spread, most neighboring countries began redeploying their armies to their borders with the Empire. Additionally, countless envoys from various royal families made their way to neighboring nations.

– An alliance. The only option to confront the Empire is through an alliance.

The minor nations began preparations to survive according to their own means.

And among all these changes, the most responsive to the stirrings was undoubtedly the Empire, the master of Aserian.

* * *

Bang!

“The Great War has been distorted even before it began!”

The thunderous voice filled with malice dominated the great hall.

It was a rare shout from the Emperor, resonating with an air of authority.

“What in the world has led to this situation? Explain, Luctus.”

This was not just a name called out, but an explicit insult, lacking even formal respect.

Luctus Gusfeld, a chancellor who had long served the Emperor, understood the chilling intent behind the cold words.

‘Perhaps today could be my last.’

The stern-faced old man, sensing the hand of death approach, raised his head with an unflinching expression.

“First, I shall report the analysis results from the staff regarding the current situation.”

Although no answer emerged from the throne, Luctus nodded towards the back.

At that moment, one of the twenty ministers who had also been kneeling in a similar position hurriedly sprang to Luctus’s side.

“Staff Deputy, Larry……”

“Make it brief.”

“……Yes. Allow me to present the findings regarding the current situation.”

Larry, a young man, nervously licked his dry lips in response to Luctus’s resolute voice.

“The agents of the Special Inspection Department, commonly referred to as ‘ghosts,’ are trained primarily to deal with detection and recording magic due to the nature of their assignments. 

However, all agents shown in the footage remain entirely unaware of the magical surveillance. 

Had they sensed even a trace of being recorded, the ghosts would have prioritized eliminating the evidence above all else. The fact that they did not implies one key truth.”

He looked straight back into the pitch-black eyes. Despite the suffocating pressure causing cold sweat to trickle down his back, Larry Gusfeld’s voice did not waver.

“Either an artifact of a level exceeding the 5th Class was used, or a spellcaster of the mage class covertly recorded the footage without revealing their identity.”

If the artifact was above 5th Class, only legendary or mythical beings could craft such items. 

Thus, the answer could only be the latter option.

“In other words, the Prince Baros……”

The moment the word “Prince” passed his lips, the owner of the cold gaze narrowed their eyes.

Larry swallowed hard.

“No, I mean, the traitor Baros must have been aware of the truth prior and conspired with a hostile sorcerer to guarantee his own safety while recording the footage. 

And likely, that sorcerer was……”

“The Black Serpent, I presume.”

The voice from the chilling throne acknowledged the young man’s insight for the first time.

“Yes, Your Majesty. And the owner of the hidden silver aura in the footage…”

“Jerome?”

“Yes, indeed. They prepared both the agents to block our forces and the equipment to record this event beforehand. 

The traitor Baros has likely been plotting against the Empire since then.”

“And?”

“……Yes?”

“Has the work of the staff been merely to reiterate what I am already aware of?”

Facing the ominous voice and fierce gaze, Larry faltered and glanced sideways.

Cold sweat poured down his forehead, and his eyes could not control themselves from trembling as the Chancellor, Luctus, remained steadfast and focused on the throne.

He showed no intention of helping his grandson.

Rather, that stern demeanor jolted young Larry Gusfeld into clarity. 

It was not the time to rely on others; his life hung in the balance.

“Absolutely not, Your Majesty! An unexpected obstacle has arisen. However, our staff has devised a plan that may turn this very situation to our advantage.”

“……Speak.”

“However, for that to succeed… I need Your Majesty to make a bold decision first.”

Before the Emperor could react, Luctus turned to him with a piercing gaze.

“Larry. How dare you…!”

Even without hearing the rest, Larry understood.

– To demand something from his Majesty!

Fortunately, before Luctus’s reprimand could echo throughout the hall, the Emperor raised his hand.

“Continue.”

“……Thank you for your kindness, Your Majesty.”

“Your plan.”

Although jolted by the steady authority, Larry steadied his breath and continued speaking.

“First, we must publicly announce our withdrawal from the conquest of the Sacred Kingdom.”

“Larry!”

To suggest abandoning the Imperial family’s wish, held for centuries, was a dangerous statement. 

The Chancellor Luctus shouted out again, but the Emperor quietly asked back.

“What would be the reason for such action?”

“Even if we were to forcefully seize the Sacred Kingdom, we would not achieve the Empire’s ultimate goal.”

“Ultimate goal….”

“Yes. The Imperial family’s ambition of becoming the spiritual pillar of the continent cannot be fulfilled under the current circumstances. 

If we disregard justification and claim the Sacred Kingdom, the subjects of the continent will not accept it, and we will only repeat the grave mistake made four hundred years ago.”

Four hundred years prior, the dissolution of a corrupt church during the Cadre Resolution.

Most believed that event arose through self-reflective efforts from the priests, but in truth, the Imperial family had manipulated the situation behind the scenes. 

At that time, the Emperor, claiming to act as a representative of the Nine Deities, summoned the scattered true priests while feigning submission. 

But they, who had bended their knees, established Novience following the nine saints who appeared in their era, forming a powerful church within the Empire.

The authority consolidated by the Emperor over a century crumbled at once with the rise of the god-sent saints. 

To make matters worse, foreign powers established themselves within the Empire’s territory.

The Emperor at the time burned with rage but could not express it, given the public sentiment formed in favor of the church based on the miracles demonstrated by the nine saints. 

The Emperor’s previous claim to divinity only aided the reformation of the church.

In the end, that wrath turned towards the deities themselves.

– The timing and the locations of the saints were too well-timed. Investigate how far the deities were meddling in humanity’s affairs.

Since then, the royal family had secretly investigated the mechanisms behind the births of saints and priesthood, as well as the methods of producing paladins and knights.

A trove of ancient information, once thought absurd, became crucial to unlocking the mysteries of deities and temples. 

As a result, the royal family could provide rough conclusions concerning mechanisms related to the deities, saints, and knights.

– A justification worthy of divine acknowledgment. That was paramount.

What was ironic was that this justification did not necessarily have to be the truth.

A justification recognized by the Nine Deities did not have to align perfectly with reality. As long as the populace’s opinions acknowledged it, the church’s authority could be maintained.

This contradictory nature appeared incompatible with the ideal principles espoused by the Nine Deities.

Once they realized this contradiction, the royal family could not escape from their mistrust of the gods and divinity.

Given that the Emperor had learned the divine and temple mechanisms behind the emergence of saints and deities, he began viewing the Nine Deities not as revered figures, but as threatening competitors.

In consequence, the endeavor to seize control of the temple formed part of a grander scheme. 

‘Of course, that was a sentiment I couldn’t publicly declare.’

The Emperor’s lips curled into a slight smile as he regarded Larry once more.

“Indeed. Under the current circumstances, it will be difficult. 

Yet I established this office not merely to hear about challenges we face; it exists for the staff to devise means to achieve our goals even in extreme situations. 

I am not asking to hear that we should abandon our efforts.”

The air turned chilling around Larry’s throat. 

Yet, owing to his determination that he would present his opinion as the representative of the staff, he stood firm as he addressed the Emperor.

“Your Majesty, relinquish the Sacred Kingdom and instead seize the entire world.”

“Ha.”

That silence, breathless, resonated through the hall. The Emperor’s response was unanticipated, sounding like a mix between amazement and resignation.

“Accept defeat merely to gain the world? You may jest.” 

“Not at all, Your Majesty. You can publicly declare your grievance for the sake of peace in this continent. Speeched as an act of genuine pain for a cause. 

Until the truth comes to light, profess that you are giving up for the sake of peace.”

“…….”

“Then negotiate with the Sacred Kingdom to secure respect and declarations of support in return for ceasing conquests.”

“And?”

“Once the Sacred Kingdom has declared their support, we can simply pursue the Black Serpent to ‘quickly reveal the truth.’ 

They, who propagate malignant rumors about the Empire and instigate regional fears, will have fortuitously ‘coincidentally’ sought refuge among neighboring kingdoms.”

Ah!

A subdued exclamation escaped from the officials kneeling around them, but Larry remained unflinching. 

The Emperor simply chuckled and inquired further.

“Are you, too, implying that I regard the leaders surrounding our borders and their nobility as fools?”

“Individuals may act foolishly, but groups cannot. Yet, because a group cannot represent the interests of all its members, it sometimes makes foolish decisions.”

“……Wise words of Arius.”

“Indeed. Whether the truth holds up or not, if we present a justification, it will divide opinions among the masses.”

“Go on.”

“Among the neighboring countries, there is no nation that does not trade with the Empire. 

And substantial profit comes as a result of this trade, benefiting the ruling nobility directly. 

Thus, we can manipulate their interests to instigate conflict among them. 

Encourage them to cooperate with the Empire.”

“Oh?”

“If they agree to cooperate, the Empire’s military could openly enter that kingdom. Even if it fails, we will still possess justification: The military’s intentions were clearly to assist against enemies endeavoring to aid the Kingdom.”

Upon hearing this logic, the Emperor’s simmering expression broke into a smile for the first time.

“Excellent. You are not worth your mettle for nothing.”

The simple acknowledgment of his effort sent waves of relief through the sweating Larry as the Chancellor clenched his fists steadily. 

The Empire’s ultimate goals were the same as the current plan’s success.

The conquest of the continent and the unification of the Sacred Kingdom—two apparent targets reflected one grand ambition: 

To establish the Empire’s Emperor as the tangible and spiritual ruler of the realm.

“Should either of the targets be met, the other is merely a matter of time.”

Though plans had twisted slightly, the order of operations mattered little.

With fervent ambition simmering deep in his chest, the Emperor raised his voice.

“I shall accept the counsel of the staff. After negotiating with the temple, put the plan into action. 

We will initiate the grand scheme once the winds of war shift in our favor!”

“Yes!”

“Yes, Your Majesty!”

The bindings of death loosened for those who had narrowly escaped oblivion. The boisterous cries of over twenty civil ministers enveloped the great hall.

Outside the window, warm sunlight poured in, an unusual sight for winter.  

Yet, the face of the beauty gazing out from within the palace was as cold as the weather was warm.

She would persuade the prince to betray the king.  

Wasn’t that a usual plot in the novels circulating in the markets?  

Just as Luisa was lost in pleasant yet futile fantasies, a voice she didn’t wish to hear came from outside the door.  

– Count Ronian has come to visit.  

“Ugh, the timing really…”  

It was a theatrical performance meant to cover up the imperial interference in the ambush incident and portray a friendly relationship.  

She found this stage bothersome, yet the other lead was particularly reluctant.  

Creak.  

“Are you free?”  

As soon as the attendant served tea and stepped out, Luisa shot a cold remark with an expressionless face.  

There was no longer any need for pretenses between them.  

However, the large young man with red hair and red eyes simply smiled and responded.  

“Well, this is my work right now.”  

“You surely don’t seem to enjoy it.”  

“Well, at least it’s nice to have an attractive company.”  

At around twenty years of age, he was full of youthful vigor.  

Surprisingly, even with a planned beauty practically undressing before him, the young man’s eyes held no glimmer of lust.  

‘Such restraint with his powers at that age; he must have considerable self-control.’  

That thought only made Luisa recall her own past that was shrouded in secrecy, causing a wry smile to escape her lips.  

Well, ultimately, since that was exposed, Baron Ronian’s disinterest might seem more pronounced.  

“How brazen. It seems you brothers are quite similar.”  

“Haha, that’s a first for me to hear. You think I resemble my elder brother?”  

Indeed, while the intense features of red-haired Ronian were prominent, the shapes of their faces were entirely different.  

Logan, who took after their mother, had gentle features, while Ronian sharply resembled their father, often leading those around them to expect discord between the brothers.  

Except for the fact that he once enjoyed hearing that he looked like his brother.  

Ronian, smiling naturally, put down his teacup and said cheekily.  

“Well, who’s more brazen? The princess or the terrorist who claims to be a victim? What could be more brazen than that?”  

“Victim? Who ever was truly victimized? It seems I solely spat blood.”  

“Our knight suffered serious injuries too. Or do normal knights no longer count as humans to you?”  

“As long as he’s alive, that’s all that matters.”  

The laughter exchanged bore thorns hidden within their smiles.  

Since that incident, her conversations had continued to be tiresome, yet the attendants outside would assume that everything was congenial.  

“I heard that you received gifts from the Dong-wang palace. At this rate, we really might set a wedding date soon.”  

“Don’t worry; that won’t happen.”  

“If you continue to stay here, it might become a reality you should fear.”  

“I’ll be leaving soon anyway. So just forget about it.”  

Sipping cautiously, as her nerves heightened, she couldn’t even taste the tea that flowed down her throat.  

After about an hour, she would have to endure more tiresome resistance, but there was no way around it.  

As Luisa gathered her thoughts, a rather enticing piece of information slipped out from Ronian unexpectedly.  

“Oh, it seems my brother is planning something big again recently.”  

“Something big? Hm.”  

Feigning indifference, her attention was entirely now singularly focused on him.  

Whether he knew how intrigued she became, Ronian wore a slightly amused smile, gazing steadily at her.  

“However, there was a message that the Empire may be interested, so I hope it’s solved amicably with the Dong-wang palace.”  

“Uh? Why are you telling me this?”  

“We’re not on bad terms, are we? Outwardly, at least.”  

“That’s merely surface-level.”  

“It’s for the purpose of combating the Empire. I think ‘they’ might like it.”  

Oddly emphasized words irked her ears, but curiosity quickly overtook them.  

“Go on. What is it about?”  

“There are plans to build fortresses at several key locations along the border.”  

“Pfft.”  

Her tea spluttered out, as her jaw almost dropped from surprise.  

She blamed Ronian’s evasive smile for suddenly dodging it.  

“What did you just say?”  

“Considering your response, it seems your ears are functioning well.”  

“Are you seriously going to build fortresses on the border? Are you blatantly declaring war against the Empire? And then asking us to soothe things over?”  

“Officially, we won’t announce it as just the ‘West’ but rather the entire frontier. Of course, we plan on constructing it solely in the West.”  

“Do you think the Empire is blind!?”  

“What do you want? They won’t interfere with internal affairs anyway. They might issue a warning, at worst. Or they might even march in sooner.”  

– The mere act of the Empire preparing for war will send ripples through the world. With decades spent in peace policies, they won’t be able to hide changes forever.  

– If the war is inevitable, why not choose the timing ourselves?  

Recalling her brother’s words, Ronian was smiling, “Heh… In the end, you’re all doomed.”  

Luisa sighed, neither knowing if it was a laugh or a scoff.  

Soon after, their gazes remained sharp, a fierce determination sparkling.  

‘Makryn knows of war against the Empire as an established fact.’  

‘They do not deny it. They are aware of the Empire’s preparations for war.’  

Just with one query, both sides found confirmation; one side understood the kingdom’s situation, while the other confirmed their guess was true.  

After a moment of silence, Luisa broke the ice first.  

“Officially, we won’t announce it, but a subtle pressure will emerge. What are the consequences?”  

“Perhaps the princess’s safe return?”  

“Hmph. Even if you threaten me with my life, you won’t sway my decisions.”  

“It’s not a threat; it’s merely a suggestion. ‘They’ will likely want it.”  

Upon Luisa’s brief silence, Ronian reclined against the couch, eyeing her carefully.  

But despite the carefree disposition of his posture, there was a noticeable tension.  

“Then my father may respond without making any official proclamations, but subtle pressures are inevitable.”  

The very thought brought further unease to her mind.  

“You may find yourself faced with some unusual requests.”  

“Seems plausible. But we might just take proper preventive measures.”  

“Yes, we understand. As long as information is reported, from now on, any small changes should be conveyed without delay.”  

“Yes, understood.”  

Staring deeply into Luisa’s sapphire eyes, Ronian suddenly leaned forward.  

“Actually, I’ve no intention of entirely cutting ties. Additional contacts can indeed be established.”  

With that said, Luisa couldn’t help but express her surprise.  

“But if you say there’s value in maintaining contact, I’d rather report to the Empire than to my brother.”  

“What will you do?”  

Biting her lip slightly, the depth of Ronian’s indigo gaze seemed to require careful consideration.  

“How can I approach giving up my connections with intention?”  

With sudden strength, Luisa declared, refusing to feel subject to sudden commercial laws.  

Forcing a smile to Ronian’s unfurling laughter, she managed to regain her composure.  

“Hmph. What’s worse than being tied down?”  

“Good luck with that. I’ll convey your words along with our own requests, regardless of anything.”  

“Alright. It’s not as if I can change matters overnight, but no need to panic just yet.”  

“Let’s get things settled straightforwardly.”  

When they finally stood up and embraced, she left the space with her own determined stance.  

Staring after her retreating figure, Ronian chuckled.  

Once the door swung shut behind her, he sighed deeply.  

“Haah… The princess is indifferent.”  

Staring blankly out the window, Ronian pondered aloud, though no one offered a reply.  

With that, the chapter closed, leaving unanswered questions lingering like shadows from the past.



-chapter 329-

Outside the window, warm sunlight poured in, an unusual sight for winter.  

Yet, the face of the beauty gazing out from within the palace was as cold as the weather was warm.  

– Thanks to the Second Prince’s blunder, we have a good opportunity.  

– The Makryn confusion operation will be put on hold.  

– Before returning, implant more people in the Makryn royal palace.  

– If war breaks out between the Empire and Makryn, it will only cause further chaos. And…  

– I will accelerate the post-deity era.  

“My life being targeted is just a blunder…?”  

Luisa’s expression hardened again as she recalled her communication with her mentor.  

She knew the tower’s purpose and resonated fully with it.  

But how could she accept the idea that it would be her own sacrifice to achieve that purpose?  

Even so, she had no choice but to endure it for now.  

What could she possibly say in a situation where her partial mission failure had turned into nothing?  

“Baros. One day, I will make you pay.”  

She could only grit her teeth and make that vow.  

Moreover, the orders that accompanied those words were equally absurd.  

The instruction to plant people from the Kassel Magic Tower meant creating brainwashed individuals.  

‘Someone whose mind can deteriorate suddenly without attracting attention, yet occupies an important position.’  

“Is there even such a person?”  

The conditions seemed so unreasonable that a self-derisive comment escaped her lips. After all, wasn’t there a king in a country capable of breaking the tower’s magic just by coming near?  

“It would be easier to seduce a genuine prince.”  

Thinking of the rumors circulating in society, she let out a small laugh.  

The tales about Count Ronian and herself had become intertwined, adorned with all sorts of embarrassing stories.  

Though she had never seriously considered marriage, as a woman, it was hard not to be somewhat concerned.  

Furthermore, when she pondered on these daunting orders, it naturally led her to daydreams of escape, allowing those awkward stories to resurface more frequently.  

“…Should I actually try seducing him?”  

She would persuade the prince to betray the king.  

Wasn’t that a usual plot in the novels circulating in the markets?
